Union as Mixture: The Impossibility of Divine Contact with Creation
Baqillani refutes the doctrine of union as mixture (mumazaja).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Christian doctrine of union as mixture (mumazaja) leads to absurd consequences about God's attributes and the eternity of matter.

Core Idea
If the eternal Word can mix with a body, then God could be touched, move, and change—impossible for the Divine.

Baqillani next addresses Christians who say the union is a genuine mixture of the Word with Christ's body. He argues that if the eternal can mix with the temporal, then there is no reason to deny physical contact, spatial location, or even change in God. This would undermine God's transcendence and lead to the absurd conclusion that other bodies could also be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice Baqillani's conditional argument: 'If it is permissible... then why not?'
Focus on the logical consequences he draws.
2
Identify the main argument
Baqillani argues that if the Word can mix with a body, then it can touch it, be adjacent, move, etc.
3
Consider the reductio on eternity
He then argues: if something eternal can later become mixing, then other bodies that are always mixing could also be eternal.
This is a powerful argument from analogy.
4
Reflect on divine transcendence
Reflect on how this refutation upholds the Islamic doctrine of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدهما وتخليط من قائله؛ وذلك أن الظاهر في الشمع شيء مثل نقش الخاتم، وهو غيره، لأن الحروف الموجودة بالشمع هي بعض له وجزء من أجزائه؛ وما في الطابع من الحروف هو بعض الطابع ومن جملته وهما غيران يصح وجود مع عدم الآخر، فظنهم أن نفس النقش الذي في الشمع هو نفس الطابع جهل وتخليط فيجب على هذا إن لم تكن الكلمة نفسها هي الظاهرة في جسد المسيح أن يكون الظاهر فيه غيرها وهو شيء مثلها، وأن يكون الله سبحانه ابنان وكلمتان، أحدهما لا يحل الأجسام ولا يتخذها هيكلاً ومكاناً، والآخر حال في جسد المسيح، وهذا قول بأربعة أقانيم وترك القول بالتثليث. وأما من قال إن الاتحاد إنما هو حلول الكلمة في المتحد به واختلاطها به وممازجتها له، فإنه يقال له: إذا جاز على الكلمة الحلول في الجسد المخلوق وممازجتها له واختلاطها به، وهي مع ذلك قديمة، فما أنكرتم من اجتماعها مع الجسد ومماستها له؟ وإذا جاز على القديم سبحانه المماسة والمجاورة والمخالطة للمحدث والممازجة له فلم لا يجوز عليه مقابلة المحدث ومحاذاته؟ ولم لا يجوز عليه الظهور والكمون والحركة والبعد والقرب والشغل، والتفريغ والتصوير والتركيب؟ فإن راموا في ذلك فصلاً لم يجدوه وإن مروا على ذلك قيل لهم: فإذا جاز أن يكون ما هذه صفته قديماً وقد كان في القدم غير مماس ولا ممازج ولا مخالط، فما أنكرتم أن يكون سائر الأجسام المماسة المختلطة المتحركة الساكنة قديمة؟ وما الذي جعل الكلمة التي هذه صفتها بالقدم أولى منها بالحدث؟ وما الذي جعل الأجسام بالحدث أولى من الكلمة؟ ويقال لليعقوبية: إذا جاز أن ينقلب ما ليس بلحم ولا دم لنفسه وما هو مخالف للدم واللحم لنفسه، لحماً ودماً بالاتحاد، فلم لا يجوز أن تنقلب الكلمة، التي تخالف المحدثات لنفسها وليست بمحدثة لنفسها محدثة بالاتحاد، فيصير القديم لنفسه بالاتحاد محدثاً عند اتحاده كما صار لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده، ولم لا يصير المحدث لنفسه قبل اتحاد القديم به قديماً عند اتحاد القديم به المتحد به فتصير الطبيعتان واحدة ويصير ما ليس بلحم ودم لحماً ودماً وما هو لحم ودم غير لحم ولا دم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك سبيلاً. فيخرج عن أن يكون لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده في وأما قول من قال إن الاتحاد هو حلول الكلمة في الناسوت من غير مماسة، وأنه كحلول الباري سبحانه في السماء وكحلوله على العرش من غير مماسة لهما، فإنه باطل غير معقول؛ وذلك أن الباري سبحانه ليس في السماء ولا هو مستو على عرشه بمعنى حلوله على العرش؛ لأنه لو كان حالاً في أحدهما ومستوياً على الآخر، بمعنى الحلول لوجب أن يكون مماساً لهما لا محالة. وأما قولهم إن العقل جوهر حال في النفس مماس لها فإنه باطل لأن الجوهر لا يحل في العرض وإنما يحل في الجسم على معنى المماسة له والاعتماد عليه واتخاذه مكاناً يعتمده ويحيط به من جهاته
One of them is confusion and nonsense from its speaker; that is because what appears in the wax is something like the engraving of the seal, and it is other than it, because the letters present in the wax are part of it and a portion of its parts; and what is in the stamp of letters is part of the stamp and from its entirety, and they are two different things, the existence of each is valid without the other. So their assumption that the very engraving that is in the wax is the same as the stamp is ignorance and confusion. Therefore, if the Word itself is not what appears in the body of Christ, then what appears in it must be other than it and something like it, and that God, exalted, would have two sons and two words: one of them does not indwell bodies nor take them as a temple and place, and the other is indwelling in the body of Christ. This is a statement of four hypostases and abandonment of the doctrine of trinity. As for one who says that the union is only the indwelling of the Word in that with which it is united, its mixing with it and its blending with it, it is said to him: If it is permissible for the Word to indwell in the created body, to blend with it and to mix with it, while it is eternal, then why do you deny its joining with the body and its touching it? And if it is permissible for the Eternal, exalted, to touch, be adjacent, mix with the originated, and blend with it, then why is it not permissible for Him to be opposite the originated and alongside it? And why is it not permissible for Him to have appearance, concealment, movement, distance, proximity, occupation, emptying, formation, and composition? If they seek a distinction in that, they will not find it, and if they pass over that, it is said to them: If it is permissible for that which has this description to be eternal, while in pre-eternity it was not touching, not blending, not mixing, then why do you deny that all other bodies that are touching, mixing, moving, and still could be eternal? And what makes the Word, which has this description, more deserving of eternity than of origination? And what makes bodies more deserving of origination than the Word? And it is said to the Jacobites: If it is permissible for that which is not flesh and blood in itself and which is contrary to flesh and blood in itself to be transformed into flesh and blood through union, then why is it not permissible for the Word, which is contrary to originated things in itself and is not originated in itself, to become originated through union, so that the Eternal in itself becomes originated through union at the time of its union, just as it became flesh and blood at the time of its union? And why does the originated in itself before the union of the Eternal with it not become eternal at the union of the Eternal with it, with which it is united, so that the two natures become one, and that which is not flesh and blood becomes flesh and blood, and that which is flesh and blood becomes not flesh and blood? They will find no way to repel that. It thus departs from being flesh and blood at its union in. As for the statement of one who says that the union is the indwelling of the Word in the humanity without touching, and that it is like the indwelling of the Creator, exalted, in heaven and like His being established on the Throne without touching them, it is false and unintelligible; that is because the Creator, exalted, is not in heaven, nor is He established on His Throne in the sense of His indwelling on the Throne; for if He were indwelling in one of them and established on the other, in the sense of indwelling, it would necessarily entail that He touches them without exception. And as for their statement that the intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul and touching it, it is false because a substance does not indwell in an accident; rather, it indwells in a body in the sense of touching it, depending on it, and taking it as a place on which it depends and which surrounds it from its directions.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a series of refutations of Christian doctrines concerning the incarnation and union (ittihad) of the divine Word with the body of Christ. Baqillani begins by criticizing the analogy of a seal impression on wax. He argues that the letters in wax are part of the wax, not the seal itself; similarly, if the Word (al-kalima) is not identical to what appears in Christ, then there would be two sons and two words, leading to four hypostases instead of the Trinity. Next, he addresses those who claim that union is a mixture (mumazaja) or solution (hulul) of the Word in the body. If the eternal Word can mix with a created body, then why deny physical contact? This would imply that God can be touched, move, etc., which are impossible for the Eternal. He then argues that if something eternal can later become touching and mixing, then other bodies that are always touching could also be eternal, which is absurd. He then turns to the Jacobite doctrine of transformation: if a non-flesh substance can become flesh through union, then the Word could become originated, leading to the absurdity that the eternal becomes temporal. Finally, he refutes the analogy of God's 'indwelling' in heaven or on the Throne without contact. Baqillani asserts that God is not literally in heaven or on the Throne in a spatial sense; if He were, He would have to touch them. He also refutes the idea that the intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul with contact, because a substance cannot indwell in an accident; it indwells only in bodies with contact and dependence.

Key Terms
الحلول
الممازجة
الاختلاط
المماسة
القديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani claim necessarily follows from the idea that the eternal Word can mix with a body?
A) The Word becomes created.
B) The Word can touch the body.
C) The body becomes eternal.
D) The Word ceases to be divine.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument shows that the doctrine of union as mixture leads to attributing physical limitations to God, contradicting His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'God is with me,' do you unconsciously imagine a spatial presence? How does this lesson challenge that mental image, and what can you replace it with to maintain both closeness and transcendence?
?
If you believe in a God who is beyond all physical attributes, how does your daily worship and conversation reflect that belief? Are there phrases you use that contradict this truth?
?
Baqillani's argument shows that mixing God with creation leads to absurdity. Have you ever thought of God as being 'in your heart' in a literal sense? How can you cultivate a sense of divine presence without reducing God to something that mixes or indwells?

The Jacobite Transformation Refuted: Eternity Cannot Become Temporal
Baqillani refutes the Jacobite doctrine of transformation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Jacobite Christian doctrine that in the union, the non-flesh and blood substance of the Word is transformed into flesh and blood, leading to absurd consequences about the nature of God.

Core Idea
If the Word can become flesh through union, then it could also become originated, destroying its eternity.

Baqillani now addresses the Jacobite (monophysite) Christian view that the union involves a transformation of the divine Word into flesh and blood. He argues that if a non-flesh substance can become flesh, then the Word, which is eternal, could also become originated (muhdath) through union. This would imply that the eternal becomes temporal, which is absurd. The same logic would also allow the originated to become eternal, leading to confusion of natures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the parallelism in Baqillani's argument.
He uses the same structure: 'if it is permissible... then why not...'
2
Identify the two sides of the analogy
Baqillani argues that if transformation is possible in one direction (non-flesh to flesh), then it is possible in the opposite direction (eternal to originated).
3
Recognize the conclusion
The result is that the two natures would become one, which is contradictory to Christian doctrine.
4
Reflect on the defense of divine immutability
Reflect on how Baqillani's argument upholds the Islamic belief that God does not change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الكلمة التي هذه صفتها بالقدم أولى منها بالحدث؟ وما الذي جعل الأجسام بالحدث أولى من الكلمة؟ ويقال لليعقوبية: إذا جاز أن ينقلب ما ليس بلحم ولا دم لنفسه وما هو مخالف للدم واللحم لنفسه، لحماً ودماً بالاتحاد، فلم لا يجوز أن تنقلب الكلمة، التي تخالف المحدثات لنفسها وليست بمحدثة لنفسها محدثة بالاتحاد، فيصير القديم لنفسه بالاتحاد محدثاً عند اتحاده كما صار لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده، ولم لا يصير المحدث لنفسه قبل اتحاد القديم به قديماً عند اتحاد القديم به المتحد به فتصير الطبيعتان واحدة ويصير ما ليس بلحم ودم لحماً ودماً وما هو لحم ودم غير لحم ولا دم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك سبيلاً. فيخرج عن أن يكون لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده في وأما قول من قال إن الاتحاد هو حلول الكلمة في الناسوت من غير مماسة، وأنه كحلول الباري سبحانه في السماء وكحلوله على العرش من غير مماسة لهما، فإنه باطل غير معقول؛ وذلك أن الباري سبحانه ليس في السماء ولا هو مستو على عرشه بمعنى حلوله على العرش؛ لأنه لو كان حالاً في أحدهما ومستوياً على الآخر، بمعنى الحلول لوجب أن يكون مماساً لهما لا محالة. وأما قولهم إن العقل جوهر حال في النفس One of them is confusion and nonsense from its speaker; that is because what appears in the wax is something like the engraving of the seal, and it is other than it, because the letters present in the wax are part of it and a portion of its parts; and what is in the stamp of letters is part of the stamp and from its entirety, and they are two different things, the existence of each is valid without the other. So their assumption that the very engraving that is in the wax is the same as the stamp is ignorance and confusion. As for one who says that the union is only the indwelling of the Word in that with which it is united, its mixing with it and its blending with it, it is said to him: If it is permissible for the Word to indwell in the created body, to blend with it and to mix with it, while it is eternal, then why do you deny its joining with the body and its touching it? And why is it not permissible for Him to have appearance, concealment, movement, distance, proximity, occupation, emptying, formation, and composition? And what makes the Word, which has this description, more deserving of eternity than of origination? And what makes bodies more deserving of origination than the Word? Commentary
This passage is a series of refutations of Christian doctrines concerning the incarnation and union (ittihad) of the divine Word with the body of Christ. Baqillani begins by criticizing the analogy of a seal impression on wax. He argues that the letters in wax are part of the wax, not the seal itself; similarly, if the Word (al-kalima) is not identical to what appears in Christ, then there would be two sons and two words, leading to four hypostases instead of the Trinity. Next, he addresses those who claim that union is a mixture (mumazaja) or solution (hulul) of the Word in the body. If the eternal Word can mix with a created body, then why deny physical contact? This would imply that God can be touched, move, etc., which are impossible for the Eternal. He then argues that if something eternal can later become touching and mixing, then other bodies that are always touching could also be eternal, which is absurd. He then turns to the Jacobite doctrine of transformation: if a non-flesh substance can become flesh through union, then the Word could become originated, leading to the absurdity that the eternal becomes temporal. Finally, he refutes the analogy of God's 'indwelling' in heaven or on the Throne without contact. Baqillani asserts that God is not literally in heaven or on the Throne in a spatial sense; if He were, He would have to touch them. He also refutes the idea that the intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul with contact, because a substance cannot indwell in an accident; it indwells only in bodies with contact and dependence.

Key Terms
اليعقوبية
الطبيعة
القديم
المحدث
الاتحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The transformation in the incarnation is a one-way change from non-flesh to flesh without affecting the divine nature.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if transformation is possible, it must be reversible, leading to the eternal becoming temporal and vice versa.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would follow from the Jacobite claim that non-flesh becomes flesh through union?
A) The Word remains eternal.
B) The Word could become originated.
C) The flesh becomes divine.
D) The union is only apparent.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's refutation demonstrates that the Jacobite doctrine of transformation undermines the fundamental distinction between the eternal Creator and temporal creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself expecting God to change His eternal nature to fit your comfort or desires? Think of a specific prayer or hope you held that assumed God would act contrary to His unchangeable attributes. How can you today repent of that assumption and align your heart with His true nature?
?
The Jacobites tried to bring the eternal into the temporal without losing the eternal, but Baqillani shows that mixing the two leads to absurdity. In what areas of your life are you trying to merge worldly, temporal values with your devotion to the Eternal? What concrete step can you take this week to purify your worship from that mixture?
?
Baqillani's argument forces a clear distinction: God is Eternal, we are temporal. Do you truly live as if that distinction matters? When was the last time your life's decisions were genuinely shaped by the reality that God is entirely other and not subject to change? If you're honest, what would need to change in your daily routine to make that distinction practical?

Indwelling Without Contact: A False Analogy
Baqillani refutes the analogy of indwelling without contact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani rejects the Christian analogy that the union is like God's 'indwelling' in heaven or on the Throne without physical contact, and why it is impossible for a substance to indwell an accident like the soul.

Core Idea
If God indwells without contact, then He would be spatially located, which is impossible; furthermore, a substance cannot indwell an accident.

In the final refutation, Baqillani addresses Christians who say the union is like God's presence in heaven or on the Throne—without any physical contact. He argues that if God were literally indwelling in a place, He would have to touch it, which is impossible. He also refutes an analogy from philosophy: the claim that the intellect indwells in the soul with contact. Baqillani explains that a substance cannot indwell in an accident; it can only indwell in a body with contact and dependence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note Baqillani's rejection of the 'indwelling without touch' idea.
2
Understand the first refutation
Baqillani argues that if God is in heaven or on the Throne in a literal sense, then He must touch them, which is impossible.
This relates to divine transcendence beyond space.
3
Understand the second refutation
He refutes the analogy of intellect in soul, showing that a substance cannot indwell an accident.
This is a philosophical argument about categories.
4
Reflect on the implications
Reflect on how Baqillani upholds the absolute transcendence of God and the proper understanding of creation.

أحدهما وتخليط من قائله؛ وذلك أن الظاهر في الشمع شيء مثل نقش الخاتم، وهو غيره، لأن الحروف الموجودة بالشمع هي بعض له وجزء من أجزائه؛ وما في الطابع من الحروف هو بعض الطابع ومن جملته وهما غيران يصح وجود مع عدم الآخر، فظنهم أن نفس النقش الذي في الشمع هو نفس الطابع جهل وتخليط فيجب على هذا إن لم تكن الكلمة نفسها هي الظاهرة في جسد المسيح أن يكون الظاهر فيه غيرها وهو شيء مثلها، وأن يكون الله سبحانه ابنان وكلمتان، أحدهما لا يحل الأجسام ولا يتخذها هيكلاً ومكاناً، والآخر حال في جسد المسيح، وهذا قول بأربعة أقانيم وترك القول بالتثليث. وأما من قال إن الاتحاد إنما هو حلول الكلمة في المتحد به واختلاطها به وممازجتها له، فإنه يقال له: إذا جاز على الكلمة الحلول في الجسد المخلوق وممازجتها له واختلاطها به، وهي مع ذلك قديمة، فما أنكرتم من اجتماعها مع الجسد ومماستها له؟ وإذا جاز على القديم سبحانه المماسة والمجاورة والمخالطة للمحدث والممازجة له فلم لا يجوز عليه مقابلة المحدث ومحاذاته؟ ولم لا يجوز عليه الظهور والكمون والحركة والبعد والقرب والشغل، والتفريغ والتصوير والتركيب؟ فإن راموا في ذلك فصلاً لم يجدوه وإن مروا على ذلك قيل لهم: فإذا جاز أن يكون ما هذه صفته قديماً وقد كان في القدم غير مماس ولا ممازج ولا مخالط، فما أنكرتم أن يكون سائر الأجسام المماسة المختلطة المتحركة الساكنة قديمة؟ وما الذي جعل الكلمة التي هذه صفتها بالقدم أولى منها بالحدث؟ وما الذي جعل الأجسام بالحدث أولى من الكلمة؟ ويقال لليعقوبية: إذا جاز أن ينقلب ما ليس بلحم ولا دم لنفسه وما هو مخالف للدم واللحم لنفسه، لحماً ودماً بالاتحاد، فلم لا يجوز أن تنقلب الكلمة، التي تخالف المحدثات لنفسها وليست بمحدثة لنفسها محدثة بالاتحاد، فيصير القديم لنفسه بالاتحاد محدثاً عند اتحاده كما صار لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده، ولم لا يصير المحدث لنفسه قبل اتحاد القديم به قديماً عند اتحاد القديم به المتحد به فتصير الطبيعتان واحدة ويصير ما ليس بلحم ودم لحماً ودماً وما هو لحم ودم غير لحم ولا دم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك سبيلاً. فيخرج عن أن يكون لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده في وأما قول من قال إن الاتحاد هو حلول الكلمة في الناسوت من غير مماسة، وأنه كحلول الباري سبحانه في السماء وكحلوله على العرش من غير مماسة لهما، فإنه باطل غير معقول؛ وذلك أن الباري سبحانه ليس في السماء ولا هو مستو على عرشه بمعنى حلوله على العرش؛ لأنه لو كان حالاً في أحدهما ومستوياً على الآخر، بمعنى الحلول لوجب أن يكون مماساً لهما لا محالة. وأما قولهم إن العقل جوهر حال في النفس مماس لها فإنه باطل لأن الجوهر لا يحل في العرض وإنما يحل في الجسم على معنى المماسة له والاعتماد عليه واتخاذه مكاناً يعتمده ويحيط به من جهاته
One of them is confusion and nonsense from its speaker; that is because what appears in the wax is something like the engraving of the seal, and it is other than it, because the letters present in the wax are part of it and a portion of its parts; and what is in the stamp of letters is part of the stamp and from its entirety, and they are two different things, the existence of each is valid without the other. So their assumption that the very engraving that is in the wax is the same as the stamp is ignorance and confusion. Therefore, if the Word itself is not what appears in the body of Christ, then what appears in it must be other than it and something like it, and that God, exalted, would have two sons and two words: one of them does not indwell bodies nor take them as a temple and place, and the other is indwelling in the body of Christ. This is a statement of four hypostases and abandonment of the doctrine of trinity. As for one who says that the union is only the indwelling of the Word in that with which it is united, its mixing with it and its blending with it, it is said to him: If it is permissible for the Word to indwell in the created body, to blend with it and to mix with it, while it is eternal, then why do you deny its joining with the body and its touching it? And if it is permissible for the Eternal, exalted, to touch, be adjacent, mix with the originated, and blend with it, then why is it not permissible for Him to be opposite the originated and alongside it? And why is it not permissible for Him to have appearance, concealment, movement, distance, proximity, occupation, emptying, formation, and composition? If they seek a distinction in that, they will not find it, and if they pass over that, it is said to them: If it is permissible for that which has this description to be eternal, while in pre-eternity it was not touching, not blending, not mixing, then why do you deny that all other bodies that are touching, mixing, moving, and still could be eternal? And what makes the Word, which has this description, more deserving of eternity than of origination? And what makes bodies more deserving of origination than the Word? And it is said to the Jacobites: If it is permissible for that which is not flesh and blood in itself and which is contrary to flesh and blood in itself to be transformed into flesh and blood through union, then why is it not permissible for the Word, which is contrary to originated things in itself and is not originated in itself, to become originated through union, so that the Eternal in itself becomes originated through union at the time of its union, just as it became flesh and blood at the time of its union? And why does the originated in itself before the union of the Eternal with it not become eternal at the union of the Eternal with it, with which it is united, so that the two natures become one, and that which is not flesh and blood becomes flesh and blood, and that which is flesh and blood becomes not flesh and blood? They will find no way to repel that. It thus departs from being flesh and blood at its union in. As for the statement of one who says that the union is the indwelling of the Word in the humanity without touching, and that it is like the indwelling of the Creator, exalted, in heaven and like His being established on the Throne without touching them, it is false and unintelligible; that is because the Creator, exalted, is not in heaven, nor is He established on His Throne in the sense of His indwelling on the Throne; for if He were indwelling in one of them and established on the other, in the sense of indwelling, it would necessarily entail that He touches them without exception. And as for their statement that the intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul and touching it, it is false because a substance does not indwell in an accident; rather, it indwells in a body in the sense of touching it, depending on it, and taking it as a place on which it depends and which surrounds it from its directions.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a series of refutations of Christian doctrines concerning the incarnation and union (ittihad) of the divine Word with the body of Christ. Baqillani begins by criticizing the analogy of a seal impression on wax. He argues that the letters in wax are part of the wax, not the seal itself; similarly, if the Word (al-kalima) is not identical to what appears in Christ, then there would be two sons and two words, leading to four hypostases instead of the Trinity. Next, he addresses those who claim that union is a mixture (mumazaja) or solution (hulul) of the Word in the body. If the eternal Word can mix with a created body, then why deny physical contact? This would imply that God can be touched, move, etc., which are impossible for the Eternal. He then argues that if something eternal can later become touching and mixing, then other bodies that are always touching could also be eternal, which is absurd. He then turns to the Jacobite doctrine of transformation: if a non-flesh substance can become flesh through union, then the Word could become originated, leading to the absurdity that the eternal becomes temporal. Finally, he refutes the analogy of God's 'indwelling' in heaven or on the Throne without contact. Baqillani asserts that God is not literally in heaven or on the Throne in a spatial sense; if He were, He would have to touch them. He also refutes the idea that the intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul with contact, because a substance cannot indwell in an accident; it indwells only in bodies with contact and dependence.

Key Terms
الحلول
المماسة
العرش
الجوهر
العرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The union of the Word with humanity can be compared to God's presence in heaven without contact.
Correction: Baqillani shows that such indwelling would entail contact, which is impossible for God, and also that the analogy of intellect in soul is invalid because a substance cannot indwell an accident.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the analogy of the intellect indwelling in the soul?
A) Because the soul is eternal.
B) Because a substance cannot indwell in an accident.
C) Because the intellect is not a substance.
D) Because the soul is a body.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's refutation shows that any attempt to explain the incarnation through analogies of divine presence or philosophical concepts ultimately fails to preserve divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that God does not indwell anything spatially, not even heaven or the Throne. Have you ever, in your thoughts or prayers, pictured God as being 'up there' in a literal sense? How might that image subtly undermine your understanding of His transcendence? Will you consciously replace that image with a recognition that He is beyond all space and direction?
?
Baqillani says a substance cannot indwell an accident; it only indwells a body with contact. Your own intellect is not truly 'in' your soul as a separate thing—it is tied to your body. When you think of your 'self', do you imagine a non-physical soul floating inside your body? How does the lesson's warning against false analogies apply to your own self-concept? What would it mean to think of yourself as a unified whole, body and soul, without the illusion of separation?
?
The opponents used weak analogies to defend the incarnation, and Baqillani tore them apart. But what about you? Are there comfortable beliefs or practices you hold about God that, if scrutinized with the same rigor, would be found to rely on false analogies? Name one right now—and commit to examining it against the clear teachings of tawḥīd.

Refuting the Jacobite Doctrine of Union: The Logical Inconsistency of Incarnation
Baqillani refutes the Jacobite interpretation of incarnation via logical parity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes the Jacobite doctrine of union (ittihad) by exposing its logical consequences.

Core Idea
If the eternal can become flesh, then the eternal can become contingent.

Imam al-Baqillani engages with the Jacobite Christian claim that the divine Word united with flesh to become Christ. He does not merely reject it dogmatically; he shows that the doctrine, when examined logically, leads to self-contradiction. In this passage, he demonstrates that if union allows contrary properties to be exchanged, then nothing prevents the eternal from becoming temporal and the temporal from becoming eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the logical flow sink in.
Notice the rhetorical opening.
2
Identify the rhetorical question
Baqillani begins by challenging an assumption: 'Who made bodies more worthy of contingency than the Word?' Ask yourself what this question implies.
3
Follow the conditional argument
Trace the 'if...then' reasoning. If union can change what is not flesh into flesh, then why can't the same logic apply to the Word, making it contingent?
This is a parity argument.
4
Recognize the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that the Jacobites have no way to repel these implications. The doctrine leads to absurdities like the eternal becoming temporal.
This demonstrates self-refutation.
5
Reflect on the method
See how kalam uses logical consistency to refute opposing views. The argument does not rely on scripture but on rational necessity.
This is a hallmark of classical Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي جعل الأجسام بالحدوث أولى من الكلمة؟ ويقال لليعقوبية: إذا جاز أن ينقلب ما ليس بلحم ولا دم لنفسه وما هو مخالف للدم واللحم لنفسه، لحماً ودماً بالاتحاد، فلم لا يجوز أن تنقلب الكلمة، التي تخالف المحدثات لنفسها وليست بمحدثة لنفسها محدثة بالاتحاد، فيصير القديم لنفسه بالاتحاد محدثاً عند اتحاده كما صار لحماً ودماً عند اتحاده، ولم لا يصير المحدث لنفسه قبل اتحاد القديم به قديماً عند اتحاد القديم به فتصير الطبيعتان واحدة ويصير ما ليس بلحم ودم لحماً ودماً وما هو لحم ودم غير لحم ولا دم؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك سبيلاً.
Who made bodies more worthy of contingency than the Word? And it is said to the Jacobites: If it is permissible that what is neither flesh nor blood in itself, and what is contrary to blood and flesh in itself, becomes flesh and blood through union, then why is it not permissible that the Word, which is contrary to contingent things in itself and is not contingent in itself, becomes contingent through union, so that the eternal in itself becomes temporal through union at its union just as it became flesh and blood at its union? And why does the contingent in itself before the union of the eternal with it not become eternal at the union of the eternal with it, so that the two natures become one, and what is not flesh and blood becomes flesh and blood, and what is flesh and blood becomes not flesh and blood? They find no way to repel that.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative refutation refuting the Jacobite Christian doctrine of union (ittihad) in the incarnation. Baqillani begins with a rhetorical question: 'Who made bodies more worthy of contingency than the Word?' This challenges the underlying assumption that bodies change while the Word does not. Then he addresses the Jacobites directly: if they allow that what is not flesh and blood can become flesh and blood through union, then logically the opposite should also be possible. The Word, which is unlike contingent things, could become contingent through union, and the eternal could become temporal. Similarly, the temporal could become eternal. If two natures become one, then the properties of each nature would be exchangeable, leading to contradictions like flesh becoming non-flesh. He concludes that the Jacobites have no way to refute these implications; their doctrine is self-defeating.

Key Terms
اتحاد
كلمة
قديم
محدث
لحم
دم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this argument only attacks one specific Christian group.
Correction: It actually demonstrates a logical inconsistency in any claim of hypostatic union, regardless of sect.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue must also happen if the eternal Word becomes flesh through union?
A) The flesh must become eternal.
B) The Word must become contingent.
C) The union must be by contact.
D) The Word must remain unchanged.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the doctrine of union leads to logical absurdities, proving its invalidity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a belief that seems logically inconsistent, do you examine it or ignore it? How can you apply Baqillani's method of pressing the analogy to its logical conclusion in your own faith today?
?
Are there areas in your life where you accept contradictions because they are comfortable or familiar? What is one such area you need to re-examine, and what step will you take this week to address it?
?
If the Jacobites could not see the flaw in their own reasoning, what blind spots might you have in your own understanding of God? Will you seek out someone to challenge your assumptions?

Refutation of Indwelling Without Contact
Baqillani rejects the view that union is indwelling without contact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani rejects the idea that union is an indwelling without contact, and why any indwelling necessarily implies contact.

Core Idea
Indwelling without contact is logically impossible.

Baqillani addresses a Christian theological claim that the union of the divine Word with Christ's humanity is an indwelling without physical contact, using an analogy to God's relation to heaven and the Throne. He argues that such a concept is not only false but unintelligible, because indwelling by definition entails contact. This lesson unpacks his logical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Baqillani's own reasoning come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: claim → refutation → argument.
2
Identify the claim being refuted
The passage begins by stating a view: union is indwelling without contact. Baqillani declares it false. Find the exact wording of the claim.
The claim includes an analogy to God in heaven and on the Throne.
3
Understand Baqillani's reasoning
Baqillani argues that if indwelling were real, it would require contact. Since God is not literally in heaven or on the Throne, the analogy fails. Trace the logical steps.
Baqillani does not deny istiwa'; he only denies a literal spatial interpretation.
4
Apply the logic to the analogy
Consider why the analogy is broken: the proponents claimed indwelling without contact, but Baqillani shows that indwelling itself implies contact. Reflect on the implications for divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول من قال إن الاتحاد هو حلول الكلمة في الناسوت من غير مماسة، وأنه كحلول الباري سبحانه في السماء وكحلوله على العرش من غير مماسة لهما، فإنه باطل غير معقول؛ وذلك أن الباري سبحانه ليس في السماء ولا هو مستو على عرشه بمعنى حلوله على العرش؛ لأنه لو كان حالاً في أحدهما ومستوياً على الآخر، بمعنى الحلول، لوجب أن يكون مماساً لهما لا محالة.
As for the saying of the one who said that union is the indwelling of the Word in the human nature without contact, and that it is like the indwelling of the Exalted Creator in heaven and like His establishing on the Throne without contact with them, it is false and unintelligible. That is because the Exalted Creator is not in heaven, nor does He settle on His Throne in the sense of His indwelling on the Throne; because if He were indwelling in one of them and settled on the other, in the sense of indwelling, then it would necessarily be that He would be in contact with them without exception.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative refutation of the claim that the union in Christ is an 'indwelling' (hulul) of the divine Word in the human nature without physical contact (mumassa). The proponents analogize it to God's 'being in heaven' or 'sitting on the Throne'. Baqillani declares this view false and unintelligible. His reasoning: God is not literally in heaven nor literally sitting on the Throne in a spatial sense. If one insists on interpreting those expressions as genuine indwelling, then God would have to be in contact with heaven or the Throne, which is impossible for the transcendent Creator. Therefore, the analogy fails. The key point is that any concept of indwelling necessarily implies contact, which cannot apply to the divine Word, which is not a body.

Key Terms
حلول
مماسة
ناسوت
باري
عرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Baqillani denies God's attribute of istiwa' (establishing on the Throne).
Correction: Baqillani only denies that istiwa' implies spatial contact; he affirms the attribute in its proper, non-physical sense.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the analogy of indwelling without contact?
A) Because God cannot dwell in anything.
B) Because indwelling necessarily implies contact.
C) Because the Word is a body.
D) Because the Throne is not a place.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the concept of indwelling without contact is logically incoherent because indwelling necessarily implies contact, which cannot be attributed to the transcendent Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever unconsciously pictured God as being physically close to you, like a friend at your side? How does Baqillani's uncompromising logic challenge that image? What will you do today to worship a God who is beyond all contact, yet closer than anything?
?
The argument shows that claiming 'indwelling without contact' is self-contradictory. What similar logical contradictions might you unknowingly hold about God's attributes? Are you willing to examine your beliefs with the same rigor Baqillani applies?
?
If God is truly beyond spatial indwelling, does your prayer reflect a deep awareness of His transcendence? What specific posture or inner focus would align with the majesty of a God who cannot be contained? Commit to one concrete change in your next prayer.

Refutation of Intellect as a Substance in the Soul
Baqillani refutes the idea that intellect is a substance indwelling the soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the claim that intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul, and why this argument is used to deny spatial or bodily categories for the divine Word.

Core Idea
Indwelling (hulul) requires bodily contact, so neither intellect nor God's Word can indwell an accident.

Baqillani continues his theological argument by tackling a specific claim: that the intellect is a substance that dwells in the soul. This idea, sometimes used to analogize the relationship between God and His Word, is systematically refuted. Baqillani clarifies what 'indwelling' truly means in physical terms, and then applies this reasoning to show that the divine Word cannot be subject to such categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the claim being refuted and the core logical steps Baqillani uses.
Note the structure: claim → refutation → definition of indwelling → analogy → application to the Word.
2
Understand 'hulul' (indwelling)
Baqillani defines indwelling as contact, dependence, and surrounding. See how this definition restricts indwelling to bodies.
He gives examples: water in a well, oil in a bottle.
3
Analyze the analogy
Why does Baqillani choose water in a well and oil in a bottle? These examples illustrate that indwelling involves a container and something contained, both physical.
This strengthens the point that indwelling is a bodily property.
4
Apply to the divine Word
The Word of God (kalam Allah) is not a body. Since indwelling requires bodily attributes, it is impossible for the Word to dwell in anything.
Thus the Christological analogy fails.
5
Reflect on the broader theological context
Consider why Baqillani refutes this claim—it's not about psychology but about defending God's transcendence from spatial and corporeal categories.
This is part of a larger argument against anthropomorphic conceptions of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولهم إن العقل جوهر حال في النفس مماس لها فإنه باطل لأن الجوهر لا يحل في العرض وإنما يحل في الجسم على معنى المماسة له والاعتماد عليه واتخاذه مكاناً يعتمده ويحيط به من جهاته كحلول الماء في الجب والدهن في القارورة. وإذا لم يُعقل الحلول إلا مماسة وملاصقة وكانت المجاورة والاجتماع من صفات الأجسام وكانت كلمة الله غير جسم لم يجز عليها الاتحاد والحلول في الأماكن.
As for their saying that the intellect is a substance indwelling in the soul and in contact with it, it is false, because a substance does not indwell an accident; rather it indwells a body in the sense of contact with it, dependence on it, and taking it as a place that it depends on and surrounds from its directions, like the indwelling of water in a well and oil in a bottle. And if indwelling is not intelligible except as contact and adjacency, and adjacency and togetherness are attributes of bodies, and the Word of God is not a body, then union and indwelling in places are not permissible for it.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative refutation of a specific claim: that the intellect ('aql) is a substance (jawhar) that dwells in the soul (nafs) and is in contact with it. Baqillani calls this false. His reasoning: a substance cannot indwell an accident (the soul is considered an accident according to the author's ontology). A substance can only indwell a body, meaning it is in contact with and dependent on that body, like water in a well or oil in a bottle. Since indwelling necessarily involves contact and adjacency, and those are properties of bodies, and the divine Word is not a body, it follows that both union (ittihad) and indwelling in places are impossible for the Word. This argument extends the previous point: the Word cannot be subject to spatial or bodily categories.

Key Terms
عقل
جوهر
نفس
عرض
جسم
حلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is about psychology or the nature of human intellect.
Correction: It is actually a theological refutation of a Christological analogy that tried to compare the intellect-soul relationship to the divine Word's relationship with God.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why cannot a substance indwell the soul?
A) Because the soul is not a place.
B) Because the soul is an accident.
C) Because the soul is a body.
D) Because the soul is immaterial.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's refutation shows that the concept of 'indwelling' (hulul) is inherently physical and cannot be applied to the divine Word, thereby safeguarding God's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God's closeness to you, do you unconsciously think of it as a physical presence? How does Baqillani's refutation challenge you to purify your mental image of God?
?
Have you ever felt that your intellect 'contains' divine truth, as if truth physically indwells your mind? What would it mean to let go of that spatial metaphor and embrace God's transcendence?
?
This passage shows that any concept of 'indwelling' requires physicality. Can you identify any other beliefs you hold about God that rely on hidden physical analogies? Will you actively examine and strip them away starting today?

Refutation of the Roman Doctrine of Union as Mingling
Baqillani refutes the Roman view that union makes many into one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Christian doctrine of union as a reduction of many to one through mingling is impossible because mingling requires bodily properties, and the divine Word is not a body.

Core Idea
Mingling requires bodies; the divine Word is not a body, so the Roman doctrine of union is impossible.

Baqillani engages with Christian theological claims about the union of divine and human natures in Christ. He identifies a common ground among Roman, Jacobite, and Nestorian Christians: that union involves mingling and mixture. By showing that mingling is a property of bodies, he demonstrates that such a union cannot apply to the pre-eternal Word, which is incorporeal. This argument challenges the logical coherence of the doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the flow of the argument: it states the opponent's view, notes their agreement, then refutes it.
Pay attention to the logical connectives ('إذا', 'فإنه', 'فيلقال لهم').
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The Romans define union as the many becoming little and two becoming one. Note that Baqillani claims this is the view of all of them.
3
Understand the shared premise on mingling
Baqillani points out that Romans agree with Jacobites and Nestorians that union occurs only through mingling (imtizaj) and mixture (ikhtilat). This premise is crucial for the refutation.
Remember: this is a claim about the mechanism of union.
4
Follow the refutation reasoning
Baqillani argues that mingling involves contact (mumassa) and adjacency, which are properties specific to bodies. The divine Word is not a body, so it cannot undergo such union. Therefore the doctrine is impossible.
This is the core of the argument: bodily properties cannot apply to the non-bodily.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this refutation matters: it shows that the Christian doctrine, as stated, leads to an absurdity. Baqillani is defending the transcendence of God.
Think about how this fits into broader kalam discussions on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول الروم إن الاتحاد هو أن يصير الكثير قليلاً والاثنان واحداً فإنه قول جميعهم لأنهم كلهم يزعمون أن الاتحاد هو أن يصير الكثير قليلا والروم توافق اليعاقبة والنسطورية في أن الاتحاد لا يكون إلا بامتزاج واختلاط، فيقال لهم: إذا لم يَجُزْ أن يحصل الاتحاد وأن يصير الاثنان واحداً إلا بالاختلاط والامتزاج وكنا قد بيّنا أن ذلك مماسة وملاصقة وأنه بمنزلة الحركة والسكون والظهور والكمون وأن هذه الأمور أجمع تختص بالأجسام ولا تجوز إلا عليها لم يصح الاتحاد على الكلمة القديمة ولا أن يصير الاثنان واحداً أبداً لأنه معلّق بمحال لا يصح وهو مماسة ما ليس بجسم وذلك ممتنع محال.
As for the saying of the Romans (Rum) that union is that the many becomes little and the two become one – it is the saying of all of them, for they all claim that union is that the many becomes little. And the Romans agree with the Jacobites and Nestorians that union occurs only through mingling and mixture. So it is said to them: If union and the two becoming one cannot occur except through mixture and mingling, and we have already shown that this is contact and adjacency and it is like motion and rest, appearance and concealment, and that all of these things are specific to bodies and are not permissible except upon them, then union is not valid for the pre-eternal Word, nor can the two ever become one, because it depends on an impossible thing, namely contact of what is not a body, and that is impossible and absurd.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative refutation of the Roman (likely Byzantine) Christian view of union (ittihad) as the reduction of many to one, i.e., the two natures becoming one substance. Baqillani notes that all Christians agree that union involves mingling (imtizaj) and mixture (ikhtilat). He then argues: since mingling requires contact and adjacency, which are properties of bodies (like motion, rest, appearance, concealment), and since the Word is not a body, it cannot undergo union that involves contact. Therefore, it is impossible for the eternal Word to become one with a body in that manner. The conclusion is that the Roman doctrine is absurd because it posits contact between a non-body and a body.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani's argument rejects all forms of divine union entirely.
Correction: Baqillani only refutes the specific Christian doctrine that union requires physical mingling, not all concepts of union.

Checkpoint
What property do Jacobites, Nestorians, and Romans all agree on regarding union?
A) That it is without contact.
B) That it requires mingling and mixture.
C) That it changes the eternal into temporal.
D) That it is only through indwelling.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Christian doctrine of union as a reduction of many to one through mingling is logically untenable because it attributes bodily properties to the incorporeal divine Word.

?

?
The Romans failed because they applied physical concepts to the divine. In your daily life, where are you tempted to think of God in human or physical terms—and how can you actively purify your belief from this?
?
This argument shows that any doctrine implying bodily properties for God is impossible. What is at stake, for you personally, if you do not guard your understanding of God's transcendence? How will you ensure you never reduce Him to something the mind can fully grasp?

Absurd Consequences of the Union Doctrine
Baqillani questions the Romans with further logical absurdities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses reductio ad absurdum to refute the Christian claim that a pre-eternal being can unite with a temporal being.

Core Idea
If union is possible, absurdities follow that even opponents would reject.

Baqillani continues his debate with the Romans (Christians) by drawing out the logical consequences of their doctrine of union. He poses a series of hypothetical scenarios that, if union between the divine and human is allowed, would force them to accept equally absurd unions in ordinary experience. This lesson walks through each analogy to see how he turns their own logic against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the rhetorical questions that begin each scenario.
Each 'why do you not allow' introduces a new reductio.
2
Identify the first analogy
Find the opening question about two temporal things uniting. Recognize that if pre-eternal and temporal can unite, then two temporal things should also be able to unite by mixing.
This is a direct parallel to the Christian claim.
3
Examine the second and third analogies
Consider the examples of two pounds/cups of wine and water mixing, and two accidents (motion and blackness) in one substrate. Both are absurd consequences that follow from accepting union.
These analogies highlight that union would conflate distinct substances and properties.
4
Understand the fourth analogy
Read the final example about a simple thing (one lump of clay) becoming many things with parts. This is the most extreme absurdity, showing that unity can produce multiplicity.
This challenges the Christian notion of a simple divine essence uniting with a complex human nature.
5
Reflect on the purpose
Realize that Baqillani is not endorsing these scenarios; he is showing that the Christian position leads to contradictions that they themselves would reject. This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
The goal is to demonstrate the falsity of the union doctrine without directly attacking it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال للروم: إذا جاز أن يتحد قديم بمحدث فيصيران واحداً وقد كانا اثنين قبل الاتحاد فما أنكرتم أن يتحد محدث بمحدث، إذا خالطه ومازجه، فيصيران بذلك واحداً؟ وما أنكرتم أن يصير الرطلان والقدحان اللذان أحدهما خمر والآخر ماء إذا اختلطا وامتزجا رطلاً واحداً وقدحاً واحداً؟ وما أنكرتم أيضاً من أن يصير العرضان إذا وجدا في محل واحد عرضاً واحداً جنساً واحداً وإن كان أحدهما حركة والآخر سواداً؟ وما أنكرتم من أن تتكثر القلة فتصير الطينة الواحدة والشيء الواحد الذي لا بعض له ولا نصف ولا تأليف فيه ولا صورة له مائة ألف شيء وذا أبعاض وأبعاد وأقطار.
And it is said to the Romans: If it is permissible that a pre-eternal thing unites with a temporal thing and they become one, even though they were two before the union, then why do you not allow that a temporal thing unites with another temporal thing, if it mixes and mingles with it, and thereby they become one? And why do you not allow that the two pounds and the two cups, one of which is wine and the other water, if they mix and mingle, become one pound and one cup? And why do you not also allow that two accidents, if they exist in one substrate, become one accident of one kind, even if one of them is motion and the other blackness? And why do you not allow that the few becomes many, so that one lump of clay, and one thing that has no parts, no half, no composition, and no form, becomes a hundred thousand things having parts, dimensions, and extents?
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an argumentative refutation using reduction ad absurdum. Baqillani addresses the Romans again, building on the previous argument. He poses a series of hypotheticals that follow from their own logic: if a pre-eternal (qadim) can unite with a temporal (muhdath) to become one, then why cannot two temporal things unite to become one? He gives examples: two pounds or two cups of wine and water mixing to become one; two accidents (like motion and blackness) coexisting in one substrate becoming one accident; and a formless simple thing becoming many things with parts. These are all absurd according to standard ontological principles, but they follow if one accepts the initial premise of union. The point is that the Christian doctrine of union leads to absurd consequences that even they would reject, thus demonstrating its falsity.

قديم
محدث
عرض
جنس
جسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main strategy Baqillani uses in this passage?
A) Quoting scripture.
B) Analogy to show absurd consequences.
C) Denying the existence of union.
D) Affirming the eternity of matter.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Christian union doctrine leads to absurdities, thus refuting it by reductio ad absurdum.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This argument forces Christians to face an uncomfortable consequence. Is there an area of your own faith where you avoid following an idea to its logical end because you fear what you might find? Will you commit today to loving the truth more than your own comfort?
?
Baqillani uses concrete examples—wine and water, motion and blackness—to make the absurdity vivid. Think of a belief you hold (about God, yourself, or others) that has never been tested against such concrete examples. What would happen if you applied this same method to it?

Union Requires Physical Contact
Baqillani defines union as physical contact and argues it is impossible for the eternal Word.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Christian doctrine of union (incarnation) is impossible because it entails physical contact, which cannot apply to the non-physical Word of God.

Core Idea
If union requires physical contact, then a non-physical being cannot unite with anything.

Baqillani starts by examining the very meaning of 'union' (اتحاد) and 'indwelling' (حلول) as understood by Christians. He argues that these concepts necessarily involve physical contact and adjacency, which are properties of bodies. Since the Word of God is not a body, such a union is rationally impossible. This lesson unpacks that foundational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice the key terms and the logical flow.
Pay attention to the analogy of water in a cistern.
2
Identify the definition of union
Baqillani defines union/indwelling as physical contact and adjacency. Find where he states this and note the terms used.
3
Understand the key inference
Since contact is a property of bodies, and the Word is not a body, union cannot occur. Reflect on why this is a logical necessity.
This is the core of the refutation.
4
Review the conclusion
Read the final sentence: union is attached to an impossibility. Summarize the argument in your own words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كحُلُول الماء في الجُبِّ والدُّهْن في القارورة. وإذا لم يُعقل الحلول إلا مماسة وملاصقة وكانت المجاورة والاجتماع من صفات الأجسام وكانت كلمة الله غير جسم لم يجُز عليها الاتحاد والحلول في الأماكن. وأما قول الروم إن الاتحاد هو أن يصير الكثير قليلاً والاثنان واحداً فإنه قول جميعهم لأنهم كلهم يزعمون أن الاتحاد أن يصير الكثير قليلا والروم توافق اليعاقبة والنسطورية في أن الاتحاد لا يكون إلا بامتزاج واختلاط ، فيقال لهم : إذا لم يَجُزْ أن يحصل الاتحاد وأن يصير الاثنان واحداً إلا بالاختلاط والامتزاج وكنا قد بيّنا أن ذلك مماسة وملاصقة وأنه بمنزلة الحركة والسكون والظهور والكُمُون وأن هذه الأمور أجمع تختص بالأجسام ولا تجوز إلا عليها لم يصح الاتحاد على الكلمة القديمة ولا أن يصير الاثنان واحداً أبداً لأنه معلّق بمحال لا يصح وهو مماسة ما ليس بجسم وذلك ممتنع محال . ويقال للروم : إذا جاز أن يتحد قديم بمحدَث فيصيران واحداً وقد كانا اثنين قبل الاتحاد فما أنكرتم أن يتحد محدّث بمحدث، إذا خالطه ومازجه، فيصيران بذلك واحداً؟ وما أنكرتم أن يصير الرطلان والقدحان اللذان أحدهما خمر والآخر ماء إذا اختلطا وامتزجا رطلاً واحداً وقدحاً واحداً؟ وما أنكرتم أيضاً من أن يصير العرضان إذا وجدا في محل واحد عرضاً واحداً جنساً واحداً وإن كان أحدهما حركة والآخر سواداً؟ وما أنكرتم من أن تتكثر القلة فتصير الطينة الواحدة والشيء الواحد الذي لا بعض له ولا نصف ولا تأليف فيه ولا صورة له مائة ألف شيء وذا أبعاض وأبعاد وأقطار وصور متغايرة وأشكال مختلفة على حدّ ما يقوله بعض الفلاسفة؟ فإن مَرُّوا على هذا أجمع تركوا قولهم وتجاهلوا، وإن أبوه لم يجدوا فصلاً. ويقال للروم أيضاً إذا كان من دينكم مخالفة النسطورية واليعاقبة في قولهم إن الكلمة اتحدت بإنسان واحد جزئي دون غيره، وكنتم تزعمون أن الابن إنما اتحد بالإنسان الكلي وهو الجوهر الجامع لسائر أشخاص الناس لكي يخلص الجوهر الجامع لسائر الناس من المعصية وهو إذا اتحد بالإنسان الكلي صار معه واحداً فيجب أن يصير الجوهر الكلي جزئياً وأقنوماً واحداً لأن الابن أحد الأقانيم وليس هو كل الأقانيم والخواص فهو من حيث القنومة شخص واحدٌ جزئي فإذا صار عند الاتحاد بالإنسان الكلي الذي هو الجوهر الجامع لكل الناس شيئاً واحداً وجب أن يكون كلياً جزئياً لأنه كلي من حيث كان جوهراً جامعاً لسائر الناس وجزئي من حيث كان خاصاً وقنوماً للجوهر العام فيجب أن يكون كلياً جزئياً ؛ وهذا غاية الإحالة .
Like the dissolution of water in a cistern and oil in a bottle. And if indwelling (حلول) is not understood except as touching and contact, and adjacency and conjunction are attributes of bodies, and the Word of God is not a body, then union (اتحاد) and indwelling in places are not permissible for it. As for the statement of the Romans that union is that the many become few and the two become one, that is the statement of all of them, because they all claim that union is that the many become few, and the Romans agree with the Jacobites and Nestorians that union only occurs through mixing and blending. So it is said to them: If it is not permissible that union occurs and that the two become one except through mixing and blending, and we have already explained that that is touching and contact, and that it is like motion and rest, manifestation and concealment, and that all these matters are specific to bodies and are not permissible except upon them, then union is not valid for the eternal Word, nor that the two become one ever, because it is attached to an impossibility that is not valid, namely touching what is not a body, and that is impossible and absurd. And it is said to the Romans: If it is permissible that an eternal thing unites with a temporal thing and they become one, when they were two before union, then why do you deny that a temporal thing could unite with a temporal thing, if it mixes and blends with it, and they become one thereby? And why do you deny that two pounds and two cups, one of which is wine and the other water, when they mix and blend, become one pound and one cup? And why do you also deny that two accidents, if they exist in one substrate, become one accident of one genus, even if one is motion and the other blackness? And why do you deny that the few multiplies, so that the one clay and the one thing that has no part, no half, no composition, no form becomes a hundred thousand things having parts, dimensions, distances, diverse forms, and different shapes, according to what some philosophers say? If they pass over all of this, they abandon their statement and feign ignorance; and if they refuse, they find no decisive answer. And it is also said to the Romans: If it is part of your religion to oppose the Nestorians and Jacobites in their statement that the Word united with one particular individual human to the exclusion of others, and you claim that the Son only united with the universal human, which is the substance (جوهر) encompassing all individual persons of people, in order that the universal substance encompassing all people be saved from disobedience, then when it unites with the universal human, it becomes one with it, so it is necessary that the universal substance become particular and one hypostasis (أقنوم), because the Son is one of the hypostases and is not all the hypostases and properties; thus from the perspective of hypostasis (قنومة) it is one particular person. So when it becomes, upon union with the universal human which is the substance encompassing all people, one thing, it must be universal and particular, because it is universal insofar as it is a substance encompassing all people, and particular insofar as it is a property and a hypostasis for the universal substance. So it must be universal and particular; and this is the utmost absurdity.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the incarnation (union of the divine Word with humanity). It begins by defining the concept of 'indwelling' (حلول) as involving physical contact and adjacency, which are properties of bodies. Since the Word of God is not a body, such indwelling is impossible. The author then addresses the Roman (Byzantine) Christian view that union (اتحاد) means the many become few and two become one. He notes that the Romans agree with the Jacobites and Nestorians that union requires mixing and blending. The argument proceeds: if union requires mixing and contact, and these are bodily attributes, then the eternal Word cannot undergo union because it cannot physically contact a body. Next, the author poses a series of reductio ad absurdum objections: if an eternal and temporal can unite to become one, why can't two temporals unite in the same way? Why can't two substances (like wine and water) become one? Why can't two accidents in one substrate become one? Why can't a simple thing become complex? These analogies highlight the logical consequences of the Christian claim. The author then addresses the Roman distinction from Nestorians and Jacobites: the Romans claim the Son united with the 'universal human' (the universal substance) rather than a particular individual, to save all humanity. The author points out a contradiction: if the Son (a particular hypostasis) unites with the universal human, the result would be both universal (as encompassing all) and particular (as a single hypostasis), which is impossible. The passage ends by calling this the utmost absurdity.

Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that the very concept of union, as understood by Christians, entails physical contact, which is impossible for a non-physical divine being.

C) Because the Word is one of the hypostases and cannot unite with many.
D) Because the Bible does not mention the term 'union'.

Key Takeaway
The Christian concept of union logically entails physical contact, which cannot apply to a non-physical God, making the incarnation impossible.

?

Reductio Arguments Against Union
Baqillani presents four reductio arguments against the possibility of union between eternal and temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the series of reductio ad absurdum arguments Baqillani uses to show the logical consequences of accepting the possibility of union between an eternal and a temporal being.

Core Idea
If an eternal and temporal can unite, then so can two temporals, two substances, two accidents, and a simple thing can become complex.

Having established that union requires physical contact, Baqillani now challenges the Christian position by drawing out its absurd implications. He poses a series of rhetorical questions, each showing that if eternal-temporal union is possible, then many other impossible things would also be possible. This lesson examines those logical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage (the second section) and its translation. Notice the pattern of rhetorical questions.
There are four 'why do you deny' questions.
2
Identify each reductio argument
Go through each of the four objections: (1) two temporals unite, (2) two substances (wine and water) become one, (3) two accidents become one, (4) a simple thing multiplies.
Each one is a consequence of the Christian claim.
3
Understand the logical structure
Baqillani is using analogies. If eternal-temporal union is accepted, then similar unions in the physical world would also have to be accepted, leading to absurdities.
Christians would either have to accept these absurdities or abandon their claim.
4
Reflect on the final sentence
Read the conclusion: if they pass over, they are ignorant; if they refuse, they have no answer. Understand the rhetorical force.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كحُلُول الماء في الجُبِّ والدُّهْن في القارورة. وإذا لم يُعقل الحلول إلا مماسة وملاصقة وكانت المجاورة والاجتماع من صفات الأجسام وكانت كلمة الله غير جسم لم يجُز عليها الاتحاد والحلول في الأماكن. وأما قول الروم إن الاتحاد هو أن يصير الكثير قليلاً والاثنان واحداً فإنه قول جميعهم لأنهم كلهم يزعمون أن الاتحاد أن يصير الكثير قليلا والروم توافق اليعاقبة والنسطورية في أن الاتحاد لا يكون إلا بامتزاج واختلاط ، فيقال لهم : إذا لم يَجُزْ أن يحصل الاتحاد وأن يصير الاثنان واحداً إلا بالاختلاط والامتزاج وكنا قد بيّنا أن ذلك مماسة وملاصقة وأنه بمنزلة الحركة والسكون والظهور والكُمُون وأن هذه الأمور أجمع تختص بالأجسام ولا تجوز إلا عليها لم يصح الاتحاد على الكلمة القديمة ولا أن يصير الاثنان واحداً أبداً لأنه معلّق بمحال لا يصح وهو مماسة ما ليس بجسم وذلك ممتنع محال . ويقال للروم : إذا جاز أن يتحد قديم بمحدَث فيصيران واحداً وقد كانا اثنين قبل الاتحاد فما أنكرتم أن يتحد محدّث بمحدث، إذا خالطه ومازجه، فيصيران بذلك واحداً؟ وما أنكرتم أن يصير الرطلان والقدحان اللذان أحدهما خمر والآخر ماء إذا اختلطا وامتزجا رطلاً واحداً وقدحاً واحداً؟ وما أنكرتم أيضاً من أن يصير العرضان إذا وجدا في محل واحد عرضاً واحداً جنساً واحداً وإن كان أحدهما حركة والآخر سواداً؟ وما أنكرتم من أن تتكثر القلة فتصير الطينة الواحدة والشيء الواحد الذي لا بعض له ولا نصف ولا تأليف فيه ولا صورة له مائة ألف شيء وذا أبعاض وأبعاد وأقطار وصور متغايرة وأشكال مختلفة على حدّ ما يقوله بعض الفلاسفة؟ فإن مَرُّوا على هذا أجمع تركوا قولهم وتجاهلوا، وإن أبوه لم يجدوا فصلاً. ويقال للروم أيضاً إذا كان من دينكم مخالفة النسطورية واليعاقبة في قولهم إن الكلمة اتحدت بإنسان واحد جزئي دون غيره، وكنتم تزعمون أن الابن إنما اتحد بالإنسان الكلي وهو الجوهر الجامع لسائر أشخاص الناس لكي يخلص الجوهر الجامع لسائر الناس من المعصية وهو إذا اتحد بالإنسان الكلي صار معه واحداً فيجب أن يصير الجوهر الكلي جزئياً وأقنوماً واحداً لأن الابن أحد الأقانيم وليس هو كل الأقانيم والخواص فهو من حيث القنومة شخص واحدٌ جزئي فإذا صار عند الاتحاد بالإنسان الكلي الذي هو الجوهر الجامع لكل الناس شيئاً واحداً وجب أن يكون كلياً جزئياً لأنه كلي من حيث كان جوهراً جامعاً لسائر الناس وجزئي من حيث كان خاصاً وقنوماً للجوهر العام فيجب أن يكون كلياً جزئياً ؛ وهذا غاية الإحالة .
Like the dissolution of water in a cistern and oil in a bottle. And if indwelling (حلول) is not understood except as touching and contact, and adjacency and conjunction are attributes of bodies, and the Word of God is not a body, then union (اتحاد) and indwelling in places are not permissible for it. As for the statement of the Romans that union is that the many become few and the two become one, that is the statement of all of them, because they all claim that union is that the many become few, and the Romans agree with the Jacobites and Nestorians that union only occurs through mixing and blending. So it is said to them: If it is not permissible that union occurs and that the two become one except through mixing and blending, and we have already explained that that is touching and contact, and that it is like motion and rest, manifestation and concealment, and that all these matters are specific to bodies and are not permissible except upon them, then union is not valid for the eternal Word, nor that the two become one ever, because it is attached to an impossibility that is not valid, namely touching what is not a body, and that is impossible and absurd. And it is said to the Romans: If it is permissible that an eternal thing unites with a temporal thing and they become one, when they were two before union, then why do you deny that a temporal thing could unite with a temporal thing, if it mixes and blends with it, and they become one thereby? And why do you deny that two pounds and two cups, one of which is wine and the other water, when they mix and blend, become one pound and one cup? And why do you also deny that two accidents, if they exist in one substrate, become one accident of one genus, even if one is motion and the other blackness? And why do you deny that the few multiplies, so that the one clay and the one thing that has no part, no half, no composition, no form becomes a hundred thousand things having parts, dimensions, distances, diverse forms, and different shapes, according to what some philosophers say? If they pass over all of this, they abandon their statement and feign ignorance; and if they refuse, they find no decisive answer. And it is also said to the Romans: If it is part of your religion to oppose the Nestorians and Jacobites in their statement that the Word united with one particular individual human to the exclusion of others, and you claim that the Son only united with the universal human, which is the substance (جوهر) encompassing all individual persons of people, in order that the universal substance encompassing all people be saved from disobedience, then when it unites with the universal human, it becomes one with it, so it is necessary that the universal substance become particular and one hypostasis (أقنوم), because the Son is one of the hypostases and is not all the hypostases and properties; thus from the perspective of hypostasis (قنومة) it is one particular person. So when it becomes, upon union with the universal human which is the substance encompassing all people, one thing, it must be universal and particular, because it is universal insofar as it is a substance encompassing all people, and particular insofar as it is a property and a hypostasis for the universal substance. So it must be universal and particular; and this is the utmost absurdity.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the incarnation (union of the divine Word with humanity). It begins by defining the concept of 'indwelling' (حلول) as involving physical contact and adjacency, which are properties of bodies. Since the Word of God is not a body, such indwelling is impossible. The author then addresses the Roman (Byzantine) Christian view that union (اتحاد) means the many become few and two become one. He notes that the Romans agree with the Jacobites and Nestorians that union requires mixing and blending. The argument proceeds: if union requires mixing and contact, and these are bodily attributes, then the eternal Word cannot undergo union because it cannot physically contact a body. Next, the author poses a series of reductio ad absurdum objections: if an eternal and temporal can unite to become one, why can't two temporals unite in the same way? Why can't two substances (like wine and water) become one? Why can't two accidents in one substrate become one? Why can't a simple thing become complex? These analogies highlight the logical consequences of the Christian claim. The author then addresses the Roman distinction from Nestorians and Jacobites: the Romans claim the Son united with the 'universal human' (the universal substance) rather than a particular individual, to save all humanity. The author points out a contradiction: if the Son (a particular hypostasis) unites with the universal human, the result would be both universal (as encompassing all) and particular (as a single hypostasis), which is impossible. The passage ends by calling this the utmost absurdity.

Key Terms
القديم
المحدث
الاختلاط
الامتزاج
العرض
الجوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the union of eternal and temporal is a unique, one-time event that does not imply other unions.
Correction: Baqillani shows that accepting such a union logically opens the door to many other impossible unions, exposing inconsistency.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the reductio arguments Baqillani uses?
A) Two temporal things uniting
B) Two pounds of wine and water becoming one pound
C) Two angels uniting into one
D) A simple clay becoming a complex thing

Key Takeaway
Accepting the possibility of union between eternal and temporal leads to absurd consequences that even Christians would reject.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you confront a logical inconsistency in a belief you hold dear, do you tend to ignore it (like Baqillani says the Christians might) or do you seek an honest resolution? Where in your own faith are you tempted to claim 'mystery' to avoid logical tension, and what would it cost you to follow the argument where it leads?
?
Think of a specific belief or practice you consider 'special' and immune to reason. How would you respond if someone applied the same reductio method to it—pushing it to an absurd conclusion? Would you reject the conclusion and feel exposed, or would you double down? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in logic as a gift from God?
?
Baqillani forces the reader to see that accepting one absurdity opens the door to many. Is there an area in your life where you have made an exception to a principle you hold elsewhere? If so, name it. Can you honestly maintain that exception after seeing how Baqillani dismantles the exemption claim? What would it mean for you to be consistent?

Sects and Disagreements
advanced
7 min
Refutation of Universal Human Union
Baqillani refutes the Roman view of union with the universal human by showing it entails a logical contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's specific refutation of the Roman Christian doctrine that the Son united with the universal human (الجوهر الكلي) rather than a particular individual, and why this leads to contradiction.

Core Idea
If the Son (a particular hypostasis) unites with the universal human, the result would be both universal and particular, which is impossible.

Baqillani now addresses a finer point of Christian theology: the Roman view that the Son united with the universal human substance (the essence of humanity) rather than a specific person. He draws out a logical impossibility: the result of such a union would have to be both universal (as it encompasses all humans) and particular (as it is a single hypostasis), which is contradictory. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage (the third section) and its translation. Note the terms 'الجوهر الكلي' and 'الأقنوم'.
2
Understand the Roman position
The Romans claim the Son united with the universal human to save all humanity, not just one individual. Find where this is stated.
3
Identify the contradiction
Baqillani argues that the Son is a particular hypostasis (شخص جزئي). If it unites with the universal human (الجوهر الكلي), the result must be both universal and particular. Walk through this logic.
This is the 'utmost absurdity' (غاية الإحالة).
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Why is it impossible for something to be both universal and particular? Explain in your own words.

Why does Baqillani consider the Roman view of union with the universal human absurd?
A) Because the universal human does not exist.
B) Because the result would have to be both universal and particular.
C) Because the Son is eternal and cannot unite with a temporal substance.
D) Because the Nestorians are correct that the Word united with one individual.
