How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever hold a belief about God that seems noble or appealing but, when examined carefully, contradicts the pure, logically consistent oneness of Allah? What is that belief, and are you willing to test it against the arguments of the scholars like Baqillani?
?
This passage exposes that even a seemingly small error in theology (like the nature of union) leads to absurdity. Where in your understanding of Tawheed might you be tolerating a small error because it feels comfortable? Will you search for the truth even if it means abandoning a long-held view?
?
The Romans wanted to save all humanity, but their method was impossible. Is there a desire in your heart to 'save' people through something other than pure submission to Allah—perhaps by softening the truth or accommodating falsehood? How will you repent from that and rely only on Allah's guidance?

Argument Against Union as an Act
Baqillani questions whether the act of union has an agent and explores contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's method of questioning the Christian doctrine of union by analyzing whether the act of union has an agent and who that agent could be.

Core Idea
Union as an act requires an agent — the Christian position leads to an unresolved dilemma.

Baqillani begins by stating the Christian consensus that the union is an act. He then poses a critical question: does this act have an agent or not? This simple question unravels the coherence of the doctrine, forcing Christians to specify the agent of union in a way consistent with their trinitarian theology. The passage sets up a series of possibilities that expose logical difficulties.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the dilemma
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the claim that union is an act and the first question Baqillani asks.
Notice that Baqillani states the unanimous Christian position before questioning it.
2
Analyze the two branches
Consider the two possible answers: no agent, or an agent. Reflect on the implications of each branch.
The 'no agent' branch leads to a contradiction with Christian acceptance of agents for other acts.
3
Examine the agent options
If they say there is an agent, Baqillani asks who that agent is. The passage lists several possibilities, all of which are problematic.
The argument is incomplete but sets up a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في قول النصارى إن الاتحاد فعل وقد أطبقت النصارى على أن الاتحاد فعل من الأفعال صار به المتحد متَّحِداً والمسيح مسيحاً فيقال لهم : خبرونا عن الاتحاد بالإنسان المتحدة به الكلمة إذا كان فعلاً ، فهل له عندكم فاعل أم لا؟ فإن قالوا : لا فاعل له، قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم من أن يكون سائر الأفعال والحوادث لا فاعل لها؟ وليس من قولهم . وإن قالوا : الاتحاد فعل لفاعل فعله وكان به متحداً قيل لهم : فمن فاعله أهو الجوهر الجامع للأقانيم دون الأقانيم أم الأقانيم الثلاثة دونه ، أم هو والثلاثة الأقانيم ، أم الفاعل له واحد من الأقانيم؟ فإن ذلك ....
Section on the Christians' statement that the union is an act. The Christians have unanimously agreed that the union is an act among acts by which the united becomes united and the Messiah becomes Messiah. So it is said to them: Inform us about the union with the human with whom the Word united—if it is an act, does it have an agent according to you or not? If they say: It has no agent, it is said to them: Then why do you not deny that other acts and events have no agent? And that is not from their statement. And if they say: The union is an act of an agent who performed it, and by it he became united, it is said to them: Who is its agent? Is it the substance common to the hypostases without the hypostases, or the three hypostases without it, or it and the three hypostases, or is its agent one of the hypostases? For that...
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a section (فصل) dedicated to the Christian claim that the union (اتحاد) is an act (فعل). Baqillani states that all Christians agree that the union is an act. He then poses a dilemma: either this act has an agent or it does not. If they say it has no agent, then they would have to deny that any other acts or events have agents, which they do not believe. If they say it has an agent, then he asks who that agent is: the common substance of the hypostases (the divine essence) apart from the hypostases, the three hypostases apart from the substance, both together, or one individual hypostasis? The argument is cut off at the bottom of the page, but the structure sets up a series of options that would likely be reduced to absurdity. The purpose is to show that the Christian doctrine of union leads to contradictory or undefined agency.

Key Terms
الاتحاد
فعل
فاعل
الأفعال
الحوادث
الجوهر
الأقانيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The union being an act does not require an agent.
Correction: Baqillani argues that if union is an act, it must have an agent; otherwise, all acts could lack agents, which Christians deny.

Checkpoint
What is the first question Baqillani asks about the union if it is considered an act?
A) Is it a physical or spiritual act?
B) Does it have an agent or not?
C) Is it eternal or temporal?
D) Is it performed by the Father, Son, or Holy Spirit?

Key Takeaway
Baqillani forces Christians to either admit that the union has no agent (contradicting their view of other acts) or to specify an agent among their hypostases in a way that is theologically problematic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When Baqillani dismantles the Christian claim that union is an act, he holds them to the same logical standard they accept elsewhere. Can you say the same about your own beliefs? Which of your convictions have you never subjected to such rigorous, honest questioning? Commit this week to examine one belief you hold about Allah's names or attributes using the Quran and Sunnah as your criteria.
?
The Christians in this passage cannot pinpoint who the agent of the union is without contradicting their own theology. In your daily worship, do you ever find yourself saying or doing things that subtly contradict the oneness of Allah—like relying on means while forgetting the Giver, or attributing outcomes to yourself rather than Allah? How will you root out such hidden shirk?
?
This lesson shows how a single incoherent premise unravels an entire belief system. Is there any inconsistency in your faith practice that you have been overlooking? Will you take the time to resolve it today, even if it means admitting you were wrong?

The Impossibility of the Word's Union with the Universal Human
Refuting Christian claim that the Word united with the universal human essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that the Word united with the universal human essence leads to a logical contradiction, as presented by Imam al-Baqillani.

Core Idea
The universal cannot become particular without absurdity.

This passage presents a key argument from Imam al-Baqillani refuting the Melkite Christian doctrine that the Word (the Son) united with the universal human essence rather than a specific individual. By exposing the logical impossibility of a universal essence becoming a particular hypostasis, the author demonstrates the incoherence of this theological claim. Understanding this argument sharpens one's ability to identify contradictions in religious doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Christian sects mentioned
The passage references Nestorians, Jacobites, and Byzantines (Melkites). Nestorians and Jacobites believe the Word united with a particular human (Jesus), while Melkites claim the Word united with the universal human essence. This sets up the argument.
The Melkites aim to explain how Christ saves all of humanity by uniting with the universal essence.
2
Follow the logical reductio
The author assumes the Melkite claim and derives a contradiction: the Son is a particular hypostasis, so if He unites with the universal human, the universal must become a particular hypostasis. But the universal is by definition all-encompassing, so it cannot be particular. Thus, it would need to be both universal and particular, which is impossible.
This is a clear example of reductio ad absurdum.
3
Appreciate the argument's force
The contradiction shows the Melkite claim is logically impossible. This reflects the use of rational argumentation in Islamic theology to refute unorthodox views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصور متغايرة وأشكال مختلفة على حدّ ما يقوله بعض الفلاسفة؟ فإن مروا على هذا أجمع تركوا قولهم وتجاهلوا، وإن أبوه لم يجدوا فصلا. ويقال للروم أيضا إذا كان من دينكم مخالفة النسطورية واليعاقبة في قولهم إن الكلمة اتحدت بإنسان واحد جزئي دون غيره، وكنتم تزعمون أن الابن إنما اتحد بالإنسان الكلي وهو الجوهر الجامع لسائر أشخاص الناس لكي يخلص الجوهر الجامع لسائر الناس من المعصية وهو إذا اتحد بالإنسان الكلي صار معه واحدا فيجب أن يصير الجوهر الكلي جزئيا وأقنوما واحدا لأن الابن أحد الأقانيم وليس هو كل الأقانيم والخواص فهو من حيث القنومة شخص واحد جزئي فإذا صار عند الاتحاد بالإنسان الكلي الذي هو الجوهر الجامع لكل الناس شيئا واحدا وجب أن يكون كليا جزئيا لأنه كلي من حيث كان جوهرا جامعا لسائر الناس وجزئي من حيث كان خاصا وقنوما للجوهر العام فيجب أن يكون كليا جزئيا؛ وهذا غاية الإحالة.
Thus, [there are] diverse forms and different shapes according to what some philosophers say? If they pass over this entirely, they abandon their statement and act ignorant, and they find no distinction. And it is said to the Byzantines also: Since your religion includes the opposition of the Nestorians and Jacobites in their statement that the Word united with one particular individual human to the exclusion of others, while you claim that the Son only united with the universal human, which is the substance comprising all human individuals, in order to save the universal substance comprising all of humanity from sin; and if He unites with the universal human, He becomes one with it, then the universal substance must become particular and one hypostasis, because the Son is one of the hypostases and He is not all the hypostases and properties, so He is in terms of hypostasis one particular person. So if at the union with the universal human, which is the substance comprising all people, He becomes one thing, then it must be that He becomes both universal and particular: universal insofar as He is a substance comprising all people, and particular insofar as He is a specific property and hypostasis of the universal substance; so it must be both universal and particular. And this is the utmost impossibility.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific Christian claim that the Word (the Son) united with the universal human essence rather than a particular individual. The author begins by noting that some philosophers (presumably Christian theologians) may try to evade the argument, but then he directly addresses the Byzantines (likely the Orthodox or Melkite Christians) who differ from the Nestorians and Jacobites. The Nestorians and Jacobites claim the Word united with a particular individual human (Jesus), while the Melkites claim the Word united with the universal human essence (the common substance of all humans) in order to save all of humanity. The author argues that this claim leads to a contradiction: The Son is a particular hypostasis (one of the three divine hypostases). If He unites with the universal human essence, then that universal essence becomes one with Him and thus must become a particular hypostasis. But the universal essence, by definition, encompasses all human individuals, so it cannot be particular. It would have to be both universal and particular simultaneously, which is impossible. Therefore, the Melkite claim is absurd.

إنسان جزئي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the universal human essence can become particular without changing its nature, but the author shows this is logically impossible.
Correction: The universal essence, by definition, includes all individuals; becoming particular would exclude the others, contradicting its universality.

Checkpoint
What is the contradiction the author points out in the claim that the Word united with the universal human?
A) The universal human would become divine.
B) The universal human would have to be both universal and particular simultaneously.
C) The Word would become a human being.
D) The union would require the Word to be both Father and Son.

Key Takeaway
The Melkite claim that the Word united with the universal human essence entails the impossible consequence that the universal must become particular, thereby refuting their doctrine.

?
The Melkites wanted to save all humanity by a universal union. Do you ever try to 'universalize' your own shortcomings or sins, hoping that a general intention covers specific failures? Where might you need to confront a particular fault rather than hiding behind a universal excuse?

The Christian Claim of Union as an Act: Does It Have an Agent?
Initial dilemma and two refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial dilemma posed by Baqillani against the Christian claim that the incarnation is an act, specifically the question of whether this act has an agent and the refutation of the first two possible answers.

Core Idea
If the union is an act, it must have an agent; but identifying that agent leads to contradictions.

Baqillani opens his refutation by first establishing the Christian claim that the incarnation (ittihad) is an act. He then asks a fundamental question: does this act have an agent? He considers two initial possibilities: either there is no agent, or the agent is the common divine essence. Both lead to problems, as this lesson will show.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Baqillani structures the argument as a series of questions.
The passage is a typical kalam dialectical argument.
2
Identify the Christian claim
Identify the statement that the union is an act. Understand why this matters for the debate.
3
Analyze the first dilemma
The author asks: does the act have an agent? Consider the two initial answers and their refutations.
Focus on the logical consequences drawn.
4
Understand the refutation for 'no agent'
If there is no agent, then all acts could be agentless, which is absurd according to the Christians' own principles.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Understand the refutation for 'agent is the common essence'
If the common essence is the agent, then it must be the one united, which contradicts the Christian claim that only the Son is incarnate.
This reveals inconsistency in their doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في قول النصارى إن الاتحاد فعل وقد أطبقت النصارى على أن الاتحاد فعل من الأفعال صار به المتحد متحدا والمسيح مسيحا فيقال لهم: خبرونا عن الاتحاد بالإنسان المتحدة به الكلمة إذا كان فعلا، فهل له عندكم فاعل أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا فاعل له، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم من أن يكون سائر الأفعال والحوادث لا فاعل لها؟ وليس من قولهم. وإن قالوا: الاتحاد فعل لفاعل فعله وكان به متحدا قيل لهم: فمن فاعله أهو الجوهر الجامع للأقانيم دون الأقانيم أم الأقانيم الثلاثة دونه، أم هو والثلاثة الأقانيم، أم الفاعل له واحد من الأقانيم؟ فإن قالوا: هو الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم، قيل: فيجب أن يكون الجوهر هو المتحد بالجسد والإنسان الكلي أو الجزئي على ما تختارونه؛ لأن المتحد عندكم هو من فعل الاتحاد دون من لم يفعله ويجب أيضا أن يكون هو الإله المستحق للعبادة؛ لأنه هو الفعال لها. وكذلك إن قالوا: الجوهر والأقانيم فعلوا الاتحاد قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون هو والثلاثة الأقانيم متحدين بالإنسان؛ ولا معنى لتولكم: إن الابن وحده هو المتحد دون الأب والروح ودون الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم وهذا نقض قولكم إن الاتحاد للابن فقط. وكذلك إن قالوا: إنما فعل الاتحاد الأقانيم الثلاثة دون الجوهر قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون الروح أيضا متحدا وألا يكون الابن وحده من خواص الجوهر متحدا. وإن قالوا: فاعل الاتحاد إنما هو الابن وحده ولانفراده بفعل الاتحاد متحدا دون الروح، قيل لهم: فإذا جاز أن ينفرد الابن بفعل حادث هو الاتحاد دون الروح والأب ودون الجوهر العام، فلم لا يجوز أن ينفرد الروح بفعل حادث وحوادث أخر وأن ينفرد كل أقنوم من الأقانيم بعوالم وأفعال لا يفعلها الآخر وينفرد الجوهر الجامع بفعل غير فعلها؟. وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، جاز أن تتمانع وتختلف ويقال هم: إذا كانت الأقانيم تفعل كما أن الجوهر الجامع لها يفعل فلم صار بأن يكون جامعا لها وأن تكون خواص له أولى، أولى من أن يكون هو خاصا لها وهي
Section on the statement of the Christians that the union is an act. The Christians have agreed that the union is one of the acts by which the united becomes united and the Christ becomes Christ. So it is said to them: Inform us about the union with the human to whom the Word is united, since it is an act: does it have an agent according to you or not? If they say: It has no agent, it is said to them: What prevents you from [saying] that all acts and events have no agent? And that is not from their statement. If they say: The union is an act of an agent who performed it and by it became united, it is said to them: Who is its agent? Is it the common substance of the hypostases without the hypostases, or the three hypostases without it, or it and the three hypostases, or the agent is one of the hypostases? If they say: It is the common universal substance of the hypostases, it is said: Then the substance must be the one united with the body and the universal or particular human according to your choice; because the united according to you is the one who performed the union, not the one who did not perform it; and it must also be the god worthy of worship because He is the one who acts upon it. Likewise, if they say: The substance and the hypostases performed the union, it is said to them: Then He and the three hypostases must be united with the human; and there is no meaning to your statement that the Son alone is the united, to the exclusion of the Father and the Spirit and the common universal substance of the hypostases, and this contradicts your statement that the union is only for the Son. Likewise, if they say: Only the three hypostases performed the union without the substance, it is said to them: Then the Spirit must also be united, and the Son alone should not be united as one of the properties of the substance. And if they say: The agent of the union is only the Son alone, and by His sole performance of the union He is united to the exclusion of the Spirit, it is said to them: If it is permissible for the Son to perform alone a contingent act which is the union, to the exclusion of the Spirit and the Father and the common substance, then why is it not permissible for the Spirit to perform alone a contingent act and other contingent acts, and for each hypostasis of the hypostases to perform alone worlds and acts that the other does not perform, and for the universal substance to perform an act other than their acts? And if that is so, it becomes permissible for them to be mutually opposed and differ; and it is said to them: If the hypostases act as the universal substance acts, then why is it more appropriate that it be comprehensive of them and that they be properties of it, rather than that it be a property of them and they
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine that the incarnation (ittihad) is an act (fi'l). The author begins by stating that the Christians unanimously claim the union is an act. He then poses a dilemma: if it is an act, does it have an agent (fā'il)? He considers several possible answers the Christians might give and refutes each. First, if they say it has no agent, then that would imply all acts have no agent, which is absurd and contradicts their own principles. Second, if they say the agent is the common divine essence (al-jawhar al-āmm) without the hypostases, then the essence itself would be the one united with the human body, making it the deity incarnate, contradicting the Christian claim that only the Son is incarnate. Third, if they say the agent is the essence and the three hypostases together, then all three hypostases would be united with the human, not just the Son. Fourth, if they say the agent is the three hypostases alone without the essence, then the Spirit would also be united, not exclusively the Son. Fifth, if they say the agent is the Son alone, then by the same logic each hypostasis could perform acts independently, leading to polytheism and undermining the unity of the divine essence. The argument is incomplete but clearly demonstrates the logical contradictions in the Christian view.

Key Terms
الاتحاد
فعل
فاعل
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Christian claim is internally consistent if they simply say the union has an agent.
Correction: The author shows that even if there is an agent, identifying it as the common essence leads to contradiction with the doctrine of the Son's exclusive incarnation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the consequence if the Christians say the union has no agent?
A) It would mean the union is not a real act.
B) It would imply that all acts could have no agent, which contradicts their own principles.
C) The union would be impossible because an act requires an agent.
D) The Son would not be truly incarnate.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that the incarnation is an act by first demanding an agent, then showing that the two initial possibilities (no agent or agent=common essence) are untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you believe something about God, do you examine whether it logically holds, or do you accept it out of tradition? Are you willing to follow the truth even if it means rejecting what you've been taught?
?
The Christians hold that the union is an act. But if we claim that God does something, we must think about what that implies about His nature. Do you ever make claims about God without thinking through their implications?
?
This passage shows how a false belief collapses under logical scrutiny. What false beliefs might you be holding that you have never subjected to such scrutiny? Commit to examining them today.

Further Refutations: The Candidates for Agent of the Union
Refutations of remaining three agent candidates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutations of the remaining possible agents for the union: the essence with hypostases, the hypostases alone, and the Son alone.

Core Idea
Every attempt to identify the agent of the union leads to a contradiction with Christian trinitarian doctrine.

Baqillani continues his dialectical argument by considering three more possible agents for the act of union: the essence together with the hypostases, the hypostases alone without the essence, and finally the Son alone. Each is refuted, showing the logical inconsistency of the Christian position. The argument for the Son alone is cut off but the direction is clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the remaining passage
Read the Arabic from 'وكذلك إن قالوا' to the end, along with the translation. Note that the passage ends mid-sentence.
The text is incomplete; we have only the beginning of the refutation for the Son as agent.
2
Analyze the third option
If the agent is the essence and the hypostases together, then all three hypostases would be united, contradicting the exclusive incarnation of the Son.
3
Analyze the fourth option
If the agent is the hypostases alone without the essence, then the Spirit would also be united, not just the Son.
4
Analyze the fifth option
If the agent is the Son alone, then by the same logic each hypostasis could act independently, leading to a plurality of gods.
The argument is cut off but the implication is clear.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how Baqillani systematically eliminates all possible answers, showing the Christian position is untenable.
This is a classic kalam reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في قول النصارى إن الاتحاد فعل وقد أطبقت النصارى على أن الاتحاد فعل من الأفعال صار به المتحد متحدا والمسيح مسيحا فيقال لهم: خبرونا عن الاتحاد بالإنسان المتحدة به الكلمة إذا كان فعلا، فهل له عندكم فاعل أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا فاعل له، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم من أن يكون سائر الأفعال والحوادث لا فاعل لها؟ وليس من قولهم. وإن قالوا: الاتحاد فعل لفاعل فعله وكان به متحدا قيل لهم: فمن فاعله أهو الجوهر الجامع للأقانيم دون الأقانيم أم الأقانيم الثلاثة دونه، أم هو والثلاثة الأقانيم، أم الفاعل له واحد من الأقانيم؟ فإن قالوا: هو الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم، قيل: فيجب أن يكون الجوهر هو المتحد بالجسد والإنسان الكلي أو الجزئي على ما تختارونه؛ لأن المتحد عندكم هو من فعل الاتحاد دون من لم يفعله ويجب أيضا أن يكون هو الإله المستحق للعبادة؛ لأنه هو الفعال لها. وكذلك إن قالوا: الجوهر والأقانيم فعلوا الاتحاد قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون هو والثلاثة الأقانيم متحدين بالإنسان؛ ولا معنى لتولكم: إن الابن وحده هو المتحد دون الأب والروح ودون الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم وهذا نقض قولكم إن الاتحاد للابن فقط. وكذلك إن قالوا: إنما فعل الاتحاد الأقانيم الثلاثة دون الجوهر قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون الروح أيضا متحدا وألا يكون الابن وحده من خواص الجوهر متحدا. وإن قالوا: فاعل الاتحاد إنما هو الابن وحده ولانفراده بفعل الاتحاد متحدا دون الروح، قيل لهم: فإذا جاز أن ينفرد الابن بفعل حادث هو الاتحاد دون الروح والأب ودون الجوهر العام، فلم لا يجوز أن ينفرد الروح بفعل حادث وحوادث أخر وأن ينفرد كل أقنوم من الأقانيم بعوالم وأفعال لا يفعلها الآخر وينفرد الجوهر الجامع بفعل غير فعلها؟. وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، جاز أن تتمانع وتختلف ويقال هم: إذا كانت الأقانيم تفعل كما أن الجوهر الجامع لها يفعل فلم صار بأن يكون جامعا لها وأن تكون خواص له أولى، أولى من أن يكون هو خاصا لها وهي
Section on the statement of the Christians that the union is an act. The Christians have agreed that the union is one of the acts by which the united becomes united and the Christ becomes Christ. So it is said to them: Inform us about the union with the human to whom the Word is united, since it is an act: does it have an agent according to you or not? If they say: It has no agent, it is said to them: What prevents you from [saying] that all acts and events have no agent? And that is not from their statement. If they say: The union is an act of an agent who performed it and by it became united, it is said to them: Who is its agent? Is it the common substance of the hypostases without the hypostases, or the three hypostases without it, or it and the three hypostases, or the agent is one of the hypostases? If they say: It is the common universal substance of the hypostases, it is said: Then the substance must be the one united with the body and the universal or particular human according to your choice; because the united according to you is the one who performed the union, not the one who did not perform it; and it must also be the god worthy of worship because He is the one who acts upon it. Likewise, if they say: Only the three hypostases performed the union without the substance, it is said to them: Then the Spirit must also be united, and the Son alone should not be united as one of the properties of the substance. And if that is so, it becomes permissible for them to be mutually opposed and differ; and it is said to them: If the hypostases act as the universal substance acts, then why is it more appropriate that it be comprehensive of them and that they be properties of it, rather than that it be a property of them and they

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine that the incarnation (ittihad) is an act (fi'l). The author begins by stating that the Christians unanimously claim the union is an act. He then poses a dilemma: if it is an act, does it have an agent (fā'il)? He considers several possible answers the Christians might give and refutes each. Fourth, if they say the agent is the three hypostases alone without the essence, then the Spirit would also be united, not exclusively the Son. The argument is incomplete but clearly demonstrates the logical contradictions in the Christian view.

Baqillani refutes the remaining possible agents for the act of union, showing that each leads to a contradiction with Christian trinitarian doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a long-standing belief, have you ever rigorously tested it by asking 'What if I trace this to its logical consequences?' like Baqillani did with the Christian claims? If not, what might you discover about your own assumptions?
?
Baqillani exposed contradictions by examining each candidate for the union. What belief do you hold that might hide contradictions if you honestly examined every possible way it could be true? Are you willing to confront that discomfort?
?
If you discovered that a fundamental premise of your faith leads to a logical absurdity, would you have the courage to abandon it? Or would you rationalize it away rather than face the cost of change?

Refuting the Claim that the General Substance Is the Subject of Union
Baqillani refutes the union of the general substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the Christian claim that the general substance is the subject of union, and why this implies that the substance alone would deserve worship.

Core Idea
If the substance is the subject of union, it alone deserves worship.

Baqillani begins by addressing the Christian claim that the divine is the general substance that encompasses the three hypostases. He argues that if this substance is the one that unites with the human being in Christ, then it must be the active agent of union, and thus the only true deity. This undermines the Trinity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the argument. Then read the translation to understand the logical structure.
Notice that Baqillani uses conditional reasoning starting with 'if they say...'.
2
Identify the Christian claim
The Christians claim that God is the general substance that encompasses the hypostases. This is the premise Baqillani attacks.
3
Trace Baqillani's logical consequence
Baqillani argues that if that substance is united with the human body, then it must have performed the act of union, making it the sole agent and thus the only deity worthy of worship.
This directly contradicts the Christian belief in a Trinity of persons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: هو الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم، فيجب أن يكون الجوهر هو المتحد بالجسد والإنسان الكلي أو الجزئي على ما تختارونه؛ لأن المتحد عندكم هو من فعل الاتحاد دون من لم يفعله ويجب أيضاً أن يكون هو الإله المستحق للعبادة؛ لأنه هو الفعّال لها. وكذلك إن قالوا: الجوهر والأقانيم فعلوا الاتحاد قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون هو والثلاثة الأقانيم متحدين بالإنسان؛ ولا معنى لقولكم: إن الابن وحده هو المتحد دون الأب والروح ودون الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم وهذا نقض قولكم إن الاتحاد للابن فقط. وكذلك إن قالوا: إنما فعل الاتحاد الأقانيم الثلاثة دون الجوهر قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون الروح أيضاً متحداً وأن لا يكون الابن وحده من خواص الجوهر متحداً. وإن قالوا: فاعل الاتحاد إنما هو الابن وحده ولإنفراده بفعل الاتحاد متحداً دون الروح، قيل لهم: فإذا جاز أن ينفرد الابن بفعل حادث هو الاتحاد دون الروح والأب ودون الجوهر العام، فلِمَ لا يجوز أن ينفرد الروح بفعل حادث وحوادث أُخر وأن ينفرد كل أقنوم من الأقانيم بعوالم وأفعال لا يفعلها الآخر وينفرد الجوهر الجامع بفعل غير فعلها؟ وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، جاز أن تتمانع وتختلف ويقال: إذا كانت الأقانيم تفعل كما أن الجوهر الجامع لها يفعل فلِمَ صار بأن يكون جامعاً لها وأن تكون خواص له أولى، أولى من أن يكون هو خاصاً لها وهي جامعة له فيكون أقنوماً من أقانيمها؟ فلا يجدون لذلك مدفعاً.
They said: He is the general substance that encompasses the hypostases. So it must be that the substance is that which united with the body and with the universal or particular human being, according to your choice; because the united one according to you is the one who performed the act of union, not the one who did not perform it. And it must also be that He is the deity worthy of worship because He is the one who performs worship. Likewise, if they say: The substance and the hypostases performed the union, it is said to them: Then it must be that He and the three hypostases united with the human being; and there is no meaning to your statement that only the Son united without the Father and the Spirit and without the general substance encompassing the hypostases, and this invalidates your statement that the union is only for the Son. Likewise, if they say: Only the three hypostases performed the union without the substance, it is said to them: Then the Spirit must also be united, and the Son alone from the properties of the substance should not be united. And if they say: The agent of the union is only the Son alone, and because of His uniqueness in performing the union He is united without the Spirit, it is said to them: So if it is permissible for the Son to be unique in performing a temporal act which is the union without the Spirit and the Father and without the general substance, then why is it not permissible for the Spirit to be unique in performing a temporal act and other acts, and for each hypostasis among the hypostases to be unique in worlds and acts that the other does not do, and for the general substance to be unique in an act other than their act? And if that is so, it becomes possible that they oppose and differ, and it is said: Since the hypostases act as the general substance that encompasses them acts, why is it more fitting for it to encompass them and for them to be properties of it, than for it to be a property of them and for them to encompass it, so that it would become a hypostasis among their hypostases? They will find no way to repel that.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of Christian claims about the union (ittihad) of the divine substance (jawhar) and the hypostases (aqanim) in Christ. Baqillani addresses successive Christian responses by applying the Christians' own logic. He begins with the claim that the general substance is the subject of union: if so, then that substance must be the one that actively performed the union, making it the only true deity, which contradicts the Trinity. Next, if they say both substance and hypostases performed the union, then all three hypostases must be united, not just the Son. If they say only the three hypostases performed the union without the substance, then the Spirit must also be united. If they say only the Son performed the union alone, then Baqillani argues that if the Son can act independently in performing the union, then the Spirit and each hypostasis could also act independently in other acts, leading to multiple distinct agents. This would imply that the hypostases could oppose each other and that the general substance might itself become a property of them, making it just another hypostasis. This conclusion is absurd to Christians, so they have no defense.

Key Terms
الجوهر العام
الأقانيم
الاتحاد
الإنسان الكلي
الإنسان الجزئي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani conclude if the general substance is the subject of union?
A) The substance is not divine.
B) The substance alone is the deity worthy of worship.
C) The hypostases are also united.
D) The union is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that if the general substance is the subject of union, it would logically be the only deity, undermining the Trinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani insists that only the one who acts deserves worship. Examine your own life: do you attribute power, provision, or guidance to anyone or anything other than Allah? Are there moments when you subconsciously rely on created means as if they have independent power? Today, consciously detach your heart from all created causes and direct your reliance solely to Allah, the true actor.
?
The Christians in this passage hold a belief that logically leads to a contradiction. Are there any beliefs or practices in your own life that, if followed to their logical conclusion, would clash with the Oneness of Allah? For instance, do you ever reverence a saint, a scholar, or a leader in a way that compromises tawheed? Ask Allah for clarity and courage to abandon any such association.
?
Baqillani's argument forces his opponents to confront the implications of their claim. When was the last time you honestly examined your own theological positions and asked, 'Does this belief lead to something I do not truly accept?' Are you willing to follow the truth even when it is uncomfortable? Commit to study a topic in 'aqeedah that you usually avoid, and let the evidence guide your heart.

Refuting Claims of Joint or Hypostatic-Only Union
Baqillani refutes two Christian responses on union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes two additional Christian responses: that both substance and hypostases performed the union, or that only the hypostases did.

Core Idea
If both substance and hypostases act, all three hypostases must unite; if only hypostases act, then the Spirit must also unite.

After the first refutation, Baqillani anticipates two alternative Christian positions: either the substance and hypostases together performed the union, or only the three hypostases did. He shows that both options lead to contradictions with the Christian claim that only the Son is united.

Guided Path
1
Read the two conditional arguments
The passage contains two 'if they say...' statements. Read each carefully and see how Baqillani responds.
The structure is: Christian claim -> necessary consequence -> contradiction.
2
Analyze the first alternative
If they say the substance and hypostases together performed the union, then all three hypostases must be united, but Christians claim only the Son united. This invalidates their doctrine.
3
Analyze the second alternative
If they say only the three hypostases (without the substance) performed the union, then the Spirit must also be united, contradicting the claim that only the Son is united.
Baqillani exposes the inconsistency in Christian theology.

The Consequences of the Son Acting Alone
Baqillani refutes the claim that only the Son performed the union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the Christian claim that only the Son performed the union, and how this leads to multiple independent agents and the absurdity of the substance becoming a property of the hypostases.

Core Idea
If the Son acts alone, other hypostases can act independently, leading to multiple gods.

Baqillani now addresses the final Christian position: that only the Son performed the act of union. He argues that if the Son can act independently in performing a temporal act like the union, then there is no reason why the other hypostases cannot also act independently. This would imply multiple agents and potentially multiple gods. Moreover, the general substance could become a property of the hypostases, making it just another hypostasis, which is absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth conditional
Read the passage starting from 'If they say: The agent of the union is only the Son alone...' and follow the argument to its conclusion.
This is the longest and most complex part of Baqillani's refutation.
2
Understand the consequence of independent action
Baqillani argues that if the Son can perform a temporal act (the union) alone, then the Spirit and other hypostases could also perform other temporal acts alone, leading to multiple independent agents.
This would imply a plurality of gods, which Christians reject.
3
Examine the final absurdity
Baqillani then flips the relationship: if hypostases act independently, then the general substance could become a property of them, and they could become a substance encompassing it. This would make the general substance just another hypostasis.
Christians affirm that the substance is the source of the hypostases, not vice versa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: هو الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم، فيجب أن يكون الجوهر هو المتحد بالجسد والإنسان الكلي أو الجزئي على ما تختارونه؛ لأن المتحد عندكم هو من فعل الاتحاد دون من لم يفعله ويجب أيضاً أن يكون هو الإله المستحق للعبادة؛ لأنه هو الفعّال لها. وكذلك إن قالوا: الجوهر والأقانيم فعلوا الاتحاد قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون هو والثلاثة الأقانيم متحدين بالإنسان؛ ولا معنى لقولكم: إن الابن وحده هو المتحد دون الأب والروح ودون الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم وهذا نقض قولكم إن الاتحاد للابن فقط. وكذلك إن قالوا: إنما فعل الاتحاد الأقانيم الثلاثة دون الجوهر قيل لهم: فيجب أن يكون الروح أيضاً متحداً وأن لا يكون الابن وحده من خواص الجوهر متحداً. وإن قالوا: فاعل الاتحاد إنما هو الابن وحده ولإنفراده بفعل الاتحاد متحداً دون الروح، قيل لهم: فإذا جاز أن ينفرد الابن بفعل حادث هو الاتحاد دون الروح والأب ودون الجوهر العام، فلِمَ لا يجوز أن ينفرد الروح بفعل حادث وحوادث أُخر وأن ينفرد كل أقنوم من الأقانيم بعوالم وأفعال لا يفعلها الآخر وينفرد الجوهر الجامع بفعل غير فعلها؟ وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، جاز أن تتمانع وتختلف ويقال: إذا كانت الأقانيم تفعل كما أن الجوهر الجامع لها يفعل فلِمَ صار بأن يكون جامعاً لها وأن تكون خواص له أولى، أولى من أن يكون هو خاصاً لها وهي جامعة له فيكون أقنوماً من أقانيمها؟ فلا يجدون لذلك مدفعاً.

?

Baqillani's Critique of Exclusive Union of the Word
Baqillani questions how the Word could unite with the body without the Father and Spirit also uniting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical argument against the Christian claim that only the Son (Word) united with Christ's body, using the analogy of mixed wine and water.

Core Idea
If the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, His union must include them.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani challenges the Christian doctrine of the union (ittihad) by pointing out a logical inconsistency. If the Word (Son) is said to be inseparable from the Father and the Holy Spirit, how can He alone unite with the body of Christ? Baqillani uses a powerful analogy of wine and water mixed inseparably to expose this contradiction. As you read, consider how this argument defends the absolute oneness of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the challenging tone: 'So answer this if you are able.'
2
Identify the core logical question
Baqillani asks: How can the Son unite with the body without the Father and Spirit, given that they are inseparable? This is the central problem.
The argument depends on the claim of inseparability, not on physical notions.
3
Examine the wine-water analogy
Consider the analogy: If wine and water are completely mixed and inseparable, one cannot drink the wine without also drinking the water. Baqillani uses this to show that if the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then any action of the Son must involve them.
The analogy is about logical inseparability, not chemical mixing.
4
Understand the refutation of the anticipated objection
Baqillani anticipates a Christian response about the Word uniting with the universal human in the particular Jesus. He refutes it by insisting the question is about the impossibility of exclusive union given inseparability.
This shows Baqillani's thoroughness in argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في الاتحاد ويقال لهم: كيف اتحدت الكلمة التي هي الابن بجسد المسيح دون الأب والروح، مع قولكم بأنه غير مباين لهما ولا منفصل عنهما؟ وإن جاز ذلك، فما أنكرتم من أن يكون الماء الممازج للخمر المختلط به مشروباً دون الخمر أو الخمر مشروباً دون الماء وإن كانا غير منفصلين ولا متباينين؟ وإذا استحال هذا عندكم وجب أن يكون شارب الخمر الممتزج بالماء شارباً للخمر والماء إذا كانا غير منفصلين ولا متباينين فما أنكرتم من أن يجب إذا كان الابن متحداً، وهو غير منفصل من الروح والأب ولا مباين لهما، أن يكون الأب والروح متحدين به كما أن الابن متحد به؟ فإن قالوا: إن الكلمة إنما اتحدت بالإنسان الكلي في الجزئي الذي ولدته مريم عليهما السلام قيل لهم: فيجب أيضاً أن يكون الأب والروح متحدين بالكلي في الجزئي الذي ولدته مريم؛ لأننا لسنا نقصد بهذا السؤال الكلام في الإنسان الذي اتحدت به الكلمة، وهل هو جزئي أو كلي، أو اتحاد بالكلي في الجزئي الذي ولدته مريم؛ وإنما الكلام في كيف يمكن أن يكون الابن متحداً بما اتحد به كلي أو جزئي دون الأب والروح، وهو غير مباين لهما ولا منفصل عنهما؛ فأجيبوا عن هذا إن كنتم قادرين.
An issue concerning the union. And it is said to them: How did the Word, which is the Son, unite with the body of the Christ without the Father and the Spirit, given your statement that He is not separate from them nor distinct from them? And if that is permissible, then what prevents you from allowing that water mixed with wine, blended with it, could be drunk without the wine, or the wine drunk without the water, even though they are not separate nor distinct? And if this is impossible in your view, then it must be that the drinker of wine mixed with water is a drinker of both the wine and the water, since they are not separate nor distinct. So what prevents you from admitting that if the Son is united, and He is not separate from the Spirit and the Father nor distinct from them, then the Father and the Spirit must also be united with Him just as the Son is united with Him? If they say: The Word only united with the universal human being in the particular one whom Mary gave birth to—peace be upon them—it is said to them: Then it must also be that the Father and the Spirit are united with the universal in the particular whom Mary gave birth to; because we do not intend by this question to discuss the human being with whom the Word united, whether it is particular or universal, or the union of the universal in the particular whom Mary gave birth to; rather the discussion is about how it is possible for the Son to be united with that with which He united, whether universal or particular, without the Father and the Spirit, while He is not distinct from them nor separate from them. So answer this if you are able.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a separate objection-and-answer concerning the union (ittihad) of the Word (al-kalima) with the body of Christ. Baqillani challenges the Christian claim that only the Son united: since the Son is said to be inseparable from the Father and Spirit, any action of the Son must involve them. He uses an analogy: if wine and water are completely mixed and inseparable, one cannot drink the wine without drinking the water. Similarly, if the Son is united and inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then the Father and Spirit must also be united with what the Son is united with. He then anticipates a Christian response: that the Word united with the universal human essence in the particular individual born of Mary. Baqillani refutes this by noting that the question is not about the nature of the human (universal or particular) but about the logical necessity that if the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then the union cannot be exclusive to the Son. He demands an answer.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The wine-water analogy is about physical mixing and chemical properties.
Correction: The analogy is about logical inseparability: if two things are inseparable in existence, any action involving one necessarily involves the other.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Baqillani use to argue that if the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then they must also be united?
A) The sun and its rays.
B) Fire and heat.
C) Wine and water mixed inseparably.
D) Body and soul.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that if the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then any union of the Son must also involve them, preserving divine oneness.

Baqillani's Refutation of the Incarnation
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim of the Word's exclusive union with Christ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses logical analogy and dialectic to argue against the Christian doctrine of the exclusive union of the Son with Christ, and why the response about the universal man does not resolve the problem.

Core Idea
If the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, his exclusive union with Christ is impossible.

This passage presents a sharp dialectical exchange between Baqillani and Christian theologians. It begins with an objection to the Christian claim that the Word (the Son) united exclusively with Christ's body, while the Father and Spirit remained separate— despite being inseparable from the Son. Using the analogy of mixed wine and water, Baqillani exposes the logical inconsistency and then rebuts the Christian defense involving the 'universal man.' This lesson walks you through each step of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: a brief preamble, then a question, an analogy, a hypothetical Christian response, and a final rejoinder.
The passage uses formal dialectical language common in kalam.
2
Understand the initial objection
Identify the key question: How can the Son unite with Christ's body without the Father and Spirit, given that he is inseparable from them? This is the core challenge.
3
Analyze the wine-water analogy
Baqillani draws a parallel: if water and wine are mixed inseparably, you cannot drink one without the other. Similarly, if the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, his exclusive union with Christ is contradictory. Grasp why this analogy is powerful.
The analogy illustrates the principle that inseparable entities cannot have separate effects.
4
Examine the Christian response and Baqillani's rejoinder
The Christians respond that the Word united with the 'universal man' in the particular Jesus. Baqillani then argues that this still forces the Father and Spirit to be united with that universal man as well, since they are inseparable from the Son. See how this closes the loophole.
The terminology (kullī/partial, juz'ī) reflects philosophical concepts of universals and particulars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جامعة له فيكون أقنوماً من أقانيمها ؟ فلا يجدون لذلك مدفعاً

مسألة في الاتحاد

ويقال لهم : كيف اتحدت الكلمة التي هي الابن بجسد المسيح دون الأب والروح، مع قولكم بأنه غير مباين لهما ولا منفصل عنهما؟ وإن جاز ذلك، فما أنكرتم من أن يكون الماء الممازج للخمر المختلط به مشروباً دون الخمر أو الخمر مشروباً دون الماء وإن كانا غير منفصلين ولا متباينين؟ وإذا استحال هذا عندكم وجب أن يكون شارب الخمر الممتزج بالماء شارباً للخمر والماء إذا كانا غير منفصلين ولا متباينين فما أنكرتم من أن يجب إذا كان الابن متحداً، وهو غير منفصل من الروح والأب ولا مباين لهما، أن يكون الأب والروح متحدين به كما أن الابن متحد به؟

فإن قالوا : إن الكلمة إنما اتحدت بالإنسان الكلي في الجزئي الذي ولدته مريم عليهما السلام قيل لهم : فيجب أيضاً أن يكون الأب والروح متحدين بالكلي في الجزئي الذي ولدته مريم ؛ لأننا لسنا نقصد بهذا السؤال الكلام في الإنسان الذي اتحدت به الكلمة، وهل هو جزئي أو كلي، أو اتحاد بالكلي في الجزئي الذي ولدته مريم؛ وإنما الكلام في كيف يمكن أن يكون الابن متحداً بما اتحد به كلي أو جزئي دون الأب والروح، وهو غير مباين لهما ولا منفصل عنهما؛ فأجيبوا عن هذا إن كنتم قادرين.
It is comprehensive for him, so it becomes a hypostasis of its hypostases? They find no defense against that. A question concerning the union. And it is said to them: How did the Word, which is the Son, unite with the body of Christ without the Father and the Spirit, while you claim that He is not separate from them nor distinct from them? And if that is permissible, then what prevents you from [allowing] that the water mingled with wine mixed with it could be drunk without the wine, or the wine drunk without the water, while they are not separate nor distinct? And if this is impossible according to you, then it would be necessary that the drinker of wine mixed with water would be a drinker of wine and water if they are not separate nor distinct. So what prevents you from [affirming] that if the Son is united, and He is not separate from the Spirit and the Father nor distinct from them, then the Father and the Spirit must be united with Him just as the Son is united with [the body]? If they say: The Word only united with the universal man in the particular [individual] whom Mary gave birth to, peace be upon them, it is said to them: Then it must also be that the Father and the Spirit are united with the universal in the particular whom Mary gave birth to; because by this question we do not intend to discuss the man with whom the Word united, whether he is particular or universal, or the union of the universal in the particular whom Mary gave birth to; rather the discussion is about how it is possible that the Son is united with that with which He united, whether universal or particular, without the Father and the Spirit, while He is not distinct from them nor separate from them. So answer this if you are able.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument against the Christian doctrine of the incarnation. It begins with a previous statement that seems to conclude a prior point: the Christian claim that the Son is a hypostasis (qunum) of the Godhead leads to an absurdity for which they have no defense. Then a new question is posed: How can the Word (the Son) unite with Christ's body while the Father and Spirit remain separate, given that the Son is supposed to be inseparable from them? The author uses an analogy of mixed wine and water: if two substances are inseparably mixed, you cannot drink one without the other. Similarly, if the Son is united with Christ's body while being inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then the Father and Spirit must also be united with that body. The Christians respond by claiming that the Word united with the universal man (al-insān al-kullī) in the particular individual Jesus. The author then rejoins: if that is the case, then the Father and Spirit, being inseparable from the Son, must also be united with that universal man in Jesus. The core of the argument is that the exclusive incarnation of the Son alone is inconsistent with the trinitarian doctrine of inseparable persons. The author concludes by challenging them to answer this.

Correction: Baqillani shows that if the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, then even with the universal man distinction, the Father and Spirit must also be united with the universal in the particular Jesus.

Key Takeaway

The Dilemma of Union with the Universal Man
Baqillani examines the modality of the Word's union with the universal man.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Christian claim of the Word's union with the universal man is rationally impossible.

Core Idea
A universal cannot be confined to a particular without logical absurdity.

In this passage, Baqillani sharpens his critique of Christian theology by examining a specific claim: that the Word united not with the individual Jesus but with the universal man. He presents a razor-sharp dilemma that shows this claim leads either to indifference (no special connection to Jesus) or spatial absurdity (a universal contained in a particular). This argument relies on basic rational principles about universals and particulars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a conditional statement, then two branches.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the dilemma
Baqillani presents two possibilities: union in a place or not in a place. Identify each branch and the consequences drawn.
3
Understand the first branch (no place)
If the union is not in a place, then the Word has no special connection to Jesus' body. This leads to problems with the crucifixion narrative.
If no union, then the body is like any other body.
4
Understand the second branch (in a place)
If the union is in a particular place (the body of Jesus), then the universal man must be confined to that particular, which contradicts reason.
A part cannot contain the whole.
5
Conclusion
Both branches are impossible, so the original claim is false. This shows the strength of rational argument in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : إن كانت الكلمة اتحدت بالإنسان الكلي، فلا تخلو أن تكون اتحدت به في مكان أو لا في مكان، فإن كانت اتحدت به لا في مكان فليس بينها الجسد المولود المأخوذ من مريم إلا ما بينه وبين سائر أجسام الناس وسائر الأجساد، ولا مزية لمريم ولا للجسد المأخوذ منها إذا لم يكن للابن اتحاد به ولا بغيره، ويجب أن يكون القتل والصلب جاريين على الجسد فقط لا على الابن ولا على المسيح، لأن الجسد الذي لا اتحاد للابن به ليس بمسيح فكيف يكون المسيح مقتولاً مصلوباً؟ وإن كان اتحاد الابن بالكلي اتحاداً به في مكان ما الجسد المأخوذ من مريم أو غيره من الأجسام، فيجب أن يكون الكلي محصوراً في ذلك المكان الجزئي وأن يكون الجزئي حاوياً محيطاً بالكلي ومكاناً له وإن كان جزءاً منه؛ وهذا عكس ما في العقل وقلبه لأن ذلك لو جاز لجاز اشتمال العدد القليل على العدد الكثير وزيادته عليه، ولجاز أن يكون الصغير من الأجسام محيطاً بالعظيم وحاوياً له وإذا علمنا بأوائل العقول فساد ذلك علمنا أيضاً استحالة اتحاد الابن بالكلي إن كان ها هنا كلي في مكان صغير جزئي.
Then it is said to them: If the Word united with the universal man, it must either be that it united with Him in a place or not in a place. If it united with Him not in a place, then between it and the body born from Mary there is only what is between it and the rest of the bodies of people and the rest of bodies, and there is no merit for Mary nor for the body taken from her, since the Son has no union with it nor with any other. And it would be necessary that killing and crucifixion occur only on the body, not on the Son nor on the Messiah, because the body with which the Son has no union is not the Messiah; so how can the Messiah be killed and crucified? And if the union of the Son with the universal is a union with it in a certain place—the body taken from Mary or other bodies—then it would be necessary that the universal be confined to that particular place, and that the particular be encompassing, surrounding the universal, and a place for it, even though it is a part of it. This contradicts reason and common sense, because if that were permissible, it would be permissible for a small number to contain a large number and exceed it, and it would be permissible for a small body to surround a large body and contain it. And since we know by the first principles of reason the corruption of that, we also know the impossibility of the union of the Son with the universal, if there is here a universal in a small particular place.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a second proof against the Christians' claim that the Word united with the universal man in the particular Jesus. Baqillani presents a dilemma: either the union occurs in a place or not. If it is not in a place, then there is no special connection between the Word and Jesus' body; the body of Jesus is like any other body, and thus the crucifixion would not affect the Son or the Messiah. If the union is in a particular place (the body of Jesus), then that particular body would have to contain the universal man, which is absurd: a part containing the whole. This would violate basic logical principles (e.g., a small number cannot contain a larger one).  Thus, the union with the universal man is impossible. The argument relies on the notion that the universal cannot be spatially confined to a particular without logical contradiction.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The claim that the Word united with the universal man rather than the individual Jesus resolves the logical difficulties of the incarnation.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this claim leads to either indifference to Jesus' body or spatial absurdity, thus it is not a solution.

Checkpoint

B) There would be no special relationship between the Word and Jesus' body
C) The universal man would be confined to Jesus' body
D) The crucifixion would affect the Word

Key Takeaway
The union of a universal with a particular in a place is rationally impossible; Baqillani's dilemma shows that the Christian claim of the Word's union with the universal man cannot avoid absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani argues that a universal cannot be contained in a particular. Do you ever assume that God's mercy or guidance is 'contained' in your own community, denomination, or tradition, excluding others? How might this be a subtle form of the same logical error? What would it take for you to truly believe that God's mercy is universal and not confined to your group?
?
The passage shows that if the union were not in a place, then Mary and her body would have no special merit. Consider your own acts of worship: do you sometimes seek closeness to God in a vague, non-committal way, avoiding concrete actions and sacrifices? How can you make your faith more embodied and particular, like the specific body of Jesus was central to the Christian claim?
?
The dilemma forces a choice: either the union is meaningless or absurd. Reflect on a belief or commitment in your life that you hold vaguely to avoid its implications. Where have you been avoiding the 'particular place' of responsibility? Will you allow the first principles of your faith to expose the absurdity and lead you to clarity?

The Melkite Dilemma on Mary's Birth
Baqillani poses a logical dilemma to the Melkites about Mary's birth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma Baqillani presents to the Melkites regarding the inseparability of the Trinity and Mary's giving birth to the Son alone.

Core Idea
If the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit, Mary cannot bear Him alone.

In this short but powerful question, Imam Baqillani turns the Trinity doctrine against itself. He asks the Melkites a simple yet devastating question: if the Son is one with the Father and Spirit, how could Mary give birth to the Son without them? The passage, though incomplete, sets up a classic theological challenge based on logical consistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the direct, interrogative style Baqillani uses to challenge the Melkites.
2
Identify the key terms
Identify the key terms: the Son, Father, Holy Spirit, and the 'substance comprising the hypostases'. Understand that these are central to the Trinity doctrine.
The term 'جوهر جامع للأقانيم' refers to the one divine substance shared by the three persons.
3
Understand the logical structure
The passage presents a premise (the Son is inseparable from the Father and Spirit) and a consequence (the one united with the body should be all three, not just the Son). This leads to a contradiction with the Melkite claim that Mary gave birth to the Son alone.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Consider the cut-off
The text ends mid-sentence. Speculate what Baqillani might have concluded. The likely continuation is that the Melkites cannot consistently hold both beliefs.
The source is incomplete, but the argument's direction is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة على الملكية

يقال لهم : خبرونا كيف ولدت مريم الابن دون الأب وروح القدس وهو غير مباين لهما ولا منفصل عنهما فيكون المتحد بالجسد حملاً في بطن مريم، والأب والروح والجوهر الجامع للأقانيم لا في بطن مريم، وهما مع
A question against the Melkites. It is said to them: Inform us, how did Mary give birth to the Son without the Father and the Holy Spirit, while He is not distinct from them nor separate from them, so that the one united with the body becomes a pregnancy in Mary's womb, while the Father, the Spirit, and the substance comprising the hypostases are not in Mary's womb, and they are with?
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a brief question posed to the Melkites (a Christian sect). It challenges the doctrine of the Trinity by focusing on the birth of Jesus. If the Son is inseparable from the Father and the Holy Spirit, how could Mary give birth to the Son alone? If the Son is united with the body in her womb, then the Father and Spirit, being inseparable, should also be present. The text cuts off mid-sentence, likely continuing with a further consequence. The core idea is that the Christian claim of Mary as mother of the Son alone contradicts the inseparability of the divine persons.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Baqillani is not disputing the birth event itself; he is using it to expose an internal inconsistency in Trinitarian doctrine. The question is purely logical: if the persons are inseparable, the birth of the Son alone is impossible.

Baqillani's Dilemma Against Union with Universal Man
Baqillani refutes the union of the Word with universal man by a disjunctive argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's disjunctive argument against the Christian doctrine of the union of the Word with universal man.

Core Idea
A universal cannot be confined to a particular place — that would defy reason.

Baqillani engages with a Christian theological claim using pure rational argumentation. He presents a dilemma: either the union is spatial or non-spatial. Both options lead to conclusions that contradict Christian doctrines or basic reason. This passage shows how kalam uses logical disjunction to refute a theological position without relying on scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of Baqillani's argument. Notice the structure: a conditional statement followed by two alternatives.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The argument presents a disjunction: either the union is in a place or not in a place. These are the two possibilities. Identify the Arabic phrases that mark this split.
Look for 'إن كانت اتحدت به في مكان أو لا في مكان'.
3
Analyze the non-spatial horn
If the union is not in a place, then the body of Mary has no special connection to the Word. Consequently, killing and crucifixion apply only to the body, not to Christ. How does this contradict Christian claims?
This undermines the doctrine of the crucifixion of Christ.
4
Analyze the spatial horn
If the union is in a place (Mary's body), then the universal would be confined to that particular. This is absurd because a particular cannot contain a universal. Baqillani uses analogies of number and size to illustrate.
Consider the principle: a part cannot encompass the whole.
5
Understand the conclusion
Since both alternatives lead to impossibility, the original claim (union with universal man) is false. Baqillani grounds this in 'first principles of reason'.
The argument does not deny incarnation entirely but refutes this specific formulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: إن كانت الكلمة اتحدت بالإنسان الكلي، فلا يخلو أن تكون اتحدت به في مكان أو لا في مكان، فإن كانت اتحدت به لا في مكان فليس بينها وبين الجسد المولود المأخوذ من مريم إلا ما بينها وبين سائر أجسام الناس وسائر الأجساد، ولا مزية لمريم ولا للجسد المأخوذ منها إذا لم يكن للابن اتحاد به ولا بغيره، ويجب أن يكون القتل والصلب جاريين على الجسد فقط لا على الابن ولا على المسيح، لأن الجسد الذي لا اتحاد للابن به ليس بمسيح فكيف يكون المسيح مقتولاً مصلوباً؟ وإن كان اتحاد الابن بالكلي اتحاداً به في مكان ما الجسد المأخوذ من مريم أو غيره من الأجسام، فيجب أن يكون الكلي محصوراً في ذلك المكان الجزئي وأن يكون الجزئي حاوياً محيطاً بالكلي ومكاناً له وإن كان جزءاً منه؛ وهذا عكس ما في العقل وقلبه لأن ذلك لو جاز لجاز اشتمال العدد القليل على العدد الكثير وزيادته عليه، ولجاز أن يكون الصغير من الأجسام محيطاً بالعظيم وحاوياً له وإذا علمنا بأوائل العقول فساد ذلك علمنا أيضاً استحالة اتحاد الابن بالكلي إن كان ها هنا كلي في مكان صغير جزئي.
Then it is said to them: If the Word is united with universal man, then it is inevitable that it is united with him either in a place or not in a place. If it is united with him not in a place, then there is no distinction between it and the body born taken from Mary except what distinguishes it from all other bodies of people and all other bodies, and there is no special merit for Mary nor for the body taken from her if the Son has no union with it nor with anything else. And it would necessarily follow that the killing and crucifixion apply only to the body, not to the Son nor to the Christ, because the body with which the Son has no union is not Christ, so how can Christ be killed and crucified? And if the union of the Son with the universal is a union with it in some place, [namely] the body taken from Mary or other bodies, then it would be necessary that the universal be confined to that particular place and that the particular encompass the universal, surround it, and be a place for it even though it is a part of it; and this is the reverse of what reason and heart [know], because if that were permissible, then the inclusion of a small number containing a large number and exceeding it would be permissible, and it would be permissible for a small body to encompass a large one and contain it. And since we know by the first principles of reason the corruption of that, we also know the impossibility of the union of the Son with the universal, if there is a universal in a small particular place.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the incarnation, specifically the claim that the Word (the second person of the Trinity) is united with universal human nature. The author presents a disjunctive argument: either the union occurs in a place or not. If it is not in a place, then the body born of Mary has no special connection to the Word, so the crucifixion would not affect Christ. If the union is in a place (i.e., the body of Mary), then the universal would be confined to a particular, which is absurd because a particular cannot encompass a universal. The argument uses basic rational principles to show impossibility.

Correction: He only refutes a specific claim about union with a universal, not necessarily all incarnational models.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's argument, if the union of the Word with universal man is not in a place, what follows?
A) The body of Mary is specially honored.
B) The crucifixion applies only to the body, not to Christ.

Refuting Melkite Christology with Universal and Particular Categories
Baqillani uses the universal-particular distinction to refute Melkite Christology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the philosophical categories of universal and particular to expose a contradiction in Melkite Christology.

Core Idea
Universal and particular categories collapse Melkite claims into absurdity.

Baqillani presents a clever argument against the Melkite Christian sect by asking about Mary: is she a universal human or a particular human? This simple question forces a dilemma that demolishes their doctrine of the Son's union with universal humanity. The argument uses basic philosophical distinctions to show that their position leads to the absurdity of a universal being the son of a particular.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
Baqillani asks whether Mary is a universal human (kullī) or a particular human (juz'ī), setting up a two-horned argument.
2
First horn: Mary is universal
If they say Mary is universal, then every human would be universal, eliminating particularity and destroying their doctrine.
This horn reduces Melkite position to absurdity by denying particular humans.
3
Second horn: Mary is particular
If they say Mary is particular, then the human she bore (Jesus) must be universal according to their claim that the Son united with universal humanity.
4
Consequence of the second horn
This leads to the absurdity that a universal human (Jesus) is the son of a particular human (Mary), and the doctrine collapses into Nestorianism or Jacobitism.
5
Observe the incomplete ending
The text ends mid-sentence with 'Wa kayfa yakūn' (And how can...), suggesting the reductio continues, possibly showing that Mary's existence depends on universal humanity.
The page break may cut the argument short.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سألة أخرى على الملكية

يقال لهم: خبرونا عن مريم: أهي إنسان كلي أم إنسان جزئي؟ فإن قالوا: إنها كلي تجاهلوا، وقيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن يكون كل ذكر وأنثى من الناس إنساناً كلياً؟ فإن قالوا هو كذلك تركوا قولهم، وقيل لهم: فأي الإنسان الجزئي، وكل جزئي تشيرون إليه على قولكم هذا فهو كلي؟ فلا يجدون إلى إثبات الجزئي سبيلا وفي هذا هدم مذهبهم.

وإن قالوا مريم عليها السلام إنسان جزئي، قيل لهم: فالإنسان الذي ولدته أليس هو الذي اتحد الابن بولادته؟ وإذا قالوا: نعم، قيل لهم: فخبرونا عن الإنسان الذي ولدته مريم: أكلي هو أم جزئي؟ فإن قالوا جزئي تركوا قولهم بأن الابن متحد بالإنسان الكلي الذي أراد خلاصه؛ وصاروا إلى قول النسطورية واليعاقبة.

وإن قالوا: الإنسان المأخوذ من مريم هو ابن مريم؟ فإذا قالوا: أجل قيل لهم فهو كلي وأمه التي هي مريم إنسان جزئي؛ فيجب على قولكم أن يكون الإنسان الكلي ابن الإنسان الجزئي وهذا طريف جداً؛ لأننا لو فرضنا عندهم عدم مريم لم يعدم الإنسان الكلي، ولو فرضنا عدم الإنسان الكلي لم تكن مريم ولا غيرها من جزئيات الإنسان. وكيف يكون
Another question concerning the Melkites.

It is said to them: Inform us about Mary: is she a universal human or a particular human? If they say she is universal, they are being ignorant, and it is said to them: What prevents you from saying that every male and female human is a universal human? If they say that is the case, they abandon their position, and it is said to them: Which human is the particular human, and every particular you point to according to this statement of yours is universal? So they cannot find a way to establish the particular, and in this is the destruction of their doctrine.

And if they say Mary, peace be upon her, is a particular human, it is said to them: The human whom she gave birth to, is it not he with whom the Son united through his birth? And if they say yes, it is said to them: Inform us about the human whom Mary gave birth to: is it universal or particular? If they say particular, they abandon their statement that the Son is united with the universal human whom he intended to save; and they come to the position of the Nestorians and Jacobites.

And if they say: The human taken from Mary is the son of Mary? If they say yes, it is said to them: Then he is universal and his mother who is Mary is a particular human; so according to your statement it would be necessary that the universal human be the son of the particular human, and this is very strange. Because if we assume, according to them, the non-existence of Mary, the universal human would not be non-existent, and if we assume the non-existence of the universal human, Mary nor any other particular humans would not exist. And how can...
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument against the Melkite Christian sect. The author uses the philosophical categories of universal (kullī) and particular (juz'ī) to force a contradiction. He first asks about Mary: if they say she is universal, then all humans would be universal, eliminating the particular. If they say she is particular, then the human she bore (Jesus) must be universal according to their doctrine, leading to the absurdity that a universal is the son of a particular. The argument concludes that their position collapses into Nestorianism or Jacobitism, which they rejected. The text ends mid-argument with 'Wa kayfa yakūn' (And how can...), likely continuing the reductio.
