The Mary Dilemma: Refuting Incarnation via Universals and Particulars
Dialectical dilemma on Mary's universality or particularity refuting Melkite incarnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a logical dilemma about universality and particularity refutes the Melkite Christian claim of incarnation.

Core Idea
A universal cannot be the son of a particular, exposing the incarnation as impossible.

Imam Baqillani presents a sharp logical dilemma to the Melkites (Byzantine Christians). He asks: Is Mary a universal human or a particular human? Whichever they answer leads to contradictions or heretical positions they reject. This lesson walks through that dialectic and shows why incarnation as they conceive it is rationally untenable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Baqillani sets up the dilemma with two possible answers.
The argument uses the Aristotelian concepts of universal (kulli) and particular (juz'i).
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
Find where Baqillani considers Mary as universal, then as particular. See what absurdity follows each.
The first horn (Mary=universal) leads to everything being universal. The second horn (Mary=particular) leads to further sub-dilemmas about Jesus.
3
Trace the sub-branches of the particular horn
If Mary is particular, then Jesus must be either particular or universal. Both options cause problems for the Melkite position.
If Jesus is particular, they become Nestorians or Jacobites. If Jesus is universal, the absurdity of a universal son of a particular mother arises.
4
Analyse the ultimate absurdity
Baqillani shows that if Jesus is universal and Mary particular, then the universal human would be independent of Mary's existence, yet she is his mother. That is contradictory.
This final part uses the logical relationship between universals and particulars to seal the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سألة أخرى على الملكية
يقال لهم : خبرونا عن مريم : أهي إنسان كلي أم إنسان جزئي؟ فإن قالوا : إنها كلي تجاهلوا ، وقيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون كل ذكر وأنثى من الناس إنساناً كلياً؟ فإن قالوا هو كذلك تركوا قولهم ، وقيل لهم : فأي الإنسان الجزئي ، وكل جزئي تشيرون إليه على قولكم هذا فهو كلي؟ فلا يجدون إلى إثبات الجزئي سبيلا وفي هذا هدم مذهبهم .
وإن قالوا مريم عليها السلام إنسان جزئي، قيل لهم : فالإنسان الذي ولدته أليس هو الذي اتحد الابن بولادته؟ وإذا قالوا: نعم، قيل لهم : فخبرونا عن الإنسان الذي ولدته مريم : أكلي هو أم جزئي ؟ فإن قالوا جزئي تركوا قولهم بأن الابن متحد بالإنسان الكلي الذي أراد خلاصه ؛ وصاروا إلى قول النسطورية واليعاقبة .
وإن قالوا : الإنسان المأخوذ من مريم هو ابن مريم؟ فإذا قالوا : أجل قيل لهم فهو كلي وأمه التي هي مريم إنسان جزئي ؛ فيجب على قولكم أن يكون الإنسان الكلي ابن الإنسان الجزئي وهذا طريف جداً؛ لأننا لو فرضنا عندهم عدم مريم لم يعدم الإنسان الكلي، ولو فرضنا عدم الإنسان الكلي لم تكن مريم ولا غيرها من جزئيات الإنسان. وكيف يكون الكلي ابن ما لا يجب أن يعدم بعدمه ويرتفع بارتفاعه ويكون الجزئي حاويا للكلي؟
Another question against the Melkites. It is said to them: Inform us about Mary: Is she a universal human or a particular human? If they say: She is universal, they feign ignorance, and it is said to them: What prevents you from saying that every male and female of people is a universal human? If they say: So, they abandon their statement, and it is said to them: Which is the particular human, and every particular you indicate according to this statement of yours is universal? So they find no way to affirm the particular, and in this is the demolition of their doctrine. And if they say: Mary, peace be upon her, is a particular human, it is said to them: The human she gave birth to, is it not the one with whom the Son united through his birth? And if they say: Yes, it is said to them: Inform us about the human whom Mary gave birth to: Is it universal or particular? If they say: Particular, they abandon their statement that the Son is united with the universal human whom He intended to save; and they turn to the statement of the Nestorians and Jacobites. And if they say: The human taken from Mary is the son of Mary? If they say: Indeed, it is said to them: Then he is universal and his mother Mary is a particular human; so it is necessary according to your statement that the universal human is the son of the particular human, and this is very strange; because if we suppose in their view the non-existence of Mary, the universal human would not cease to exist, and if we suppose the non-existence of the universal human, there would be no Mary nor any other particular humans. And how can the universal be the son of that which does not necessarily cease to exist with its non-existence and is removed by its removal, and the particular encompasses the universal?
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument against the Melkite Christian doctrine of the incarnation. The author (Imam Baqillani) poses a dilemma about Mary's ontological status: is she a universal (kulli) human or a particular (juz'i) human? He first considers the case where they claim she is universal. That would entail that every human being is universal, which destroys their distinction between universal and particular. If they instead say she is particular, then the human born from her (Jesus) must be either universal or particular. If they say he is particular, they abandon their claim that the Son united with a universal human for salvation, falling into the Nestorian or Jacobite position. If they say he is universal, then a universal human is the son of a particular human (Mary). This leads to absurd consequences: eliminating Mary does not eliminate the universal human, and eliminating the universal human would eliminate all particulars, including Mary. The argument shows the logical impossibility of the incarnation as the Melkites conceive it.

جزئي

ابن مريم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Melkite incarnation is about a divine person taking a human body, but the argument shows they claimed union with a universal humanity, not a particular body.
Correction: The Melkites held that the Son united with a universal human nature, not with a particular individual. Baqillani's dilemma forces them to specify whether Mary herself is universal or particular, exposing inconsistency.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's argument, if the Melkites say Mary is a particular human and Jesus is universal, what is the resulting absurdity?
A) Jesus would be a particular human like Mary.
B) The universal human would be the son of a particular human, which is contradictory.
C) Mary would cease to exist when the universal human disappears.
D) The Nestorian position would be refuted.

Key Takeaway
The incarnation doctrine is defeated by a logical dilemma: either Christ is not united with universal humanity, or Mary becomes the mother of a universal being—both impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This arguments shows that a single logical flaw can collapse an entire theological system. Are there any beliefs you currently hold that you have not examined with this kind of rigorous logic? Would you be willing to scrutinize them even if it makes you uncomfortable?
?
The Melkites were unable to resolve the dilemma without contradicting themselves. How do you respond when your own reasoning leads to a contradiction? Do you change your position or rationalize the contradiction away?
?
Baqillani's argument defends God's transcendence by denying any incarnation. Does your theology preserve a clear distinction between Creator and creation, or have you unintentionally blurred that line? Ask yourself honestly and commit to clarity.

Universal Substance Cannot Be Born or Located
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim by showing the impossibility of a universal being born or located.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that a universal substance cannot undergo birth or spatial confinement, and how this refutes the Christian claim about Christ.

Core Idea
A universal cannot be born or be in a place; only particulars have these properties.

Imam Baqillani addresses a Christian theological claim that Christ is a 'universal substance' (al-jawhar al-kulli) yet was born of Mary. In this passage, he exposes the logical contradiction in this claim by showing that birth and spatial location are properties of particular things, not universals. Through a powerful reductio ad absurdum, he demonstrates that accepting the Christian premise leads to absurd genealogical inversions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Get a sense of Baqillani's tone and flow.
Notice the repeated rhetorical questions.
2
Identify the Christian premise and Baqillani's premise
Identify what Christians claim (universal substance born of Mary) and Baqillani's counter-premise (a universal cannot be born or located).
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Trace how Baqillani applies the Christian logic to absurd cases like Mary being daughter of Jesus.
This is a key refutation method.
4
Reflect on the implication for divine transcendence
Consider why this argument matters for Islamic theology: it safeguards God and the divine attributes from being subject to physical limitations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم أنتم تقولون : إن الجوهر الكلي وكل ما تقولون إنه كلي لا تصح ولادته ولا أن يحويه مكان دون مكان ؛ والمولود من مريم في بطنها، وكان مكانه منها حاوياً له، فكيف يكون كلياً؟ فإن جاز أن يكون الكليّ ابن الجزئي ، فلِمَ لا يجوز أن تكون مريم ابنة عيسى المولود منها، وأن يكون آدم ونوح ابني مريم التي هي ابنة لهما؟ هذا تجاهل عظيم لا يبلغه صاحب تحصيل .
And it is said to them: You claim that the universal substance and everything you say is universal, its birth is not valid, nor can a particular place contain it; but the one born from Mary was in her womb, and her place contained him, so how can he be universal? And if it is permissible for the universal to be the son of the particular, then why is it not permissible for Mary to be the daughter of Jesus born from her, and for Adam and Noah to be sons of Mary who is their daughter? This is great ignorance that no possessor of sound intellect can attain.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a direct refutation of the Christian claim that Christ is a universal substance (al-jawhar al-kulli) while being born of Mary. Baqillani states the premise that a universal cannot undergo birth (wilada) nor be confined to a specific place. Since Jesus was born in Mary's womb and his place was her body, he cannot be universal. The author then reduces the Christian position to absurdity by applying their logic to genealogical relations: if a universal can be the son of a particular, then Mary could be the daughter of her own son Jesus, and Adam and Noah could be sons of Mary—a manifest absurdity. The passage emphasizes that such a claim is the height of ignorance, unattainable by any sound intellect.

Key Terms
جوهر كلي
ولادة
مكان
ابن الجزئي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A universal substance can be born and located in a particular place.
Correction: Baqillani argues that universals cannot undergo birth or be contained in a specific location; these are properties of particulars.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's main objection to the claim that Christ is a universal substance born of Mary?
A) A universal cannot be born or confined to a place.
B) Mary was not a particular human.
C) Jesus was not truly born.
D) The universal substance is imaginary.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument that a universal cannot be born or located refutes the Christian claim that Christ is a universal substance born of Mary, preserving divine transcendence.

?

When someone challenges a deeply held religious belief of yours with a logical argument, do you become defensive or do you engage with the reasoning? Remember a time when you changed your mind because of sound evidence. What would it cost you to do so again?

The Crucifixion Dilemma: God's Death or Broken Union
Baqillani's logical dilemma on the union of the Son during crucifixion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a logical dilemma to refute the Christian doctrine of the incarnation by showing that both options lead to an impossibility.

Core Idea
The crucifixion dilemma: either God died or the union failed—both impossible.

Baqillani presents a sharp logical dilemma against Christians who believe in the incarnation. He asks a simple yes-or-no question about the union of the divine Son with the human body at the moment of crucifixion. Whichever way they answer, their doctrine collapses. This passage shows how kalam arguments often dismantle opposing views by exposing internal contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
Baqillani poses a question: was the Son still united to the body during crucifixion? Yes or no? Read the passage to see how he sets up the two options.
The question forces Christians to choose between two problematic answers.
2
Follow the first horn
If they say yes, then Christ died as both divine and human. This means the Son of God died, which is impossible because God cannot be dead or deficient.
This horn leads to: if the Son died, then the Father and Spirit could also die, which Christians reject.
3
Follow the second horn
If they say no, then the union ended at the crucifixion. This contradicts the Christian belief in a permanent incarnation.
Either way, the Christian position is refuted. The argument is a classic example of sabr wa-taqsim (dividing and eliminating).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة على جميعهم
ويقال لهم : خبرونا عن اتحاد الابن بالجسد : أكان باقياً موجوداً في حال وقوع القتل والصلب به أم لا؟ فإن قالوا : كان باقياً موجوداً قيل لهم : فالذي مات مسيح من طبيعتين : لاهوت وهو الابنُ ، وناسوت وهو الجسد ؛ فيجب أن يكون ابنُ الله القديم قد مات كما قتل وصلب؛ لأن جواز القتل والصلب عليه كجواز الموت وإذا صار الابن عند القتل ميتاً، لم يجز أن يكون في تلك الحال إلهاً لأن الإله لا يكون ميتاً ولا ناقصاً ولا ممن يجوز عليه الموت ولو جاز ذلك عليه لجاز موت الأب والروح وهذا ترك قولهم .
وإن قالوا : الاتحاد بَطَلَ عند القتل والصلب ، قيل لهم : فيجب انتقاض الاتحاد عند القتل والصلب ؛ وهذا ترك قولهم . ويجب أيضاً ألا يكون ...
A question against all of them. And it is said to them: Inform us about the union of the Son with the body: Was He remaining existing at the time of the killing and crucifixion of him or not? If they say: He was remaining existing, it is said to them: Then the one who died is Christ from two natures: Divinity (Lahut) which is the Son, and humanity (Nasut) which is the body; so it is necessary that the ancient Son of God died just as He was killed and crucified; because the permissibility of killing and crucifixion for Him is like the permissibility of death. And if the Son at the time of death became dead, it is not permissible for Him in that state to be God, because God cannot be dead nor deficient nor among those for whom death is permissible. And if that were permissible for Him, then the death of the Father and the Spirit would be permissible, and this is an abandonment of their statement. And if they say: The union was cancelled at the time of killing and crucifixion, it is said to them: Then the union must be broken at the time of killing and crucifixion; and this is an abandonment of their statement. And it is also necessary that...
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a dilemma against all Christian sects that affirm the incarnation. Baqillani asks about the union (ittihad) between the Son (al-ibn) and the body during the crucifixion. If they say the Son remained present and existing, then Christ died from two natures: divine (lahut) and human (nasut). This would mean that God (the ancient Son) died, which is impossible because God is not subject to death or deficiency. If God could die, then the Father and the Holy Spirit could also die, which Christians would reject. If they instead say the union ceased at the crucifixion, then the union is broken, which contradicts their doctrine of a permanent incarnation. The argument concludes that either option is a refutation of their belief. The text is incomplete but clearly shows the logical impasse.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Christians argue that the divine nature temporarily 'emptied itself' to suffer, so God did not actually die.
Correction: Baqillani insists that if the Son remained united, then the divine nature was involved in death, which is impossible for God regardless of 'emptying.'

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's argument, if the Son remained united during the crucifixion, what follows?
A) The Son did not truly die.
B) God died, which is impossible.
C) The union was cancelled.
D) The Father died instead.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's dilemma shows that the Christian claim of incarnation is logically untenable because it either implies God died or the union was temporary, both contradicting core Christian beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This argument shows that for the Incarnation to be true, either God died or the union was temporary. Both are impossible. Are there any beliefs you hold about God that, when pressed, lead to equally impossible alternatives? If so, are you willing to abandon them?

Refuting the Universal Hypostatic Union with Mary and Jesus
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim by logical absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the Christian claim that the universal hypostatic union (Christ) was born from Mary, and the absurd consequences he derives.

Core Idea
A universal cannot be contained in a particular, or else absurdities follow.

This passage presents Baqillani's critique of the Christian doctrine of the hypostatic union, specifically the claim that Christ as a universal substance was born from Mary. He begins by defining the universal and then draws out an absurd logical consequence. Let's examine his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of the universal
Read the opening line where Baqillani defines the universal: that which does not cease to exist when the particular ceases and is not confined by place. This definition is crucial for the refutation.
Note the contrast: the universal is not dependent on any particular instance.
2
Identify the Christian claim
The Christians claim that the universal substance (the divine nature) was born from Mary and contained in her womb. Baqillani states this claim to highlight the contradiction.
3
Follow the logical reduction to absurdity
Baqillani argues that if the universal can be born from a particular, then there is no logical barrier to Mary being the daughter of Jesus, or Adam and Noah being sons of Mary—an absurd reversal of lineage.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: the claim leads to impossible consequences.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that such a claim is sheer ignorance, beyond the reach of anyone with understanding. Consider why this refutation is effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلي ابن ما لا يجب أن يُعدَم بعدمه ويرتفع بارتفاعه ويكون الجزئي حاوياً (١) للكلي؟ . ويقال لهم أنتم تقولون (۲) : إن الجوهر الكلي (۳) وكل ما تقولون إنه كلي لا تصح ولادته ولا أن (٤) يحويه مكان دون مكان ؛ والمولود من مـريـم في بطنها، وكان مكانه منها (ه) حاوياً له، فكيف يكون كلياً؟ فإن(٦) جاز أن يكون الكليّ ابن الجزئي ، فلِمَ لا يجوز أن تكون مريم ابنة عيسى المولود منها، وأن يكون آدم ونوح ابني مريم التي هي ابنة لهما؟ هذا (۷) تجاهل عظيم لا يبلغه صاحب تحصيل .
The universal is that which does not necessarily cease to exist when the particular ceases and is removed when the particular is removed, and the particular encompasses (١) the universal? And it is said to them: You claim (۲) that the universal substance (۳) and everything you claim is universal cannot be born nor can any place other than some place contain it; yet the one born from Mary in her womb, and her place from her (ه) encompassed him, so how can he be universal? If (٦) it is permissible for the universal to be the son of the particular, then why is it not permissible for Mary to be the daughter of Jesus born from her, and for Adam and Noah to be sons of Mary who is a daughter to them? This (۷) is great ignorance that no possessor of understanding attains.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that Christ, as a universal (kulli) hypostatic union, was born from Mary. The author begins by defining the universal: it is that which does not depend on the particular for its existence and is not contained by a particular place. Then he presents the Christian claim that the universal substance (or the universal Christ) was born from Mary and contained in her womb. He argues that if the universal can be born from a particular, then there is no logical barrier to Mary being the daughter of Jesus, or Adam and Noah being sons of Mary—an absurdity. The passage concludes that this claim is sheer ignorance.

Key Terms
كلي (kulli)
جزئي (juz'i)
جوهر كلي (al-jawhar al-kulli)
اتحاد (ittihad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The universal (Christ) can be born from a particular substance (Mary) and be physically contained in her womb.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the universal, by definition, cannot be confined by a particular place or be born from a particular; otherwise absurd consequences like reverse parentage follow.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does Baqillani derive from the Christian claim that the universal Christ was born from Mary?
A) That Christ must be mortal
B) That Mary could be the daughter of Jesus, and Adam and Noah could be sons of Mary
C) That the universal cannot exist
D) That Jesus was not truly human

Key Takeaway
The claim that the universal hypostatic union became incarnate in a particular person leads to logical absurdities, undermining the Christian doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever imagine Allah as being present in a physical sense, like in a particular place or inside your heart? How does the definition of the universal in this passage challenge that idea, and what specific steps will you take to purify your understanding of Allah's transcendence?
?
When you hear the Christian claim about Jesus, does your heart feel any emotional pull or sympathy? This passage shows its logical absurdity. Are you convinced by reason alone, or do you need to strengthen your knowledge of tawhid to guard against such ideas? What will you do this week to reinforce your conviction?
?
The argument forces you to confront absurd consequences. In your own life, are there any beliefs or practices that, if followed to their logical conclusion, would lead to absurdity? Are you willing to examine them and abandon them if needed? What is one such belief you will investigate today?

The Dilemma of the Crucifixion
Baqillani presents a dilemma on the union during crucifixion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a logical dilemma to refute the Christian claim that the Messiah (Son of God) was crucified.

Core Idea
Either the union remained and God died, or it ended and Jesus was not the Messiah.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents a powerful logical dilemma against the Christian doctrine of the hypostatic union, focusing on the crucifixion event. He forces the opponent to choose between two impossible options, each of which destroys their own position. This lesson unpacks the argument step by step, showing how Islamic kalam defends divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Baqillani sets up two alternative answers to the same question about the union during crucifixion.
The question is: was the union of the Son with the body still present at the time of killing and crucifixion?
2
Understand the first horn
If the union remained, then the one who died is the Messiah from two natures. This would mean the eternal Son died, which is impossible because God cannot die or be deficient.
Baqillani argues that this also implies the Father and Spirit could die, contradicting Christian doctrine.
3
Understand the second horn
If the union ceased, then the dissolution of the union implies the crucified was not the Messiah but a mere human. This also contradicts Christian claims.
Either way, the crucifixion narrative fails.
4
Reflect on the argument's structure
Notice how Baqillani uses a dilemma (two mutually exclusive options) to refute the opponent. This is a classic kalam method.
The conclusion is that the Christian position is logically incoherent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة على جميعهم (۸) ويقال لهم (۹) : خبرونا عن اتحاد الابن بالجسد : أكان (١٠) باقياً موجوداً (۱۲) (۱۳) في حال وقوع القتل والصلب به أم لا؟ فإن قالوا : كان باقياً موجوداً (۱۱) قيل لهم : فالذي مات مسيح من طبيعتين : لاهوت وهو (١٣) الابنُ ، وناسوت وهو الجسد ؛ فيجب أن يكون ابنُ الله القديم قد مات كما قتل وصلب؛ لأن جواز القتل والصلب عليه كجواز الموت وإذا صار الابن عند القتل ميتاً، لم يجز أن يكون في تلك (١٤) الحال إلهاً لأن الإله لا يكون ميتاً ولا ناقصاً ولا ممن يجوز عليه الموت ولو جاز ذلك عليه (۱۹) لجاز موت الأب والروح وهذا ترك قولهم . وإن قالوا : الاتحاد (۱۱) بَطَلَ عند القتل والصلب ، قيل لهم ) (۱۷) : فيجب انتقاض الاتحاد عند القتل والصلب ؛ وهذا ترك قولهم . ويجب أيضاً ألا يكون المقتول مسيحاً ؛ لأن الجسد عند انتقاض الاتحاد ومفارقة المتحدِ به ليس مسيحاً وإنما يكون الجسد وما اتحد به مسيحاً مع ثبوت الاتحاد ووجوده فإذا بطل كان المقتول المصلوب الواقع عليه الموت (۲) إنساناً ولا معنى لقولكم (۳) إن المسيح قتل وصلب .
A question against all of them (۸). And it is said to them (۹): Inform us concerning the union of the Son with the body: was it (١٠) remaining existing (۱۲)(۱۳) at the time of the killing and crucifixion upon him or not? If they say: He was remaining existing (۱۱), it is said to them: The one who died is the Messiah from two natures: divinity (lahut) which is (١٣) the Son, and humanity (nasut) which is the body; so it must be that the eternal Son of God died just as he was killed and crucified; because the permissibility of killing and crucifixion upon him is like the permissibility of death. And if the Son at the time of killing became dead, it is not permissible for him to be in that (١٤) state a god, because God is not dead, nor deficient, nor among those upon whom death is permissible. And if that were permissible upon him (۱۹), then the death of the Father and the Spirit would be permissible, and this abandons their statement. And if they say: The union (۱۱) ceased at the time of killing and crucifixion, it is said to them ) (۱۷): Then the dissolution of the union at killing and crucifixion is necessary; and this abandons their statement. And also, it is necessary that the killed one is not the Messiah; because the body upon the dissolution of the union and the separation of the united with it is not the Messiah, rather the body and that which united with it are the Messiah with the establishment and existence of the union. So if it ceases, the killed and crucified one upon whom death occurred (۲) is a human, and there is no meaning to your statement (۳) that the Messiah was killed and crucified.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a dilemma argument against the Christian doctrine of the hypostatic union, focusing on the crucifixion. Baqillani asks whether the union of the Son with the body persisted during the killing and crucifixion. He then examines both possible answers. First, if the union remained, then the one who died is the Messiah composed of two natures—divine and human—so the eternal Son necessarily died. But God cannot die, be deficient, or suffer death; if this were possible, then the Father and Spirit could also die, which contradicts Christian doctrine. Second, if the union ceased at the crucifixion, then the dissolution of the union is required, and the one killed was not the Messiah but merely a human. In either case, the Christian claim that the Messiah was killed and crucified is invalid.

Key Terms
اتحاد (ittihad)
لابوت (lahut)
ناسوت (nasut)
قتل (qatl)
صلب (salb)
مسيح (masih)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the union allows God to suffer death without contradiction.
Correction: If the union persisted, then God died, which is impossible. If it ceased, then the crucified was not God. Either way, the crucifixion cannot be attributed to the divine nature.

Checkpoint
What is the first horn of Baqillani's dilemma regarding the union during crucifixion?
A) If the union ended, then Jesus died as a god
B) If the union remained, then the eternal Son died
C) If the union remained, then the body was not Jesus
D) If the union ended, then the Son remained alive

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses a dilemma to show that the crucifixion of the Messiah is logically impossible if the hypostatic union is maintained.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever described Allah in human terms without realizing that you are compromising His transcendence? What practical steps will you take to ensure your speech about Allah remains consistent with His perfection, as this lesson demands?
?
Baqillani forces the Christians to face a logical contradiction. Is there any belief you hold about Allah or His attributes that crumbles when examined with similar rigor? Will you dare to test your own convictions today?
?
This passage shows that a single compromise on God's inability to die leads to absurd consequences. What small, seemingly harmless compromise in your faith have you allowed that, if carried to its logical conclusion, would undermine tawheed? How will you uproot it?

Why the Word United with Jesus and Not with Other Prophets
Baqillani questions why the Word united with Jesus specifically, not with other prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's critical argument against the Christian claim that the Word uniquely united with Jesus due to his miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles alone do not prove divinity — God's power works through all prophets.

Baqillani challenges the Christian doctrine of the Word's union with Jesus by asking why other prophets, who also performed miracles, are excluded. He then dissects the logic of using miracles as evidence, suggesting that God may be the true agent and that parallel cases undermine the exclusivity claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow of the argument.
Notice the footnote markers; they are editorial and can be ignored.
2
Identify the opening question
The passage begins with a critical question: why do Christians say the Word united with Jesus but not with Moses, Abraham, or other prophets?
This sets up the entire challenge.
3
Recognize the Christian response
The Christian answer is that Jesus performed miracles beyond human capacity, which necessitated his divinity and union with the Word.
Examples: reviving the dead, curing blindness, walking on water.
4
Understand Baqillani's two counterpoints
First, Jesus may not have been the actual agent; God could have performed the miracles through him. Second, Moses performed equally astonishing miracles, so if miracles prove union, Moses should also be divine.
The passage ends mid-sentence describing Moses' miracles.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider how Baqillani's critique undermines the Christian argument: miracles are not unique to Jesus, and agency is not necessarily with the human prophet.
This challenges the basis for claiming Jesus's divinity and union.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى على جميعهم في الاتحاد يُقال (٥) لهم : لِمَ قلتم إن كلمة الله اتحدت بجسد المسيح دون جسد (٦) موسى وإبراهيم وغيرهما من النبيين؟ فإن قالوا : لأجل ما ظهر على يد عیسى من فعل الآيات واختراع المعجزات التي لا يقدر البشر على مثلها، من نحو إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكْمَهِ والأبرص، وجعل القليل كثيراً وقلب الماء خمراً والمشي على الماء (۷) السماء وإبراء الزمن وإقامة المُقْعَد وغير وصعود ذلك من عجيب الآيات، فوجب أن يكون (۸) إلهاً وأن الكلمة متحدة به، يقال لهم : لم زعمتم أن عيسى فاعل لما وصفتم من الآيات ومخترع لها؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون غير قادر على قليل من ذلك ولا كثير وأن يكون الله تعالى هو الذي فعل جميع ما ظهر على (1) يده من ذلك (١٠) ، وتكون حاله فيه حال سائر الأنبياء فيما ظهر عليهم من الآيات؟ ثم يقال لهم : ما (١١) أنكرتم أن يكون موسى عليه السلام (۱۲) إلها وأن تكون الكلمة متحدة به لما فعله الآيات البديعة (١٣) نحو قلب العصا حيةً من ذات (١٤) فم وعينين وخروق ولم تكن من قبل حية ولا فيها رسم عينين ولا فم،
Another question against all of them concerning the union. It is said (٥) to them: Why did you say that the Word of God united with the body of the Christ to the exclusion of the body (٦) of Moses, Abraham, and other prophets? If they say: Because of what appeared at the hand of Jesus of performing signs and inventing miracles that humans are not capable of, such as reviving the dead, curing the blind and leper, making little much, turning water into wine, walking on water (۷) the heaven, curing the paralytic, raising the crippled, and such wonderful signs, so it was necessary that he be (۸) a god and that the Word be united with him, it is said to them: Why do you claim that Jesus is the doer of what you described of signs and the inventor of them? And why do you deny that he is incapable of little or much of that, and that God Almighty is the one who did all that appeared at (1) his hand of that (١٠), and his case in that is like the case of the rest of the prophets in what appeared of signs at their hands? Then it is said to them: What (١١) prevents you from holding that Moses, peace be upon him (۱۲), is a god and that the Word is united with him because of the wonderful signs he performed (١٣), such as turning the staff into a snake with a mouth, eyes, and holes, though it was not a snake before, nor had it the form of eyes or mouth?
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a critical question challenging the Christian claim that the Word (Logos) united uniquely with Jesus. It begins by asking why they refuse the same union for other prophets. The Christian answer is the miracles Jesus performed, which are beyond human power. Baqillani counters with two points: first, that Jesus might not be the actual agent of those miracles—God could be acting through him, as with other prophets; second, by analogy, Moses performed equally astonishing miracles, so if miracles prove union, Moses should also be considered divine. The argument is left incomplete due to the page break, but the implication is that the Christian argument from miracles is insufficient.

Key Terms
كلمة الله (kalimat Allah)
اتحد (ittahada)
آيات (ayat)
معجزات (mu'jizat)
نبي (nabi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That miracles performed by a prophet necessarily indicate his divinity.
Correction: Baqillani argues that God may be the true agent of miracles, and other prophets like Moses performed similar wonders, so miracles alone do not prove union or divinity.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's main objection to the Christian claim that Jesus's miracles prove the union of the Word with him?
A) Jesus did not perform miracles
B) God could have performed the miracles through Jesus, and other prophets performed similar miracles
C) Jesus's miracles were not authentic
D) Moses performed greater miracles

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's critique shows that miracles are not unique to Jesus and their performance does not necessitate union with the divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Christians saw Jesus' miracles and concluded he was God. What 'miracles' in your life—your intelligence, health, wealth—do you subtly treat as evidence of your own worth or divinity, rather than as signs pointing to Allah?
?
If you truly believed that every extraordinary event is from Allah alone, how would your prayer life change when you witness something amazing? Would you be quicker to thank Him and slower to exalt the human vessel?

Refutation of the Crucifixion: The Killed One Was Not the Messiah
Baqillani refutes the crucifixion by showing death nullifies the union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the Christian claim that the Messiah was killed on the cross, based on the dissolution of the union at death.

Core Idea
Death dissolves the union, so only a human dies, not the Messiah.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents a concise theological argument against the Christian claim that Jesus (the Messiah) was crucified. He uses the Christian concept of the union (incarnation) to show that the one who was killed could not have been the Messiah. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the key terms
Notice the terms 'المسيح', 'الاتحاد', 'الموت', 'الصلب'. Understand their role.
3
Follow the logical argument
Trace how Baqillani argues that the union constitutes the Messiah, and its dissolution at death means only a human died.
The argument assumes the Christian doctrine of union.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ليس المقتول مسيحاً ؛ لأن الجسد عند انتقاض الاتحاد ومفارقة المتحدِ به بمسيح وإنما يكون الجسد وما اتحد به مسيحاً مع ثبوت الاتحاد ووجوده فإذا بطل كان المقتول المصلوب الواقع عليه الموت إنساناً ولا معنى لقولكم إن المسيح قتل وصلب
The killed one is not the Messiah; because the body, upon dissolution of the union and separation of that with which it is united, is not the Messiah. Rather, the body and that which is united with it become the Messiah only with the establishment and existence of the union. So when it is nullified, the killed, crucified one upon whom death occurred becomes a human, and your statement that the Messiah was killed and crucified has no meaning.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage refutes the Christian claim that Jesus (the Messiah) was killed and crucified. The argument is based on the Christian doctrine of the union (incarnation). The author states that the one who was killed is not the Messiah because the union between the divine Word and the body of Jesus is what makes the composite 'Messiah'. That union is dissolved at death, so the one suffering death is only the human body, not the Messiah. Therefore, the claim 'the Messiah was killed' is meaningless.

Misconception: Christians might think that the divine nature of Christ suffered death on the cross.
Correction: Baqillani explains that the union which makes the body 'Messiah' is dissolved at death, so the divine nature is unaffected.

B) Because the union was dissolved at death, so only a human was killed
C) Because Jesus never existed

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the crucifixion by arguing that the union of divine and human in Christ is dissolved at death, so only a human died.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Consider a comfort you derive from a belief that seems unshakeable—like the permanence of a relationship or a worldview. Are you willing to let it go if truth demands it, even if it feels foundational?
?
The lesson shows that death dissolves the union that defines the Messiah. What ‘unions’ in your life—attachments, identities, or securities—will death dissolve? What remains of you that is truly eternal?

Miracles Do Not Prove Union: The Case of Moses and the Gospel
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that Jesus's miracles prove union with the Word.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that miracles alone cannot prove the incarnation, using the example of Moses and Gospel quotations showing Jesus's dependence on God.

Core Idea
Miracles prove God's power, not the performer's divinity.

In this passage, Baqillani challenges the Christian claim that Jesus's miracles prove the union of the Word with him. He argues that if miracles were sufficient, Moses would also be divine. He supports his argument with Gospel verses where Jesus prays to God, demonstrating his dependence. This lesson examines the logic and scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the argument structure: question, Christian answer, Baqillani's counter-argument using Moses, Christian defense, and Baqillani's Gospel evidence.
The passage ends mid-sentence during a Christian objection; this will be addressed later.
2
Identify the Christian claim and Baqillani's counter-example
The Christians claim Jesus's miracles prove union of the Word. Baqillani asks: what about Moses? He performed similar miracles (staff into snake, sea splitting) and yet they do not call him divine. Why the double standard?
3
Analyze the use of Gospel quotations
Baqillani cites Gospel verses where Jesus prays, weeps, and expresses dependence on God. These show Jesus is a servant, not a god. Find each quote and consider how it refutes the Christian claim.
The verses demonstrate Jesus's supplication and humility.
4
Understand the incomplete objection
The passage ends as Christians object that Jesus's prayers were for teaching. Baqillani's response is cut off. Reflect on how the argument might continue — likely Jesus's actions as a servant are real, not pedagogical.
The core point remains: miracles and prayer show Jesus is a created being.

مسألة أخرى على جميعهم في الاتحاد يُقال لهم : لِمَ قلتم إن كلمة الله اتحدت بجسد المسيح دون جسد موسى وإبراهيم وغيرهما من النبيين؟ فإن قالوا : لأجل ما ظهر على يد عيسى من فعل الآيات واختراع المعجزات التي لا يقدر البشر على مثلها، من نحو إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكْمَهِ والأبرص، وجعل القليل كثيراً وقلب الماء خمراً والمشي على الماء وصعود السماء وإبراء الزمن وإقامة المُقْعَد وغير ذلك من عجيب الآيات، فوجب أن يكون إلهاً وأن الكلمة متحدة به، يقال لهم : لم زعمتم أن عيسى فاعل لما وصفتم من الآيات ومخترع لها؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون غير قادر على قليل من ذلك ولا كثير وأن يكون الله تعالى هو الذي فعل جميع ما ظهر على يده من ذلك، وتكون حاله فيه حال سائر الأنبياء فيما ظهر عليهم من الآيات؟ ثم يقال لهم : ما أنكرتم أن يكون موسى عليه السلام إلها وأن تكون الكلمة متحدة به لما فعله الآيات البديعية نحو قلب العصا حيةً من ذات فم وعينين وخروق ولم تكن من قبل حية ولا فيها رسم عينين ولا فم، ونحو فلق البحر، وإخراج يده بيضاء، وغير ذلك، وما أتى به من الجراد والقمل والضفادع والدم، وغير ذلك مما لا يقدر عليه البشر؟ فإن قالوا: موسى لم يكن مخترعا الشيء وإنما كان يدعو ويرغب إلى الله تعالى في أن يُظهر على يديه ذلك، يقال لهم : فما أنكرتم أن تكون هذه حال عيسى وأنه كان يرغب إلى خالقه وربه ومالكه في أن يُظْهِر الآيات على يده؟ وقد نطق الإنجيل بذلك لأن في الإنجيل أن عيسى عليه السلام بكى فقال : «رب ! إن كان في مشيئتك أن تَصْرِفَ هذه الكأس عن أحد فاصرفها عني، وأنه أراد أن يُحيي كَهْلاً فقال: يا أبي ! أدعوك كما كنت أدعوك فتستجيب لي، وإنما أدعوك من أجل هؤلاء ليعلموا، وقال : يا أبي ! أنا أحمدك، وقال وهو على الخشبة وقت الصلب بزعمهم : إلهي ! إلهي ! لم تركتني ؟» وهذا وتضرعه وابتهاله فوجب أنه عبد مربوبٌ ومُحدَت مخلوق كموسى وغيره من الرسل عليهم السلام فإن قالوا : عيسى كان يدعو ويرغب بهذا الدعاء على سبيل التعليم للأتباع والتلاميذ؛ وإلا فقد كان يخترع الآيات اختراعاً ويأمر أن
Another issue against all of them concerning the union. It is said to them: Why did you say that the Word of God became united with the body of Jesus to the exclusion of the body of Moses, Abraham, and other prophets? If they say: Because of what appeared at the hand of Jesus of performing signs and inventing miracles that humans are not capable of, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and the leper, making little much, turning water into wine, walking on water, ascending to heaven, healing the paralytic, raising the crippled, and other wondrous signs, so it is necessary that he be a god and that the Word be united with him. It is said to them: Why do you claim that Jesus is the agent of these signs and their inventor? What prevents you from [saying] that he is not capable of a little or much of that, and that God Almighty is the one who did all that appeared at his hand, and his state in that is the state of all prophets regarding what appeared at their hands of signs? Then it is said to them: What prevents you from [saying] that Moses, peace be upon him, is a god and that the Word is united with him because of the wondrous signs he performed, such as turning the staff into a snake with a mouth, eyes, and holes, which was not previously a snake nor had in it the shape of eyes or mouth, and such as splitting the sea, bringing forth his hand white, and other things, and what he brought of locusts, lice, frogs, and blood, and other things that humans are not capable of? If they say: Moses was not an inventor of the thing; rather, he used to supplicate and beseech Allah Almighty to manifest that at his hands. It is said to them: What prevents you from [saying] that this is the case of Jesus and that he used to beseech his Creator, Lord, and Owner to manifest the signs at his hand? And the Gospel has stated that, because in the Gospel it is that Jesus, peace be upon him, wept and said: 'Lord! If it is in Your will to turn this cup away from anyone, turn it away from me'; and that he wanted to revive a man and said: 'O my Father! I call upon You as I used to call upon You and You answer me, and I only call upon You for the sake of these people so that they may know'; and he said: 'O my Father! I praise You'; and he said while on the wood at the time of the crucifixion, according to their claim: 'My God! My God! Why have You forsaken me?' And this, and his supplication and entreaty, necessitates that he is a subjugated servant and a created being like Moses and other messengers, peace be upon them. If they say: Jesus used to supplicate and beseech through this supplication by way of teaching for followers and disciples; otherwise, he used to invent signs inventively and command that...
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian argument that Jesus's miracles prove the Word (Logos) became united with him. The author proceeds in a question-and-answer format. First, he asks why Christians single out Jesus as the locus of union among all prophets. Their response is that Jesus performed extraordinary miracles, implying his divinity. The author counters by questioning whether Jesus was the actual agent of these miracles, suggesting that God could have performed them through him, just as with other prophets. He then brings the example of Moses, who also performed stunning miracles (turning a staff into a snake, splitting the sea, etc.) that should, by the same logic, prove Moses divine. The Christians reply that Moses only performed miracles through supplication, not by his own power. The author then cites Gospel passages showing Jesus himself prayed and beseeched God, including prayers of anguish and dependence. These demonstrate that Jesus, like Moses, was a servant dependent on God, not a god. Finally, the author anticipates the Christian objection that Jesus's prayers were for teaching purposes only, but the text ends before the complete rebuttal.

الكلمة

عيسى
الإنجيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Performing miracles proves a person is divine or united with God.
Correction: Miracles are performed by God through prophets; they do not indicate divinity. Many prophets performed similar miracles, yet they are not considered divine.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani use the example of Prophet Moses to refute the Christian claim about Jesus?
A) Moses was greater than Jesus
B) Moses also performed miracles, yet Christians do not consider him divine
C) Moses never performed miracles
D) Moses denied the union

Key Takeaway
Miracles alone cannot prove divinity or incarnation; they are signs from God performed through prophets, as shown by Moses and even Jesus's own prayers in the Gospel.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness someone with extraordinary abilities or success, do you ever subtly elevate them in your heart as if they are beyond God's control? How does this lesson's emphasis on God as the true agent of all miracles challenge that tendency?
?
Jesus wept and prayed, 'My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?' Have you ever felt abandoned by God? How does knowing that even a prophet experienced such raw dependence on God change how you approach your own moments of desperation?
?
If miracles, even resurrection, do not prove divinity, what does that mean for how you view religious figures or leaders who claim special status? Are you willing to strip away every illusion of human divinity and submit only to God, even when it feels uncomfortable?

First Refutation: Prayer Proves Servitude
First objection: Jesus' prayers show he is a servant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Jesus' own prayers from the Gospel to demonstrate that Jesus is a servant like Moses.

Core Idea
Prayer shows dependence on God, not divinity.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses the first Christian objection: that Moses supplicated for miracles while Jesus performed them by his own power. By citing Gospel accounts of Jesus praying, he shows that Jesus also relied on supplication, thus dismantling the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how the Christian objection is framed and how Baqillani responds.
The objection claims Moses only supplicated, implying Jesus did not.
2
Identify the Gospel citations
Find the instances where Jesus is reported to have prayed or supplicated. Reflect on how these undermine the Christian claim.
The citations include Gethsemane, the cross, and a healing prayer.
3
Understand the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that Jesus' prayers necessitate he is a servant and created being. Ask yourself why this conclusion follows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحو فلق البحر، وإخراج يده بيضاء، وغير ذلك، وما أتى به من الجواد والقمل والضفادع والدم، وغير ذلك مما لا يقدر عليه البشر؟ فإن من ذلك وإنما كان يدعو ويرغب. قالوا: موسى لم يكن مخترعا الشيء إلى الله تعالى في أن يظهر على يديه ذلك، يقال لهم: فما أنكرتم أن تكون هذه حال عيسى أن يظهر الآيات على يده؟ وأنه كان يرغب إلى خالقه وربه ومالكه في ذلك. وقد نطق الإنجيل بذلك لأن في الإنجيل أن عيسى عليه السلام بكى فقال: «رب ! إن كان في مشيئتك أن تصرف هذه الكأس عن أحد فاصرفها عني، وأنه أراد أن يحيي كهلا فقال: يا أبي ! أدعوك كما كنت أدعوك فتستجيب لي، وإنما أدعوك من أجل هؤلاء ليعلموا، وقال : ( يا أبي ! أنا أحمدك، وقال وهو على الخشبة وقت الصلب بزعمهم : إلهي ! إلهي ! لم تركتني ؟»، وهذا وتضرعه وابتهاله فوجب أنه عبد مربوب ومحدث مخلوق كموسى وغيره من الرسل عليهم السلام. فإن قالوا: عيسى كان يدعو ويرغب بهذا الدعاء على سبيل التعليم للأتباع والتلاميذ؛ وإلا فقد كان يخترع الآيات اختراعاً ويأمر أن يكون فيكون، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم من أن يكون دعاء موسى ورغبته إنما وقع على سبيل التعليم؟ وإلا فقد كان يخترع فلق البحر وإخراج اليد بيضاء وقلب العصا ثعباناً وتظليلهم بالغمام واختراع المن والسلوى ويأمر بأن يكون ذلك فيكون فلا يجدون إلى ذلك مدفعاً. فإن قالوا: قولنا «مسيح» اسم لمعنيين: لاهوت، هو إله، وناسوت، هو إنسان مخلوق؛ فما كان من تضرع ودعاء فإنما وقع من الإنسان الذي هو الناسوت؛ وما كان من إحداث آية وإظهار معجزة فهو واقع من الإله دون الإنسان يقال لهم: فما أنكرتم من أن يكون موسى أيضاً إسماً لمعنيين : إله وإنسان؛ فما كان من دعاء ورغبة فإنه واقع من الناسوت، وما كان من اختراع آية أو إبداع معجزة فإنه من اللاهوت دون الناسوت؛ ولا فصل في ذلك. فإن قالوا كل واحد من هؤلاء الأنبياء قد أقر بلسانه بأنه مخلوق وعبد مربوب مألوه مرسل من عند الله، عزّ وجلّ والمسيح لم يقر بذلك قيل لهم: وكذلك المسيح قد اعترف بأنه نبي مرسل وعبد مخلوق؛ لأن الإنجيل ينطق بأنه قال: «إني عبد الله وأرسلت معلماً»، وقال: «فكما بعثني أبي فكذلك أبعثكم عمدوا الناس وغسلوهم باسم الأب والابن والروح القدس قال في الإنجيل: إنّ النّبي لا يُكرم في مدينته»، في نظائر ذلك.
And such as the splitting of the sea, and the bringing forth of his hand white, and other things, and what he brought of the locusts and lice and frogs and blood, and other things which humans are not able to do? For from that, he was only supplicating and desiring. They said: Moses was not an inventor of the thing to Allah Almighty so that it appeared at his hand. It is said to them: What prevents you from this being the case of Jesus—that signs appear at his hand? And that he was desiring to his Creator and his Lord and his Owner in that. And the Gospel has stated that, because in the Gospel Jesus, peace be upon him, wept and said: 'Lord! If it is in Your will to turn this cup away from anyone, then turn it away from me.' And that he wanted to revive an old man and said: 'O my Father! I call upon You as I used to call upon You and You answer me, and I only call upon You for the sake of these people that they may know.' And he said: 'O my Father! I praise You.' And he said while on the wood at the time of the crucifixion according to their claim: 'My God! My God! Why have You forsaken me?' This and his supplication and his pleading necessitate that he is a servant, owned, created, originated like Moses and other messengers, peace be upon them. If they say: Jesus was supplicating and desiring with this supplication for the purpose of teaching his followers and disciples; otherwise he used to invent signs inventively and command and it would be. It is said to them: What prevents you from the supplication of Moses and his desire occurring only for the purpose of teaching? Otherwise he used to invent the splitting of the sea, the bringing forth of the hand white, the turning of the staff into a serpent, their shading with clouds, the invention of manna and quails, and he commands that it be and it is, and they find no way to refute that. If they say: Our statement 'Messiah' is a name for two meanings: Lahut (divine nature) which is God, and Nasut (human nature) which is a created human; so whatever was of supplication and prayer, it occurred from the human which is the Nasut; and whatever was of bringing about a sign and showing a miracle, it is from the Lahut, not from the human. It is said to them: What prevents you from Moses also being a name for two meanings: God and human? So whatever was of supplication and desire, it occurs from the Nasut, and whatever was of invention of a sign or creation of a miracle, it is from the Lahut, not from the Nasut; and there is no distinction in that. If they say: Every one of these prophets has acknowledged with his tongue that he is created and a servant, owned, worshipped, sent from Allah, Almighty and Majestic, and the Messiah did not acknowledge that. It is said to them: Likewise, the Messiah has acknowledged that he is a prophet sent and a created servant; because the Gospel states that he said: 'I am the servant of God and I have been sent as a teacher.' And he said: 'As my Father sent me, so I send you: baptize people and wash them in the name of the Father, the Son, and the Holy Spirit.' He said in the Gospel: 'A prophet is not honored in his own town.' And other similar instances.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of Christian objections regarding the divinity of Jesus. It consists of four arguments, each following an objection-answer format. The author, Imam Baqillani, uses the example of Moses to demonstrate the inconsistency in Christian reasoning. 

First objection: Christians argue that Moses did not invent miracles himself but only supplicated to God, implying that his miracles were not his own. Baqillani responds by asking why the same cannot be said for Jesus, citing Gospel passages where Jesus prays and supplicates, thus proving that Jesus also relied on God. This establishes Jesus as a servant and creature like Moses. 

Second objection: Christians claim Jesus' prayers were merely for teaching his followers, while he actually created miracles by his own command. Baqillani turns this back: Moses also commanded miracles (splitting the sea, etc.), so why cannot his prayers also be for teaching? The argument is symmetrical. 

Third objection: Christians propose a dual nature for Christ: a divine nature (Lahut) and a human nature (Nasut). All supplication and human acts come from the human nature, while miracles come from the divine nature. Baqillani retorts by suggesting that Moses could also be considered a name for two natures, with the same division, thus nullifying the Christian claim of uniqueness. 

Fourth objection: Christians assert that all prophets confessed their servitude except Jesus. Baqillani refutes this by quoting Gospel verses where Jesus calls himself a servant of God and a sent teacher, and other statements indicating his prophetic status. The argument systematically dismantles each objection by applying the same logic to Moses, showing that Christian reasoning is arbitrary.

Key Terms
دعاء
عبد مربوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Christians believe Jesus never prayed or supplicated.
Correction: The Gospel records multiple instances of Jesus praying, showing he relied on God.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani use to prove that Jesus also supplicated?
A) Quotes from the Torah
B) Gospel accounts of Jesus praying
C) Statements from the Prophet Muhammad
D) The miracles of Moses

Key Takeaway
Baqillani proves Jesus' servitude by citing his own prayers from the Gospel.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you truly feel the same desperation that Jesus (peace be upon him) showed on the cross, crying out 'My God, why have you forsaken me?' – or is your prayer a comfortable routine? What would it take for you to pray with that level of sincerity?
?
If you were stripped of every power and ability, would you still believe you are a servant owned by Allah, complete dependent on Him? How does your daily life reflect that reality, or mask it?
?
Baqillani uses Jesus' own words to prove his servitude. When was the last time you let someone else's words – even an opponent's sacred text – challenge your deeply held assumptions? Are you open to correction from unexpected sources?

Second Refutation: Teaching vs. Command
Second objection: Jesus' prayers were for teaching, but he commanded miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani counters the Christian claim that Jesus' prayers were only for teaching by applying the same logic to Moses.

Core Idea
Consistency demands that if Jesus' prayers were teaching, so were Moses'.

The second Christian objection argues that Jesus' prayers were merely to instruct his followers, while he actually created miracles by his own command. Baqillani turns the argument around: if that reasoning holds, then Moses also commanded miracles and his prayers could be seen as teaching, so no distinction exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Christian claim
Read the start of the passage to see the Christian objection: Jesus' prayers were just for teaching, but he really created miracles by command.
They assert Jesus could command and it would happen instantly.
2
Note Baqillani's counter
Baqillani asks: why not say the same for Moses? He lists Moses' miracles that occurred by command, and suggests his prayers could also be for teaching.
The counter is a straightforward analogy.
3
Reflect on the force of the argument
Consider how this parallel undermines the Christian claim of uniqueness. If the same logic applies to Moses, then Jesus is not special.

ونحو فلق البحر، وإخراج يده بيضاء، وغير ذلك، وما أتى به من الجواد والقمل والضفادع والدم، وغير ذلك مما لا يقدر عليه البشر؟ فإن من ذلك وإنما كان يدعو ويرغب. قالوا: موسى لم يكن مخترعا الشيء إلى الله تعالى في أن يظهر على يديه ذلك، يقال لهم: فما أنكرتم أن تكون هذه حال عيسى أن يظهر الآيات على يده؟ وأنه كان يرغب إلى خالقه وربه ومالكه في ذلك. وقد نطق الإنجيل بذلك لأن في الإنجيل أن عيسى عليه السلام بكى فقال: «رب ! إن كان في مشيئتك أن تصرف هذه الكأس عن أحد فاصرفها عني، وأنه أراد أن يحيي كهلا فقال: يا أبي ! أدعوك كما كنت أدعوك فتستجيب لي، وإنما أدعوك من أجل هؤلاء ليعلموا، وقال : ( يا أبي ! أنا أحمدك، وقال وهو على الخشبة وقت الصلب بزعمهم : إلهي ! إلهي ! لم تركتني ؟»، وهذا وتضرعه وابتهاله فوجب أنه عبد مربوب ومحدث مخلوق كموسى وغيره من الرسل عليهم السلام. فإن قالوا: عيسى كان يدعو ويرغب بهذا الدعاء على سبيل التعليم للأتباع والتلاميذ؛ وإلا فقد كان يخترع الآيات اختراعاً ويأمر أن يكون فيكون، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم من أن يكون دعاء موسى ورغبته إنما وقع على سبيل التعليم؟ وإلا فقد كان يخترع فلق البحر وإخراج اليد بيضاء وقلب العصا ثعباناً وتظليلهم بالغمام واختراع المن والسلوى ويأمر بأن يكون ذلك فيكون فلا يجدون إلى ذلك مدفعاً. فإن قالوا: قولنا «مسيح» اسم لمعنيين: لاهوت، هو إله، وناسوت، هو إنسان مخلوق؛ فما كان من تضرع ودعاء فإنما وقع من الإنسان الذي هو الناسوت؛ وما كان من إحداث آية وإظهار معجزة فهو واقع من الإله دون الإنسان يقال لهم: فما أنكرتم من أن يكون موسى أيضاً إسماً لمعنيين : إله وإنسان؛ فما كان من دعاء ورغبة فإنه واقع من الناسوت، وما كان من اختراع آية أو إبداع معجزة فإنه من اللاهوت دون الناسوت؛ ولا فصل في ذلك. فإن قالوا كل واحد من هؤلاء الأنبياء قد أقر بلسانه بأنه مخلوق وعبد مربوب مألوه مرسل من عند الله، عزّ وجلّ والمسيح لم يقر بذلك قيل لهم: وكذلك المسيح قد اعترف بأنه نبي مرسل وعبد مخلوق؛ لأن الإنجيل ينطق بأنه قال: «إني عبد الله وأرسلت معلماً»، وقال: «فكما بعثني أبي فكذلك أبعثكم عمدوا الناس وغسلوهم باسم الأب والابن والروح القدس قال في الإنجيل: إنّ النّبي لا يُكرم في مدينته»، في نظائر ذلك.
And such as the splitting of the sea, and the bringing forth of his hand white, and other things, and what he brought of the locusts and lice and frogs and blood, and other things which humans are not able to do? For from that, he was only supplicating and desiring. They said: Moses was not an inventor of the thing to Allah Almighty so that it appeared at his hand. It is said to them: What prevents you from this being the case of Jesus—that signs appear at his hand? And that he was desiring to his Creator and his Lord and his Owner in that. And the Gospel has stated that, because in the Gospel Jesus, peace be upon him, wept and said: 'Lord! If it is in Your will to turn this cup away from anyone, then turn it away from me.' And that he wanted to revive an old man and said: 'O my Father! I call upon You as I used to call upon You and You answer me, and I only call upon You for the sake of these people that they may know.' And he said: 'O my Father! I praise You.' And he said while on the wood at the time of the crucifixion according to their claim: 'My God! My God! Why have You forsaken me?' This and his supplication and his pleading necessitate that he is a servant, owned, created, originated like Moses and other messengers, peace be upon them. If they say: Jesus was supplicating and desiring with this supplication for the purpose of teaching his followers and disciples; otherwise he used to invent signs inventively and command and it would be. It is said to them: What prevents you from the supplication of Moses and his desire occurring only for the purpose of teaching? Otherwise he used to invent the splitting of the sea, the bringing forth of the hand white, the turning of the staff into a serpent, their shading with clouds, the invention of manna and quails, and he commands that it be and it is, and they find no way to refute that. If they say: Our statement 'Messiah' is a name for two meanings: Lahut (divine nature) which is God, and Nasut (human nature) which is a created human; so whatever was of supplication and prayer, it occurred from the human which is the Nasut; and whatever was of bringing about a sign and showing a miracle, it is from the Lahut, not from the human. It is said to them: What prevents you from Moses also being a name for two meanings: God and human? So whatever was of supplication and desire, it occurs from the Nasut, and whatever was of invention of a sign or creation of a miracle, it is from the Lahut, not from the Nasut; and there is no distinction in that. If they say: Every one of these prophets has acknowledged with his tongue that he is created and a servant, owned, worshipped, sent from Allah, Almighty and Majestic, and the Messiah did not acknowledge that. It is said to them: Likewise, the Messiah has acknowledged that he is a prophet sent and a created servant; because the Gospel states that he said: 'I am the servant of God and I have been sent as a teacher.' And he said: 'As my Father sent me, so I send you: baptize people and wash them in the name of the Father, the Son, and the Holy Spirit.' He said in the Gospel: 'A prophet is not honored in his own town.' And other similar instances.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of Christian objections regarding the divinity of Jesus. It consists of four arguments, each following an objection-answer format. The author, Imam Baqillani, uses the example of Moses to demonstrate the inconsistency in Christian reasoning. 

First objection: Christians argue that Moses did not invent miracles himself but only supplicated to God, implying that his miracles were not his own. Baqillani responds by asking why the same cannot be said for Jesus, citing Gospel passages where Jesus prays and supplicates, thus proving that Jesus also relied on God. This establishes Jesus as a servant and creature like Moses. 

Second objection: Christians claim Jesus' prayers were merely for teaching his followers, while he actually created miracles by his own command. Baqillani turns this back: Moses also commanded miracles (splitting the sea, etc.), so why cannot his prayers also be for teaching? The argument is symmetrical. 

Third objection: Christians propose a dual nature for Christ: a divine nature (Lahut) and a human nature (Nasut). All supplication and human acts come from the human nature, while miracles come from the divine nature. Baqillani retorts by suggesting that Moses could also be considered a name for two natures, with the same division, thus nullifying the Christian claim of uniqueness. 

Fourth objection: Christians assert that all prophets confessed their servitude except Jesus. Baqillani refutes this by quoting Gospel verses where Jesus calls himself a servant of God and a sent teacher, and other statements indicating his prophetic status. The argument systematically dismantles each objection by applying the same logic to Moses, showing that Christian reasoning is arbitrary.

Key Terms
تعليم
اختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani respond to the claim that Jesus' prayers were only for teaching?
A) He denies that Jesus performed miracles.
B) He says Moses also commanded miracles, so his prayers could also be teaching.
C) He quotes the Gospel to show Jesus really commanded miracles.
D) He accepts the Christian claim.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the Christian objection is self-defeating when applied consistently to Moses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make an argument for your beliefs, do you apply the same standard of proof to your own claims as you do to others? In what specific area of your faith are you most tempted to be inconsistent, like the Christians in this passage? Commit to one change this week to align your reasoning with the consistency you see in Baqillani's rebuttal.
?
Think of a time you dismissed someone else's prayer as less sincere or valid than your own. What would Baqillani's logic say about that double standard? Will you repent of that judgment today and ask Allah to purify your heart from intellectual arrogance?
?
Baqillani uses Moses' miracles to expose a flaw in the Christian argument. Is there a 'Moses' in your life—someone whose circumstances or gifts you ignore because it's inconvenient for your narrative? What would it cost you to apply the same standard to them? Are you willing to pay that price to be truthful before Allah?

Third Refutation: The Dual Nature Argument
Third objection: Christ's dual nature argument turned against Christians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Christian doctrine of Christ's dual nature by applying the same distinction to Moses.

Core Idea
If Jesus can have two natures, so can Moses.

Christians propose that Jesus has a divine nature (Lahut) and a human nature (Nasut). Supplications come from the human nature, miracles from the divine. Baqillani counters by suggesting that Moses could also be considered a name for two natures, thus nullifying the Christian claim of Jesus' uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dual nature claim
Read the Christian objection: 'Messiah' is a name for two meanings—Lahut (God) and Nasut (human). Prayers come from the human, miracles from the divine.
This is a classic Christian theological position.
2
See Baqillani's parallel
Baqillani asks: why can't Moses also be a name for two natures? Then the same division would apply, and Jesus is not unique.
The argument is simple: if you allow that for one prophet, you must allow it for another.
3
Reflect on the logical force
Consider how this refutation exposes arbitrariness. The Christians have no criterion to limit this dual nature to Jesus alone.

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of Christian objections regarding the divinity of Jesus. It consists of four arguments, each following an objection-answer format. The author, Imam Baqillani, uses the example of Moses to demonstrate the inconsistency in Christian reasoning. 

First objection: Christians argue that Moses did not invent miracles himself but only supplicated to God, implying that his miracles were not his own. Baqillani responds by asking why the same cannot be said for Jesus, citing Gospel passages where Jesus prays and supplicates, thus proving that Jesus also relied on God. This establishes Jesus as a servant and creature like Moses. 

Second objection: Christians claim Jesus' prayers were merely for teaching his followers, while he actually created miracles by his own command. Baqillani turns this back: Moses also commanded miracles (splitting the sea, etc.), so why cannot his prayers also be for teaching? The argument is symmetrical. 

Third objection: Christians propose a dual nature for Christ: a divine nature (Lahut) and a human nature (Nasut). All supplication and human acts come from the human nature, while miracles come from the divine nature. Baqillani retorts by suggesting that Moses could also be considered a name for two natures, with the same division, thus nullifying the Christian claim of uniqueness. 

Fourth objection: Christians assert that all prophets confessed their servitude except Jesus. Baqillani refutes this by quoting Gospel verses where Jesus calls himself a servant of God and a sent teacher, and other statements indicating his prophetic status. The argument systematically dismantles each objection by applying the same logic to Moses, showing that Christian reasoning is arbitrary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Christians think the dual nature concept is unique to Jesus.
Correction: Baqillani shows it can be applied to Moses by the same logic.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's response to the dual nature argument?
A) He accepts the dual nature of Jesus.
B) He argues Moses could also have two natures, making Jesus non-unique.
C) He denies that miracles come from the divine nature.
D) He quotes the Bible to refute the dual nature.

Key Takeaway
The dual nature argument is not unique to Jesus; it can be applied to Moses, undermining its validity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself holding a belief about someone or something simply because it was convenient or traditional, without considering if it could be applied consistently? How does Baqillani's argument challenge you to examine your own inconsistencies?
?
When you hear arguments that seem to prove something unique about a person or group, do you ever ask yourself if the same logic could apply to someone else? What would it cost you to apply the same reasoning to others?
?
The Christians in this argument attributed Jesus' miracles to his divine nature and his prayers to his human nature. Is there any area in your own life where you separate your actions into 'divine' and 'human' categories, absolving yourself of responsibility? What would change if you saw all your actions as coming from the same human self accountable to God?

Fourth Refutation: Jesus' Own Acknowledgment of Servitude
Fourth objection: Gospel shows Jesus acknowledging servitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Gospel passages where Jesus calls himself a servant and prophet to refute the Christian claim that Jesus never acknowledged being a creature.

Core Idea
The Gospel itself records Jesus confessing he is a servant of God.

The fourth Christian objection states that all prophets except Jesus confessed their servitude. Baqillani counters by quoting the Gospel where Jesus explicitly says, 'I am the servant of God' and other statements that show he considered himself a sent prophet and a servant.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
The Christians claim Jesus never said he was a creature. Baqillani responds with direct Gospel quotes.
Look for the verses quoted: 'I am the servant of God and I have been sent as a teacher.'
2
Analyze the Gospel evidence
Note the specific phrases: 'I am the servant of God', 'I was sent', 'the prophet Muhammad?' - wait, no, it's 'a prophet is not honored in his own town.'
These show Jesus identified as a prophet and servant.
3
Reflect on the implication
If Jesus himself says he is a servant, then the Christian claim is false. This directly supports the Islamic view.
