Barahima's Denial and Refutation of Their Argument
Baqillani reports the Barahima's position and argument against prophethood, then begins refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Barahima's rejection of all prophets except Adam, their argument based on equality of human nature, and Baqillani's initial refutation challenging the assumption that preference entails injustice.

Core Idea
Preference by God is not injustice; it is His wisdom and grace.

Imam Baqillani begins his dialectical engagement with the Barahima, a sect that denied prophethood after Adam. He first reports their position and the argument they use to justify their rejection. Then he launches a critical question that exposes the flaw in their reasoning: why must divine preference be considered unjust? This lesson unpacks that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Barahima's claim
Read the opening sentences to grasp what the Barahima do and do not believe about prophets. Note that they accept Adam (or Ibrahim) but deny all others.
The text mentions two opinions within the Barahima: some accept only Adam, others only Ibrahim.
2
Understand their argument
Notice the reasoning they present: the messenger is of the same species and essence as humans, so giving one human superiority over another would be injustice (ḥayf) and favoritism (muḥābāh), which cannot be attributed to the Wise God.
Key terms: jins (species), jawhar (substance), tafḍīl (preference), ḥayf (injustice).
3
Examine the refutation
See how Baqillani challenges the premise that preference necessarily implies injustice. He asks: why must it be injustice? God may bestow favor on whom He wills, and all His actions are just and wise.
This is the first step in a longer argument; Baqillani forces the opponent to defend their assumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الفريق الآخر: إن الله تعالى ما أرسل رسولاً سوى آدم عليه السلام وكذبوا كل مدع للنبوة سواه . وقال قوم منهم : بل ما بعث الله تعالى غير إبراهيم وحده وأنكروا نبوة من سواه. وهذا جملة قولهم . فيقال لمن أحال من الله سبحانه إنفاذ رسله إلى خلقه لم قلت ذلك وما دليلك عليه ؟ فإن قال : لعلمه سبحانه بأن الرسول من جنس المُرْسَلِ إليه وأن جوهرهما واحد وأن تفضيل أحد المتماثلين المتساويين على مِثْلِهِ ونوعه ومن هو بصفته حَيْفٌ ومحاباة وميل وخروج عن الحكمة وذلك غير جائز على الحكيم، يقال لهم : لم قلتم إن تفضيل الله سبحانه بعض الجنس على بعض ورفع بعضهم إذا كان محاباة للمُتَفَضّل عليه وجب أن يكون ظلماً وخروجاً عن الحكمة؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون الله سبحانه أن يختص بفضله مَنْ يشاء مِنْ خَلْقِه ، وله التسوية بين سائرهم ؛ فإن ذلك أجمع عَدْلٌ منه وصواب من تدبيره؟
And the other group said: Verily Allah the Exalted did not send any messenger except Adam (peace be upon him), and they denied every claimant of prophethood besides him. And some of them said: Rather Allah the Exalted sent none other than Ibrahim alone, and they denied the prophethood of anyone else. And this is the sum of their statement. So one says to him who impossible deems it from Allah the Sublime to send His messengers to His creation: Why did you say that, and what is your proof for it? For if he says: Because of His knowledge the Sublime that the messenger is of the same kind as the one sent to, and that their substance is one, and that preferring one of the similar equals over its like and type and one who is in his description is injustice and favoritism and inclination and departure from wisdom, and that is not permissible for the Wise, it is said to them: Why did you say that the preferring by Allah the Sublime of some of the kind over others and raising some of them, when it is favoritism towards the preferred one, must be injustice and departure from wisdom? And what prevented you from [acknowledging] that Allah the Sublime may distinguish by His bounty whom He wills from His creation, and He may treat equally all others; for all of that is justice from Him and rightness of His governance?
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage begins by reporting the position of the Barahima (Brahmin sect) who deny prophethood after Adam, with some limiting it to Adam only and others to Abraham only. Baqillani then presents their argument: if God sends a messenger, that messenger is of the same species and essence as humanity; thus, giving one human superiority over another would be unjust favoritism, which cannot be attributed to God. The refutation is then initiated: Baqillani asks why such preference must be injustice—why cannot God simply bestow His favor on whomever He wills? All His actions are just and wise. The passage serves as the first step in a dialectical argument against the Barahima.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Barahima reject all prophets without exception.
Correction: The passage clarifies they accept at least Adam (and some also accept Ibrahim).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Barahima's primary argument against sending prophets?
A) Prophets are unnecessary because humans can know God through reason.
B) A messenger is of the same species as humans, so preferring one human over another would be unjust.
C) Allah has already sent all prophets needed in the past.
D) Prophets always bring false teachings.

Key Takeaway
The Barahima's argument from equality fails because God's preference is an act of wisdom, not injustice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone blessed with abilities, wealth, or status that you lack, do you feel that God has been unfair to you? How does this lesson's affirmation that God's preference is not injustice challenge that feeling, and what concrete step can you take this week to replace resentment with trust in His wisdom?
?
Are there areas in your life where you secretly believe God owes you something—like health, success, or ease—because you think you are equally deserving as others? Reflect on the Barahima's assumption: do you also assume that equal treatment is the only just treatment? How can you surrender that expectation and instead see all of God's decrees as right and just?
?
This lesson shows that God may freely favor whom He wills without being unjust. Is there someone in your life whom you find it hard to accept as favored by God (e.g., a prosperous person of weak faith, or a struggling believer)? What would it mean for you to genuinely believe that God's distribution is always just, even when it defies your human sense of fairness? Write one concrete thought or prayer you will offer when that resentment arises.

Jewish Anthropomorphists as Origin of Tashbih
Baqillani identifies Jewish Mushabbiha as origin of tashbih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's claim that the Jewish Mushabbiha are the original source of anthropomorphism (tashbih) and that later Islamic sects like the Rawafid adopted their ideas.

Core Idea
Jewish anthropomorphists are the root of all tashbih in Islam.

Theological errors do not arise in a vacuum. Baqillani traces the heresy of anthropomorphism (tashbih) back to a group among the Jews. He then shows how this error entered Islamic discourse through sects like the Rawafid. This lesson establishes the historical lineage of a major theological deviation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Pay attention to how Baqillani divides the Jews and then focuses on the Mushabbiha as the 'origin' (الأصل) of tashbih.
2
Identify the claim about influence
Note the statement that anyone in the Islamic state who said something involving tashbih has woven after their pattern, and that the Rawafid took their doctrine from them.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Baqillani would emphasize this connection – it shows that heretical ideas can cross religious boundaries and have ancient roots.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن جميع اليهود في أصول التوحيد فريقان: فريق منهم المشبهة. وهم الأصل في التشبيه وكل من قال قولاً في دولة الإسلام بشيء من التشابه فقد نسج على منوالهم. وأخذ مقالة من مقالهم الروافض وغيرهم . والفريق الثاني منهم : هم القدرية ينكرون الرؤية ويقولون : إن الحيوانات يخلقون أفعالهم، وأكثر الأمم كان فيما بينهم جماعة من القدرية، ولهذا قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لعنت القدرية على لسان سبعين نبيا». رواه الطبراني في الأوسط والقدرية الذين ظهروا في دولة الإسلام أخذوا طريقهم من قدرية اليهود، وقد كان في عصرنا جماعة ممن ينتسب إلى أصحاب الرأي، ويتستر بمذهبهم، وهو يضمر الإلحاد والقول بالقدر، وكان يراجع اليهود ويتعلم منهم الشبه التي يعزون بها العوام وكفاهم خزياً تعلمهم من اليهود واقتداؤهم بهم. والله سبحانه وتعالى يكفي المسلمين شرهم
Know that all Jews regarding the principles of tawhid are two groups: a group among them are the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists). They are the origin of tashbih, and everyone who said something in the Islamic state involving any anthropomorphism has woven after their pattern. And the Rawafid and others took their doctrine from their doctrine. The second group among them are the Qadariyya (predestinarians) who deny the beatific vision and say that living beings create their own actions, and most nations had among them a group of Qadariyya. For this reason the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'The Qadariyya are cursed on the tongue of seventy prophets.' It is narrated by al-Tabarani in al-Awsat. And the Qadariyya who appeared in the Islamic state took their path from the Jewish Qadariyya. And in our time there was a group who claim affiliation with the people of opinion (ahl al-ra'y) and conceal themselves behind their school, while inwardly harboring heresy and the doctrine of qadar, and they used to consult the Jews and learn from them the ambiguities with which they confuse the common people. Sufficient disgrace for them is their learning from the Jews and their following them. And Allah (glorified and exalted) will suffice the Muslims against their evil.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a classification and historical warning. Baqillani divides Jews into two theological groups regarding tawhid: the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) who are the original source of tashbih, and the Qadariyya (predestinarians) who deny the vision of Allah and affirm that creatures create their own actions. He notes that later Islamic sects like the Rawafid adopted ideas from the Jewish Mushabbiha, and the Qadariyya in Islam borrowed from Jewish Qadariyya. He then criticizes contemporary (in his time) crypto-qadariyya who outwardly claim to be from Ahl al-Ra'y but secretly hold heretical views and learn sophistical arguments from Jews to mislead the public. He ends with a supplication for Allah to protect Muslims from their harm.

Key Terms
مشبهة
تشبيه
الروافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Anthropomorphism (tashbih) originated within Islamic thought alone.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Jewish Mushabbiha predate and are the original source of tashbih, influencing later Islamic sects.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, who took their doctrine from the Jewish Mushabbiha?
A) The Mu'tazila
B) The Rawafid
C) The Ash'aris
D) The Sufis

Key Takeaway
The Jewish Mushabbiha are the original source of anthropomorphism, and Islamic sects like the Rawafid inherited their ideas.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani says that anyone who holds tashbih is following the pattern of Jewish anthropomorphists. Have you ever unknowingly harbored a thought about Allah that likened Him to something in creation? How will you train yourself to purify your understanding of tawhid starting today?
?
This passage reveals that a major theological error entered Islam from an external source. What unexamined ideas about Allah have you absorbed from your culture or upbringing? What specific step will you take this week to verify them against the Quran and Sunni scholarship?
?
The Rawafid are accused of adopting doctrines from Jewish Mushabbiha without scrutiny. Are there any Islamic teachings you accept simply because they are common in your community, without verifying their basis in revelation? Make a concrete plan to investigate one such belief this month.

Jewish Qadariyya and Their Islamic Influence
Baqillani describes Jewish Qadariyya and their Islamic counterparts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's account of the Jewish Qadariyya, their denial of the beatific vision and belief in self-created actions, their influence on Islamic Qadariyya, and his warning against crypto-heretics.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya heresy has Jewish roots and is cursed by prophets.

After outlining the first Jewish sect, Baqillani turns to the second: the Qadariyya. They deny seeing Allah in the afterlife and claim that creatures create their own actions. Baqillani then links these Jewish predestinarians to the Qadariyya in Islam, citing a prophetic hadith cursing them. Finally, he warns about contemporary impostors who secretly follow this path while pretending to be from Ahl al-Ra'y.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage for this lesson
The Arabic covers the description of Qadariyya, the hadith, the claim of influence, and the warning about crypto-heretics.
2
Identify the key doctrines of the Jewish Qadariyya
They deny the beatific vision (رؤية) and say that living beings create their own actions (يخلقون أفعالهم).
3
Understand the prophetic condemnation
The Prophet (PBUH) said: 'The Qadariyya are cursed on the tongue of seventy prophets.' Reflect on the severity.
4
Trace the influence on Islamic sects
Baqillani states that the Qadariyya in Islam took their path from the Jewish Qadariyya.
5
Heed the contemporary warning
Baqillani mentions a group in his time who outwardly claim affiliation with Ahl al-Ra'y but secretly harbor heresy and learn from Jews.

Jewish Sects on Abrogation and Prophethood
Baqillani classifies Jewish sects on abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main Jewish sects' positions on abrogation and prophethood, and how they differ on the role of reason versus divine notification.

Core Idea
Jewish sects disagreed on whether abrogation is rationally possible or not.

Imam al-Baqillani begins this chapter by mapping out the Jewish sects' views on abrogation and the possibility of a new prophet. Before engaging in refutation, he presents their positions accurately, distinguishing between those who accept rational permissibility but deny actual occurrence due to scriptural texts, and those who deny rational possibility entirely. This sets the stage for the subsequent discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own classification come through before you interpret.
Notice the two sect names: الشمعنية and العناية.
2
Identify the two sects
The passage names two Jewish sects: the Shamʿaniyya and the ʿInāniyya. Write down their names and note how Baqillani introduces each.
3
Compare their positions on abrogation
The Shamʿaniyya hold that abrogation is rationally permissible but prevented by divine notification in the Torah. The ʿInāniyya hold that abrogation is rationally impossible and revelation confirms this. Compare these two views.
The key difference is whether reason alone allows abrogation.
4
Note the agreement on badāʾ
The passage ends with a consensus (except a minority) that abrogating a command before its fulfillment is badāʾ (a change of divine decision), which they reject.
Badāʾ is a disputed concept; here it is used pejoratively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على اليهود في الأخبار. وقد افترقت اليهود في الأصل على فرقتين : فزعمت الشمعنية نسخ الشرائع وإرسال نبي بعد موسى عليه السلام لنسخ شريعته جائز من طريق العقل، وأنهم إنما منعوا نسخ شريعتهم على يد نبي بعد نبيهم من جهة توقيف الله جل اسمه في التوراة وعلى لسان موسى عليه السلام، أنه لا ينسخها ولا يبعث نبي بتبديلها بألفاظ سنذكر بعضها. وزعمت العناية أن نسخ الشرائع محال من جهة العقل وأن السمع أيضاً قد ورد بتأكيد ما في العقل من ذلك. وأجمعوا إلا فريقاً منهم على أن نسخ الشيء قبل امتثاله ووقت فعله بداء.
Chapter on Discourse Concerning the Jews Regarding the Reports. The Jews originally split into two sects: The Shamʿaniyya claimed that abrogation of laws and sending a prophet after Moses (peace be upon him) to abrogate his law is permissible from the standpoint of reason, and that they only prevented the abrogation of their law at the hands of a prophet after their prophet due to a notification from Allah, glorious is His name, in the Torah and on the tongue of Moses (peace be upon him), that He will not abrogate it nor send a prophet to change it — with wording we will mention some of it. The ʿInāniyya claimed that abrogation of laws is impossible from the standpoint of reason, and that revelation has also come affirming what is in the intellect regarding that. And they all agreed, except a group among them, that abrogating a thing before its fulfillment and the time of its action is badāʾ.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a classification of Jewish sects regarding the issue of abrogation (naskh) of the Mosaic law and the sending of a new prophet. It identifies two main sects: First, the Shamʿaniyya, who hold that abrogation and sending a new prophet are rationally permissible, but they deny its actual occurrence because they claim God explicitly declared in the Torah that the law would not be abrogated — a statement the author promises to quote later. Second, the ʿInāniyya (or ʿAnāniyya), who assert that abrogation is rationally impossible (muḥāl), and they support this with revelation that confirms the rational position. The passage ends by noting a further area of agreement: most of them (except a minority) consider abrogating a command before it has been fulfilled or its time has come to be badāʾ — a term often implying a change of divine decision, which they reject.

Key Terms
اليهود
الشمعنية
العناية
النسخ
البداء
التوقيف
العقل
السمع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some readers think 'العناية' (al-ʿInāniyya) means 'the care' or 'the providence', but it is the proper name of a Jewish sect (related to ʿAnan ben David).
Correction: The term, here written as العناية, is a proper noun referring to a specific sect (likely the ʿAnāniyya). It does not mean 'care' in this context.

Checkpoint
According to the Shamʿaniyya, why is abrogation of the Mosaic law not possible?
A) It is rationally impossible
B) God explicitly stated in the Torah that it will not be abrogated
C) No prophet can come after Moses
D) They do not believe in abrogation at all

Key Takeaway
The Shamʿaniyya and ʿInāniyya represent two different approaches to abrogation: one relying on rational permissibility with scriptural prevention, the other on rational impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Shamʿaniyya admitted that abrogation is rationally possible, yet they denied it because of a scriptural statement. In your own life, do you truly submit to God's decisions even when they seem to contradict your rational expectations? Or do you, like the ʿInāniyya, let your intellect override revelation? What would change if you fully trusted God's wisdom over your own?
?
The passage says most Jews reject badāʾ—that God could change His decree before a command is fulfilled. Have you ever feared that God might change His plan for you, revealing a lack of trust in His perfection? How can this lesson deepen your certainty that God's knowledge is complete and unchanging?
?
The ʿInāniyya claimed abrogation is 'impossible from the standpoint of reason.' When you face a command of Allah that seems difficult or illogical, do you pause and submit, or do you seek to rationalize it away? What would it mean for you to embrace the possibility that His wisdom surpasses your understanding, even if it feels like a 'naskh' of your own plans?

Classification of Jewish Sects on Abrogation and Prophethood
Classification of Jewish sects on abrogation and prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major Jewish sects' positions on the abrogation of the Mosaic law and the continuation of prophethood, and how these positions are grounded in reason and revelation.

Core Idea
Jews split on abrogation: some say rationally permissible but scripturally denied, others say rationally impossible.

Baqillani opens a chapter on Jewish sects to clarify their divisions regarding abrogation (naskh) and prophethood. He identifies two main groups with opposing rational stances, then notes a minority view on punitive abrogation, and finally distinguishes the Samaritans' limited acceptance of prophets. This classification sets the stage for Muslim theological engagement with Jewish objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main sects
Read the opening sentence where Baqillani says Jews split into two sects. Note their names: Sham'aniyya and 'Ananiyya.
2
Contrast their views on abrogation
Compare the Sham'aniyya's claim that abrogation is rationally permissible but prohibited by scriptural notification, with the 'Ananiyya's claim that it is rationally impossible and revelation confirms that.
3
Note the disagreement on abrogation before compliance
Pay attention to the consensus among most Jews except a group that considers abrogation before fulfillment as badā' (change of mind) implying ignorance, and the exception that allows it as punishment.
4
Examine the Samaritan position on prophethood
Read about the Samaritans who accept only Moses, Aaron, and Joshua, rejecting later prophets.
5
Understand the position of the remaining Jews
The rest accept anyone who performs miracles as a prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على اليهود في الأخبار وقد افترقت اليهود في الأصل على فرقتين : فزعمت الشمعنية نسخ الشرائع وإرسال نبي بعد موسى عليه السلام لنسخ شريعته جائز من طريق العقل، وأنهم إنما منعوا نسخ شريعتهم على يد نبي بعد نبيهم من جهة توقيف الله جل اسمه في التوراة وعلى لسان موسى عليه السلام، أنه لا ينسخها ولا يبعث نبي بتبديلها بألفاظ سنذكر بعضها. وزعمت العناية أن نسخ الشرائع محال من جهة العقل وأن السمع أيضاً قد ورد بتأكيد ما في العقل من ذلك. وأجمعوا إلا فريقاً منهم على أن نسخ الشيء قبل امتثاله ووقت فعله بداء ودلالة على الجهل إلا فريقاً منهم فإنهم أجازوا نسخ العبادة بما أغلظ منها وأشق على سبيل العقوبة للمكلف هو وقالت السامرية منهم بنبوة موسى وهارون ويوشع بن نون؛ وأنكرت بنبوة غيرهم من الرسل الذين بعدهم. كسليمان وحزقيل واليسع وغيرهم. وقال الباقون منهم بنبوة كل من ظهرت الأعلام على يده
Chapter: Discourse on the Jews concerning reports. And the Jews originally split into two sects: The Sham'aniyya claimed that abrogation of laws and sending a prophet after Moses, peace be upon him, to abrogate his law is permissible from the way of reason, and that they only forbade abrogation of their law at the hand of a prophet after their prophet by way of a notification from God, majestic is His name, in the Torah and on the tongue of Moses, peace be upon him, that He does not abrogate it nor send a prophet to change it—with words we will mention some of them. And the 'Ananiyya claimed that abrogation of laws is impossible from the way of reason, and that the revealed text also has come confirming what is in the intellect concerning that. And they all agreed, except a group among them, that abrogating a thing before its compliance and the time of its action is a badā' and an indication of ignorance, except a group among them who permitted abrogation of worship by something more severe and more difficult by way of punishment for the obligated person. And the Samaritans among them affirmed the prophethood of Moses, Aaron, and Joshua son of Nun, and denied the prophethood of other messengers who came after them, such as Solomon, Ezekiel, Elisha, and others. And the rest among them affirmed the prophethood of everyone on whose hand miraculous signs appeared.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a classification of Jewish sects concerning the possibility of abrogation (naskh) of the Mosaic law and the sending of prophets after Moses. Baqillani first states that the Jews divided into two main sects: the Sham'aniyya and the 'Ananiyya. The Sham'aniyya held that abrogation and sending a new prophet after Moses is rationally permissible; however, they believed that God had specifically informed them through the Torah and Moses that the Mosaic law would never be abrogated or altered. The 'Ananiyya, on the other hand, considered abrogation rationally impossible, and they claimed that revelation confirms this rational judgment. Then Baqillani notes that all Jewish sects except a small group agreed that abrogating a commandment before it has been fulfilled or before its time is a form of badā' (change of mind in God) and indicates ignorance; this small group allowed abrogation by replacing the command with a more burdensome one as punishment. Finally, Baqillani discusses the Samaritans (al-Samiriyya), who accepted only the prophethood of Moses, Aaron, and Joshua, rejecting all subsequent prophets. The remaining Jews accepted the prophethood of anyone who performed miracles. This passage thus provides a detailed classification of Jewish views on abrogation and prophethood, highlighting the rational and scriptural arguments used by each sect.

Key Terms
الشمعنية
العناية
السامرية
النسخ
البداء
التوقيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Jews hold a unified view on abrogation and prophethood.
Correction: This passage shows that Jews are divided into multiple sects with differing views: Sham'aniyya and 'Ananiyya on abrogation, and Samaritans vs. rest on prophethood.

Checkpoint
Which Jewish sect believed that abrogation of the law is rationally impossible and that revelation confirms this?
A) The Sham'aniyya
B) The 'Ananiyya
C) The Samaritans
D) The rest of the Jews

Key Takeaway
The Jewish sects held divergent views on the possibility of abrogation and the acceptance of prophets, ranging from rational permissibility with scriptural restriction to rational impossibility, with the Samaritans limiting prophethood to only three figures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth from God simply because it clashed with your rational assumptions, like the 'Ananiyya who declared abrogation rationally impossible? Where in your life are you allowing intellectual pride to block you from receiving guidance?
?
The Samaritans limited God's messengers to only three. Are there people or teachings you have rejected without examining the signs God has placed with them? What would it take for you to recognize a genuine call from Him that challenges your comfort zone?
?
The Sham'aniyya accepted abrogation in principle but denied it in practice based on their scripture. Is there a command of God you acknowledge theoretically but resist implementing because it would upend your current lifestyle? What change are you avoiding right now?

Jewish Sects and Their Views on Prophethood
Baqillani categorizes Jewish sects by their stance on prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani categorizes Jewish sects based on their acceptance of prophets.

Core Idea
Jewish sects disagreed sharply on which prophets to accept.

Baqillani begins by mapping out the landscape of Jewish sectarian views on prophethood. Each sect had a different criterion for accepting or rejecting prophets. This sets the stage for his dialectical challenge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three groups
Read the passage and list the three Jewish sects mentioned: Samaritans, the majority, and the 'Isawiyya.
The Samaritans are the most restrictive.
2
Compare their criteria
Note how each group decides who is a prophet. Samaritans accept only Moses, Aaron, Joshua; the majority accept anyone with signs; the 'Isawiyya accept Abu Isa al-Isfahani and Jesus as non-law-changing prophets.
The 'Isawiyya passage contains a contradictory phrase due to manuscript issue.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why Baqillani presents this diversity. It shows that even among Jews there is no consensus, which prepares his argument for needing a universal proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت السامرية منهم بنبوة موسى وهارون ويوشع بن نون؛ وأنكرت بنبوة غيرهم من الرسل الذين بعدهم كسليمان وحزقيل واليسع وغيرهم. وقال الباقون منهم بنبوة كل من ظهرت الأعلام على يده. وزعمت العيسوية منهم أصحاب أبي عيسى أن الأصبهاني وعيسى عليهما السلام نبيان صادقان وأنهما أرسلا إلى قومهما ولم يرسلا بتبديل شريعة موسى. وعيسى عليهما السلام ليسا نبيين وأن الذي محمداً [؟] يرسلا بتبديل شريعة موسى؟ فيقال لهم جميعاً: ما الدليل على إثبات نبوت موسى السلام؟ فإن قالوا ما ظهر على يده من الأعلام المعجزة كفلق البحر وإخراج اليد البيضاء وغير ذلك من أعلامه قيل لهم: وما الدليل على صحة هذه الأعلام وثبوتها مع علمكم بخلاف من يخالف فيها من البراهمة والمجوس والملحدين وأهل التنجيم وغيرهم من الجاحدين؟ فإن قالوا:
And the Samaritans among them affirmed the prophethood of Moses, Aaron, and Joshua son of Nun; and they denied the prophethood of other messengers who came after them, such as Solomon, Ezekiel, Elisha, and others. And the rest of them affirmed the prophethood of everyone upon whose hand signs appeared. And the 'Isawiyya among them, the followers of Abu Isa, claimed that the Isfahani and Jesus, peace be upon them, are two truthful prophets, and that they were sent to their people and were not sent to change the law of Moses. And Jesus, peace be upon them both, are not two prophets? And that which Muhammad [؟] were sent to change the law of Moses? So it is said to all of them: What is the proof for establishing the prophethood of Moses, peace be upon him? If they say: what appeared at his hand of miraculous signs such as the splitting of the sea, the extraction of the white hand, and other signs of his, it is said to them: And what is the proof for the validity and establishment of these signs, given your knowledge of the opposition of those who disagree with them from the Brahmins, Magians, atheists, astrologers, and other deniers? If they say:
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a combined description and dialectical argument. Baqillani first categorizes Jewish sects: (1) Samaritans, who accept only Moses, Aaron, and Joshua as prophets, rejecting all later ones like Solomon, Ezekiel, Elisha; (2) the majority of Jews, who accept any prophet who performs miracles. He then describes the 'Isawiyya sect, who claim that Abu Isa al-Isfahani and Jesus are both true prophets sent without altering Mosaic law, though a contradictory clause follows (likely due to OCR corruption). Baqillani then shifts to a universal kalam challenge: he asks all these groups for the proof of Moses' prophethood. If they cite his miracles (splitting the sea, white hand), Baqillani counters by demanding proof that those miracles are authentic, given that Brahmins, Magians, atheists, and astrologers deny them. This typifies the kalam method of questioning the epistemological basis of religious claims by highlighting disagreement from other traditions. The passage ends mid-sentence at the beginning of their hypothetical response, leaving the argument open.

الأعلام

Correction: This passage shows that Jewish sects like the Samaritans reject many prophets accepted by other Jews, and the 'Isawiyya have their own distinct list.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Samaritans rejected prophets after Joshua simply because they fell outside their tradition. Is there any truth or guidance from God that you have dismissed because it didn't fit your existing beliefs or comfort zone? Ask yourself honestly: what am I closed to, and why?
?
The 'Isawiyya accepted Jesus and al-Isfahani as prophets but refused to let that change the Mosaic law. Have you ever accepted a spiritual insight or a call from God while resisting the change it requires in your life? Where are you holding back from full surrender?
?
The majority of Jews accepted any prophet with signs. When God speaks to you through circumstances, people, or scripture, do you respond to the evidence and obey, or do you rationalize it away? Examine your heart: do you truly want to recognize His messengers, or do you prefer to stay as you are?

The Kalam Challenge: Proving Prophethood Through Miracles
Baqillani poses a dialectical challenge on the proof of Moses' prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's dialectical strategy for challenging the proof of prophecy based on miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles need proof themselves against skeptics.

After describing the divisions among Jewish sects, Baqillani turns to a universal challenge: how can anyone prove that Moses' miracles actually happened? He anticipates that they will cite miracles like the splitting of the sea, but then points out that many groups deny these events. This forces a deeper epistemological question.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the passage from 'فيقال لهم جميعاً' to the end. Notice the back-and-forth structure: Baqillani asks for proof, they offer miracles, he counters by asking for proof of the miracles.
The text ends mid-sentence at 'فإن قالوا:'.
2
Identify the challenge
Baqillani's challenge is that citing miracles is insufficient if the events themselves are contested. He lists several groups that deny these events: Brahmins, Magians, atheists, astrologers, and others.
3
Understand the method
This is a typical kalam method: use the fact of disagreement to push for a more foundational proof. Baqillani is not denying miracles, but demanding a shared epistemological ground.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Symmetrical Refutation of Jewish Objection
Baqillani responds to the objection that not all Jews are anthropomorphists by using a symmetrical argument about Christians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a symmetrical argument to neutralize a Jewish objection about anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
A symmetrical argument turns an objection back on the objector.

Baqillani anticipates a potential Jewish objection: not all Jews are anthropomorphists. Rather than denying it, he uses a clever parallel: not all Christians are trinitarians either. This symmetrically defuses the objection, leaving the opponent with no answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the dialectical flow.
2
Identify the two moves
Notice Baqillani's two-step response: first a parallel 'not all Christians', then a stronger 'all Jews are anthropomorphists'.
The second move counters a potential counter-objection.
3
Understand the dialectical strategy
See how the objection is neutralized by symmetry: the Jew's own logic is applied to Christians, leaving no escape.
This is a classic argumentative technique.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice the final phrase 'لا جواب عن ذلك' (no answer to that). This shows the argument's strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا ليس كل اليهود يقولون ذلك، قيل لهم : ولا كل النصارى يقولون بالتثليث وإثبات النبوة على حد ما تذهب إليه الملكية واليعاقبة والنسطورية ونحن إنما نحتج بقول الموحدة منهم . فإن قالوا ليس في النصارى إلا قائل بالتثليث الذي تحيله العقول قيل لهم : ولا في اليهود إلا قائل بالتشبيه والتجسيم الذي تحيله العقول؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك .
And if they say: Not all Jews say that, it is said to them: And not all Christians say the trinity and affirmation of prophethood in the manner that the Melkites, Jacobites, and Nestorians go to; and we only argue by the statement of the unitarians among them. So if they say: There are no Christians except those who affirm the trinity which the intellects deem impossible, it is said to them: And there are no Jews except those who affirm anthropomorphism and corporealism which the intellects deem impossible; and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical response. The author argues that if the Jews object that not all Jews are anthropomorphists, then not all Christians are trinitarians either; the author only argues with the unitarian Christians. Then if they insist that all Christians are trinitarians, the author counters that all Jews are anthropomorphists. This is a classic argument using symmetry that leaves the Jew with no answer.

Key Terms
تشبيه (tashbih)
تجسيم (tajsim)
تثليث (tathlith)
موحدة (muwahhida)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This is just rhetorical parity and not a serious refutation.
Correction: It is a serious refutation because the Jew cannot escape the logical symmetry; the argument forces a contradiction if the Jew denies the universality.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say when the Jew claims not all Jews are anthropomorphists?
A) He denies it.
B) He retorts that not all Christians are trinitarians.
C) He argues that all Christians are trinitarians.
D) He insists that all Jews are anthropomorphists.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's symmetrical argument demonstrates that a consistent critic must apply the same standard to his own position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you defend your beliefs, do you apply the same logical standards to yourself that you demand of others? In what area of your life are you most likely to be inconsistent, and how does Baqillani's symmetrical argument expose that double standard?
?
Think of a recent disagreement about religion. Did you respond with a symmetrical counter-argument like Baqillani, or did you become defensive? What would it take for you to adopt this calm, logical approach in future debates?

Refuting the Jewish Objection on Forced Transmission
Baqillani refutes the Jewish claim using analogy and the 'Isawiyya example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Jewish claim that Muslim transmission was forced by the sword, using the example of Moses' law and the 'Isawiyya sect.

Core Idea
The charge of forced transmission applies symmetrically, and the 'Isawiyya prove non-compelled transmission.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani addresses a Jewish objection that Muslim transmission of prophetic reports is invalid because it was forced by the sword. He turns the argument back on his opponents by examining the history of Jewish law and introducing the 'Isawiyya, a Christian sect that transmitted the reports of both Muhammad and Jesus without compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the overall argument. Then read the translation. Notice the back-and-forth dialectical structure.
The passage is a refutation, so it contains several objections and replies.
2
Trace the two main counterarguments
Identify how Baqillani first uses Moses' law on apostasy to argue that Jewish ancestors might have been compelled, then introduces the 'Isawiyya as a non-compelled group.
These two prongs together defeat the objection.
3
Reflect on the argument's force
Consider why the 'Isawiyya example is effective: it shows that non-compelled transmission is possible, undermining the claim that all Muslim transmission was forced.
The argument does not deny compulsion entirely but shows it is not universally true.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: أليس موسى عليه السلام كان من دينه وشريعته أن يقتل من ارتد عن دينه وفارق ملته بعد الدخول فيها؟ فإذا قالوا نعم، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن تكونوا محمولين على نقل أعلام موسى بالسيف وأن يكون أسلافكم الذين كانت منهم المنة والرئاسة إنما دخلوا في دين موسى رغبة وحباً لأسباب الدنيا والترأس فيها وضمن لهم ذلك فلما دخلوا في الدين لم يمكنهم الخروج منه خوفاً من القتل فصاروا محمولين على النقل؟ فإن قالوا: لم يكن أسلافنا يحملون الناس على الدخول في الدين وإن حملوهم على المقام عليه بعد الدخول فيه فلم يكونوا لذلك محمولين؛ قيل لهم: وكذلك نحن لا نقتل من دخل في ديننا إذا لم ينقل أعلام نبينا ولا نقتل أيضاً من أدى الجزية وأقام على دينه ولم يدخل في ديننا إذا لم ينقل أعلام نبينا أو كان من أهل العهد والصلح فلم يجز أن يكونوا محمولين على نقل أعلام نبينا عليه السلام. ويقال لهم أيضاً: فيجب صحة نقل أعلام محمد بنقل العيسوية وهم أمة عظيمة لأنها لم تحمل على ذلك بالسيف وكذلك يجب صحة نقل أعلام المسيح عليه السلام لنقلهم ونقل العيسوية لها وهم غير محمولين على النقل بالسيف فإن قالوا: النصارى محمولة على النقل بالسيف قيل لهم: وكذلك أنتم محمولون، وقيل لهم: فالعيسوية غير محمولة على نقل أعلام المسيح فيجب إثبات أعلامه بنقلهم.
Then it is said to them: Was not Moses, peace be upon him, of his religion and law that he would kill whoever apostatized from his religion and left his community after entering it? If they say yes, it is said to them: What prevents you from being compelled in the transmission of the signs of Moses by the sword, and that your ancestors who had authority and leadership entered the religion of Moses out of desire and love for worldly reasons and leadership, and that was guaranteed to them, and when they entered the religion they could not leave it out of fear of death, so they became compelled in transmission? If they say: Our ancestors did not compel people to enter the religion, but rather compelled them to remain in it after entering, so they were not compelled; it is said to them: Likewise, we do not kill those who enter our religion if they do not transmit the signs of our Prophet, nor do we kill those who pay the jizya and remain on their religion and do not enter our religion if they do not transmit the signs of our Prophet, or they are people of covenant and peace, so they cannot be compelled in the transmission of the signs of our Prophet, peace be upon him. And it is also said to them: The validity of the transmission of the signs of Muhammad is necessitated by the transmission of the 'Isawiyya, who are a great nation, because they were not compelled to that by the sword; and likewise the validity of the transmission of the signs of the Messiah, peace be upon him, is necessitated by their transmission and the transmission of the 'Isawiyya of them, and they are not compelled in transmission by the sword. If they say: The Christians are compelled in transmission by the sword, it is said to them: Likewise you are compelled. And it is said to them: The 'Isawiyya are not compelled in the transmission of the signs of the Messiah, so the establishment of his signs is necessitated by their transmission.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Jewish objection. Baqillani begins by asking the Jews whether Moses' law prescribed death for apostasy. If they agree, he then argues that the Jewish ancestors may have entered the religion out of worldly desire and then stayed out of fear, so their transmission could also be considered compelled. When the Jews object that their ancestors did not force entry but only enforced remaining, Baqillani counters that Muslims also do not kill those who enter and then not transmit the Prophet's signs, nor those who pay jizya or have a covenant. He then introduces the 'Isawiyya (a Christian sect?) who transmitted the signs of Muhammad without any compulsion, and likewise the transmission of Jesus' signs is valid because they transmitted them without compulsion. If the Jews claim Christians are compelled, Baqillani turns it back on them. Finally, he concludes that since the 'Isawiyya transmitted without compulsion, their transmission establishes the signs of Jesus.

Key Terms
نقل الأعلام
العيسوية
السيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Muslim transmission of prophetic reports is invalid because it was forced by the sword.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the same charge applies to Jewish transmission if Moses' law is considered, and that the 'Isawiyya transmitted without any compulsion, proving non-forced transmission exists.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of mentioning the 'Isawiyya in Baqillani's argument?
A) To prove that Christians are compelled by the sword
B) To show that a group transmitted without compulsion, supporting the validity of Muslim transmission
C) To argue that the 'Isawiyya are not reliable transmitters
D) To refute the Muslims' own claims

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the forced transmission objection by showing its symmetry with Jewish tradition and by highlighting the 'Isawiyya as a counterexample of non-compelled transmission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an intellectual objection to your faith, do you feel a compulsion to defend it out of fear of being wrong, or can you examine the objection with the same dialectical calmness as Baqillani? What would it take for you to respond with that level of rigor and confidence?
?
Baqillani points out that the 'Isawiyya transmitted their faith freely, without coercion. Are there areas of your own religious practice that are driven more by fear—fear of punishment, social pressure, or being seen as weak—than by genuine conviction? How can you move toward a faith that is transmitted from your heart rather than imposed by circumstances?
?
The Jewish interlocutor accused Muslims of forced transmission, but Baqillani showed that the charge applied equally to them. In your life, do you ever accuse others of faults that you yourself possess? Take a moment to identify one such accusation you have made recently, and consider how you can address it in yourself first.

Refuting the Christian Objection on Forced Transmission
Baqillani responds to objections about forced transmission by turning the argument against Christians and Jews.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Christian charge of forced transmission is self-defeating because Muslims are equally widespread and their transmission also traces back to origins that could be called forced.

Core Idea
If scattered churches disprove forced transmission, scattered mosques do too.

The Christians argued that Muslim transmission was forced by the sword. Baqillani turns the argument around, pointing out that the same could be said for Christians. When they defend themselves by noting their wide geographical spread, Baqillani responds that Muslims are equally widespread—even in Christian lands and captivity—so the objection doesn't hold. He finishes by showing that all transmission ultimately traces back to someone who was or was not forced, making the Christian position inconsistent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Christian objection
Read the opening line where the Christians claim Muslims are compelled to transmit by the sword. Note how Baqillani immediately flips the accusation back on them.
This sets up the argument's structure: a symmetrical response.
2
Examine the Christian defense
The Christians argue they cannot be forced because they are scattered across deserts, mountains, and remote regions. Consider why they think this disproves compulsion.
This is a key premise: widespread presence implies voluntary transmission.
3
Analyze Baqillani's reply
Baqillani counters that Muslims are also widely scattered—in wildernesses, seas, fortresses, and even in Christian territories and captivity—yet they all transmit the Prophet's signs. The same logic that protects Christians applies to Muslims.
Notice the specific locations mentioned (Constantinople, Amorium, Rome) to show Muslim presence under Christian rule.
4
Consider the final rejoinder
The Christians might say these Muslims originally learned from people who were forced. Baqillani retorts that the same is true for Christians and Jews; all their transmission eventually traces back to someone who was compelled or brought by the sword.
This closes the argument by showing the objection is universal, not unique to Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال للنصارى إن قالوا لنا أنتم محمولون على نقلكم بالسيف ما أنكرتم أن تكونوا أيضاً محمولين على نقلكم بالسيف؟ فإن قالوا: النصارى متفرقون في البلاد والمهامه وبطون الأودية ورؤوس الجبال والصوامع وأطراف السند والهند، فكيف يكونون محمولين على النقل بالسيف ولا أحد في هذه البقاع يحملهم؟ قيل لهم ولليهود: وكذلك المسلمون منتشرون في البراري والقفار والبحار والرباطات وأطراف البلاد وفي دار مملكتكم وتحت غلبتكم بقسطنطينية وعمورية ورومية وفي قلاعكم ومطاميركم وفي أسركم منهم خلق عظيم لا يحصي عددهم إلا الله تعالى كلهم ينقلون أعلام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ويدينون بدينه يكون من ذكرناه محمولاً على تصديق محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ونقل أعلامه؟ فإن قالوا جميع من ذكرتم إنما أخذوا النقل في الأصل عن قوم محمولين عليه، قيل لهم: وكذلك جميع من ذكرتموه من النصارى واليهود في سائر الأقطار إنما أخذوا النقل عن قوم محمولين عليه في الأصل أو عمن حمل عليه والجيء إليه بالسيف ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك.
And it is said to the Christians: If they say to us, 'You are compelled in your transmission by the sword,' then what prevents you from also being compelled in your transmission by the sword? If they say, 'The Christians are scattered in the lands, deserts, valleys, mountain tops, monasteries, and the ends of Sind and India, so how can they be compelled in transmission by the sword when no one in these regions compels them?' It is said to them and to the Jews: 'Likewise the Muslims are spread out in the wildernesses, deserts, seas, fortresses, and ends of the lands, and in the domain of your kingdom and under your domination in Constantinople, Amorium, Rome, and in your fortresses and dungeons, and among your captives there is a great creation whose number only Allah knows; all of them transmit the signs of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and practice his religion. Could the one we mentioned be compelled to believe Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and transmit his signs? If they say, 'All those you mentioned only received the transmission originally from people who were compelled,' it is said to them: 'Likewise all those you mentioned among the Christians and Jews in the various regions only received the transmission from people who were compelled originally, or from one who was compelled and brought by the sword.' And they have no answer to that.'
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a response to a Christian objection. The Christians argue that Muslims are forced to transmit by the sword. Baqillani turns the argument around, asking why Christians themselves are not also forced. The Christians then object that Christians are scattered everywhere (deserts, valleys, mountains, etc.) with no one to force them. Baqillani replies that Muslims are also widely spread in wildernesses, seas, fortresses, and even in Christian territories and captivity, yet they all transmit the Prophet's signs and practice his religion. If the Christians counter that these Muslims originally received the transmission from people who were forced, Baqillani retorts that the same applies to Christians and Jews: their transmission also originates from people who were forced or brought by the sword. Thus, the Christians have no valid rebuttal.

Correction: Baqillani does not deny forced transmission; he argues it cuts both ways. The argument is about consistency, not about proving transmission was voluntary.

?

?
The Muslims in Baqillani's argument remain steadfast in transmitting their religion even when scattered and under Christian domination. Are you as consistent in living and sharing your faith when you are in a minority or in difficult circumstances (e.g., at work, school, among non-Muslim friends)? Or does your faith fade when it is inconvenient? Make a plan this week to visibly practice one aspect of Islam in a setting where you are the only Muslim.
?
Baqillani turns the Christian objection into an argument for Islam's truth. Is there a doubt or criticism you have heard about Islam that, upon reflection, actually strengthens your belief when applied consistently? What is it, and how will you use that insight to deepen your conviction?

Refutation of Forced Conversion by the Sword
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that Muslims were compelled by the sword.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani uses dialectical reasoning to refute the claim that Muslims were compelled by the sword to transmit the signs of the Prophet.

Core Idea
If all Muslims were forced, there must be an uncompelled source—so transmission is voluntary.

Imam al-Baqillani takes up a common Christian polemic: that Muslims only believed because they were forced at swordpoint. Rather than simply denying it, he shows that the charge is self-refuting. By turning the same logic back on Christian and Jewish transmission, he demonstrates that no religious tradition could survive if its original transmission were entirely coerced. This passage is a masterclass in jadal (dialectical theology).

Guided Path
1
Read the complete passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage (and its translation) in full to get the overall argument. Notice that Baqillani uses a dialectical style with multiple objections and responses.
The passage is dense, so take your time.
2
Identify the first counter-argument
See how Baqillani mirrors the Christians' claim back at them: if you say we were compelled, then you too were compelled. This is a classic jadal move.
3
Analyze the scattering argument
Baqillani addresses the Christian rebuttal about being scattered by pointing to the similar scattering of Muslims. This shows the argument is symmetrical.
Note the geographical details: Constantinople, Amorium, Rome, etc.
4
Trace the compeller analysis
Baqillani forces the opponent to specify who compelled the Muslims. Each option leads to a contradiction: if voluntary, fine; if by deniers, impossible; if by other Muslims, then there is an original uncompelled group.
This is the heart of the refutation.
5
Understand the tawatur point
Baqillani counters the objection that the uncompelled group might not reach tawatur by pointing out that Jewish transmission also relies on a small initial group.
This completes the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسيح فيجب إثبات أعلامه بنقلهم . ويقال للنصارى إن قالوا لنا أنتم محمولون على نقلكم بالسيف ما أنكرتم أن تكونوا أيضاً محمولين على نقلكم بالسيف؟ فإن قالوا : النصارى مفترقون في البلاد والمهامه وبطون الأودية ورؤوس الجبال والصوامع وأطراف السند والهند ، فكيف يكونون محمولين على النقل بالسيف ولا أحد في هذه البقاع يحملهم؟ قيل لهم ولليهود : وكذلك المسلمون منتشرون في البراري والقفار والبحار والرباطات وأطراف البلاد وفي دار مملكتكم وتحت غلبتكم بقسطنطينية وعمورية ورومية وفي قلاعكم ومطاميركم وفي أسركم منهم خلق عظيم لا يحصي عددهم إلا الله كلهم ينقلون أعلام النبي صلى الله عليهم وسلم ويدينون بدينه فكيف يكون من ذكرنا محمولاً على تصديق محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ونقل أعلامه؟ فإن قالوا جميع من ذكرتم إنما أخذوا النقل في الأصل عن قوم محمولين عليه، قيل لهم : وكذلك جميع من ذكرتموه من النصارى واليهود في سائر الأقطار إنما أخذوا النقل عن قوم محمولين عليه في الأصل أو عمن حمل عليه والجيء إليه بالسيف ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك ثم يقال لهم خبرونا عن الحامل للمسلمين على النقل : أهم الحاملون لأنفسهم أم غيرهم ممن باين ملتهم وكذب نبيهم حملهم على نقل أعلامه بالسيف؟ فإن قالوا غيرهم حملهم مع تكذيبهم لنبيهم تجاهلوا وتركوا قولهم وما توجبه قضية العقل والعادة، وإن قالوا : هم الحاملون لأنفسهم على نقل أعلام نبيهم قيل لهم : فكيف يحمل الحامل نفسه على الشيء إلا من حيث لو آثروا ترك النقل لصاروا إليه وقع؛ فهذا يعود إلى أنهم نقلوا ذلك مختارين للنقل . وإن قالوا : إنما صاروا محمولين على النقل بأن حمل بعضهم بعضاً، يقال لهم : فلا بد أن تكون فيهم فرقة غير محمولة هي لغيرها؛ فإذا قالوا : هو كذلك، قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن تكون أعلام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم صحيحة ثابتة بنقل تلك الطبقة التي هي غير محمولة أصلاً؟ وهذا يبطل تعلقهم بالحمل . وإن قالوا : هذه الفرقة التي ليست بمحمولة يقصر عددها عن عدة من يوجب خبره العلم قيل لهم : وكذلك الأصل في الذين نقلوا أعلام موسى وأخذتم النقل عنهم فرقة يقصر عددها عن عدة من يوجب خبره العلم . فإن قالوا : قد أخبرت اليهود اليوم، وهم أهل تواتر أن سلفهم
The Messiah, so it is necessary to establish his signs by their transmission. And it is said to the Christians: If they say to us, 'You are compelled in your transmission by the sword,' why do you not accept that you also are compelled in your transmission by the sword? If they say: 'The Christians are scattered in the lands, deserts, valleys, mountain peaks, monasteries, and the borders of Sind and Hind, so how can they be compelled in transmission by the sword when there is no one in these regions to compel them?' It is said to them and to the Jews: Likewise, the Muslims are spread in the wildernesses, deserts, seas, frontier posts, borders of lands, in your kingdom, under your domination in Constantinople, Amorium, Rome, in your fortresses and prisons, and among your captives there is a great multitude whose number none but Allah can count, all of them transmitting the signs of the Prophet, may Allah bless them and grant them peace, and adhering to his religion. So how can those we mentioned be compelled to believe in Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and to transmit his signs? If they say: 'All those you mentioned only took the transmission originally from people who were compelled to it,' it is said to them: Likewise, all those you mentioned among the Christians and Jews in various regions only took the transmission either from people who were originally compelled to it or from one who was compelled and brought to it by the sword—and they have no answer to that. Then it is said to them: Inform us concerning the compeller of the Muslims in transmission: are they the compellers of themselves or others who differed from their religion and denied their prophet, compelling them to transmit his signs by the sword? If they say: 'Others compelled them while denying their prophet,' they become ignorant and abandon their own statement and what the judgment of reason and custom necessitates. And if they say: 'They are the compellers of themselves to transmit the signs of their prophet,' it is said to them: How can one compel oneself to a thing except that if they had preferred to abandon transmission, they would have done so? So this goes back to their transmitting that voluntarily. And if they say: 'They only became compelled in transmission because some of them compelled others,' it is said to them: Then necessarily among them there must be a group that is not compelled, which is the compass for the others. If they say: 'So it is,' it is said to them: What prevents you from accepting that the signs of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, are sound and established by the transmission of that class which is not compelled at all? And this invalidates their clinging to compulsion. And if they say: 'That group which is not compelled is insufficient in number to reach the number whose report necessitates knowledge,' it is said to them: Likewise, the original transmitters of the signs of Moses from whom you took the transmission are a group insufficient in number to reach the number whose report necessitates knowledge. If they say: 'The Jews today, who are people of tawatur (massive transmission), have informed us that their predecessors...'
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that Muslims accepted their religion and transmitted its teachings under compulsion by the sword. Imam al-Baqillani employs a dialectical argument (jadal) structured as a series of objections and answers. He begins by turning the accusation back on the Christians: if they claim Muslims were compelled, why do they not admit that their own transmission is also compelled? He then addresses their rebuttal that Christians are too scattered to be compelled, pointing out that Muslims are equally widespread across many regions under Christian control, yet they uniformly transmit the signs of the Prophet. The argument proceeds to analyze the concept of 'compulsion' (haml) itself. Baqillani forces the opponents to identify the compeller: either the Muslims themselves (voluntary) or others who deny their prophet (impossible, since deniers would not enforce propagation). If they claim some Muslims compelled others, this implies an original uncompelled group whose transmission is voluntary and reliable. He then counters the objection that such a group might be too small to yield certain knowledge (tawatur), by noting that the same applies to the transmission of Moses' signs, which the Jews accept. The passage ends mid-sentence as the opponent tries to appeal to the Jewish tawatur today. Throughout, Baqillani demonstrates that the argument from compulsion is self-defeating and cannot undermine the reliable transmission of Islamic miracles.

Key Terms
النقل
السيف
الحامل
الحمل
التواتر
الأعلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the charge of forced conversion is a historical fact that undermines the reliability of Islamic transmission.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the charge is logically incoherent: if all Muslims were forced, there must be an original uncompelled group, making the transmission voluntary and reliable.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's argument, why cannot the Christians claim that Muslims were compelled by the sword in transmitting the signs of the Prophet?
A) Because Muslims are scattered and no one could compel them all
B) Because the Christians themselves admit that their own transmission is not compelled
C) Because if Muslims were compelled, there must be an uncompelled group, which would validate the transmission
D) Because the sword was not used in Islamic history

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument shows that the claim of forced conversion is self-defeating, as it would require an original uncompelled group, making the transmission voluntary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief or practice from your family or community without personally verifying it? How does the argument that transmission must be voluntary challenge you to examine your own faith choices?
?
If you were to encounter someone who claims that Islam spread by the sword, would you be able to refute that claim using the logical structure Baqillani presents? What does your ability or inability to do so reveal about your own understanding of your faith?
?
The argument requires an original group that transmitted voluntarily. Who are the people in your life who have transmitted Islam to you voluntarily? How does their sincerity affect your own commitment to Islam?

Refutation of the 'Isawiyya on Universal Prophethood and Abrogation
Baqillani refutes the 'Isawiyya claiming Muhammad and Jesus were only sent to their own people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's dialectical argument that rejecting the universal mission and abrogation by Muhammad and Jesus leads to an absurd skepticism that undermines all transmitted knowledge about the prophets.

Core Idea
If you accept prophethood, you must accept all prophetic claims, including universal mission and abrogation.

Baqillani engages with the 'Isawiyya, a group that accepted the prophethood of Jesus and Muhammad but denied that their missions were universal or that they abrogated the Mosaic law. He shows that such a position is internally inconsistent and would ultimately destroy the basis of all transmitted knowledge about the prophets. This passage is a classic example of kalam dialectics, using the opponent's own premises against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation, to get the overall argument.
The passage uses a dialectical style with objections and replies.
2
Identify the 'Isawiyya claim
Locate the initial claim that Muhammad and Jesus were only sent to their own people and did not abrogate Moses.
3
Follow Baqillani's first objection
Note his argument: if you accept their prophethood based on their word and miracles, you must accept all their statements, including universal mission and abrogation. Rejecting these would make them liars, destroying prophethood.
4
Examine the 'Isawiyya reply and Baqillani's counter
The 'Isawiyya say the followers are lying, not the prophets. Baqillani responds: if lying is possible for followers in one report, it is possible in all, leading to total skepticism about all transmitted reports (akhbar).
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Both sides agree that total skepticism is absurd, so the 'Isawiyya position is refuted and the Muslim/Christian claim stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على العيسوية منهم الذين يزعمون أن محمداً وعيسى عليهما السلام إنما بعثا إلى قومهما ولم يُبعثا بنسخ شريعة موسى عليه السلام فيقال لهم: إذا أوجبتم تصديق محمد وعيسى عليهما السلام قولهما إنهما نبيان من عند الله فما أنكرتم من وجوب تصديقهما في قولهما إنهما قد بعثا إلى كل أسود وأبيض وأنثى وذكر وبنسخ شريعة موسى وكل صاحب شرع قبلهما؟ فإن كان قد كذبا في هذا القول مع ظهور المعجزات على أيديهما فما أنكرتم أن يكونا كاذبين في سائر أخبارهما وهذا يبطل النبوة جملة؟ فإن قالوا: نحن لا نكذب محمداً وعيسى عليهما السلام في هذا القول لو قالاه لأنهما لو كذبا في بعض ما يخبران به عن الله سبحانه لم يكونا نبيين ولكننا نكذب النصارى والمسلمين في ادعائهم ذلك عليهما فالكذب واقع من ناحية أمتيهما ولم يقع من جهتهما يقال لهم: إذا جاز الكذب على النصارى والمسلمين في هذا الخبر الذي يدعونه على محمد وعيسى عليهما السلام فلم لا يجوز عليهم الكذب في جميع ما نقلوه عنهما وفي نقلهم أعلامهما، ولم لا يجوز مثل ذلك على اليهود أيضاً ونقلة البلدان والسير؟ وهذا يعود إلى إبطال القول بالأخبار جملة وفي إطباقنا وإياهم على فساد ما أدى إلى ذلك دليل على فساد قولهم وصحة قول المسلمين والنصارى في هذا الباب.
Chapter on the discussion with the 'Isawiyya among them, who claim that Muhammad and Jesus, peace be upon them, were only sent to their own people and were not sent to abrogate the law of Moses, peace be upon him. It is said to them: If you deem obligatory the affirming of Muhammad and Jesus, peace be upon them, in their statement that they are two prophets from God, then what prevents you from deeming obligatory the affirming of them in their statement that they were sent to every black and white, female and male, and to abrogate the law of Moses and every possessor of a law before them? For if they had lied in this statement despite the appearance of miracles at their hands, then what prevents you from their being liars in the rest of their reports? And this nullifies prophethood entirely. If they say: We do not call Muhammad and Jesus, peace be upon them, liars in this statement if they had said it, because if they had lied in some of what they report about God, Exalted is He, they would not be prophets; but we call the Christians and Muslims liars in their claim of that upon them, so the lying occurs from the side of their two communities and does not occur from their side. It is said to them: If lying is permitted against the Christians and Muslims in this report which they claim upon Muhammad and Jesus, peace be upon them, then why is lying not permitted against them in all that they have transmitted from them and in their transmission of their signs? And why is the like of that not permitted also against the Jews and the transmitters of countries and biographies? And this leads to the invalidation of the acceptance of reports entirely. And in our agreement and theirs upon the corruption of what leads to that is evidence of the corruption of their statement and the correctness of the statement of the Muslims and Christians in this matter.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the 'Isawiyya, a group that believed Muhammad and Jesus were only sent to their own people and did not abrogate the Mosaic law. Baqillani presents a dialectical argument. He first states their claim, then poses a dilemma: If you accept the prophethood of Muhammad and Jesus based on their own testimony and miracles, you must also accept their testimony that they were sent universally and abrogated previous laws. If you deny that testimony, you could deny any of their reports, which would destroy the basis of prophethood. When the 'Isawiyya respond that they trust the prophets but accuse their followers (Christians and Muslims) of lying about the universal message, Baqillani counters that if lying is possible for the followers in this report, then it is possible in all transmissions from the prophets, including the transmission of miracles and signs. This would also apply to Jews and all transmitters of history, leading to complete skepticism about all transmitted reports (akhbar). Since both sides agree that such skepticism is absurd, the 'Isawiyya position is refuted and the Muslim/Christian claim is validated.

Key Terms
العيسوية
نسخ شريعة موسى
النبوة
المعجزات
الأخبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accepting prophethood does not require accepting all prophetic statements.
Correction: Baqillani argues that since prophethood is established by the prophets' own claim and miracles, rejecting any of their statements would undermine the evidence for their prophethood entirely.

Checkpoint
What is the main consequence Baqillani draws if the 'Isawiyya claim that the followers of Muhammad and Jesus are lying about the universal mission?
A) It proves the followers are truthful.
B) It could lead to rejecting all transmitted reports about the prophets.
C) It shows the prophets themselves were liars.
D) It has no consequence.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that denying the universal mission of Muhammad and Jesus leads to an absurd skepticism that undermines all transmitted knowledge about prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The 'Isawiyya claimed to believe in the prophets but rejected parts of their message by blaming the transmitters. Is there any command of Allah that you accept in theory but neglect in practice, perhaps by doubting its authenticity or applicability? Which one, and what will you do today to correct that?
?
Baqillani argues that if you accept the truthfulness of the prophets based on miracles, you must accept all their reports. Have you ever selectively accepted only those prophetic teachings that suit your desires while ignoring others? How has that selective acceptance affected your relationship with Allah? Will you commit to submitting to the full message?
?
The argument against the 'Isawiyya hinges on the absurdity of total skepticism. Yet in your daily life, do you allow doubts about the reliability of Islamic teachings to creep in, perhaps because of modern skepticism? Reflect on one such doubt and examine whether it leads to the same absurdity. What step can you take to strengthen your certainty in the transmitted message?

Refutation of the Khurramdaniyya Using the Hadith 'No Prophet After Me'
Baqillani refutes the Khurramdaniyya using the hadith 'No prophet after me'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the Khurramdaniyya by presenting a logical dilemma based on the universally transmitted hadith that there is no prophet after Muhammad.

Core Idea
The hadith 'No prophet after me' forces a choice that undermines the Khurramdaniyya belief.

Imam Baqillani tackles a sect that believed in continuous prophets after Muhammad. He uses a universally accepted hadith and presents a dilemma: either accept the hadith and reject their claim, or deny its authenticity and risk undermining all prophetic transmissions. This passage demonstrates how a single authentic narration can dismantle an entire theological system.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Khurramdaniyya belief
The Khurramdaniyya believe in a continuous succession of messengers (tawatur al-rusul) after Prophet Muhammad. Recognize what they claim to prepare for the refutation.
This sect is not well-known; focus on Baqillani's argument.
2
Identify the key hadith
Baqillani cites the widely transmitted hadith 'La nabiyya ba'di' (No prophet after me). Note that he emphasizes the hadith is emphatic and intended for perpetual negation.
The hadith is accepted by all Muslims, including the opponents of the Khurramdaniyya.
3
Follow the dilemma
Baqillani asks: Are the Muslims who transmitted this hadith truthful or liars? This forces the Khurramdaniyya to choose one of two options.
4
See the consequences
If truthful, then no prophet after Muhammad (contradicts their belief). If liars, then all transmissions (including their own) could be false, destroying their religion's foundation.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Reflect on the logical structure
Observe how Baqillani uses a single, universally accepted premise to force a conclusion that invalidates the opposing view entirely.
This is a classic kalam argumentative technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك أيضاً يقال للخرمذانية الذين يقولون بتواتر الرسل: أليس قد نقل من خالفكم من كافة المسلمين عن نبيهم أنه قال: «لا نبي بعدي»، وأنه أكد ذلك وقرنه بما علموا به ضرورة قصده إلى نفي على التأبيد وعلى كل حال؟ فإذا قالوا: أجل قيل لهم: فهل عندكم صادقون في نقلهم ذلك أم كاذبون؟ فإن قالوا: هم صادقون أبطلوا إثبات نبوة أحد بعد محمد صلى الله عليه، وإن قالوا: قد كذبوا في هذه الدعوى عليه قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أيضاً من أن تكونوا كاذبين في نقل أعلامه وما أنكرتم من جواز الكذب على اليهود والنصارى وسائر نقلة الأعلام؟ وإن جاز هذا جاز أيضاً عليكم الكذب في نقلكم أعلام كل نبي أثبتم نبوته وبطل أصل دينكم ولا جواب لهم عن شيء من ذلك.
And likewise also it is said to the Khurramdaniyya, who say regarding the successive transmission of messengers: Has not been transmitted by those who oppose you from all the Muslims from their prophet that he said: 'There is no prophet after me', and that he emphasized that and coupled it with what they knew necessarily that his intent was negation forever and in every case? And if they say: Yes, it is said to them: Are they in your view truthful in their transmission of that or liars? For if they say: They are truthful, they invalidate the affirmation of prophethood of anyone after Muhammad, may God bless him. And if they say: They have lied in this claim upon him, it is said to them: What prevents you also from being liars in the transmission of his signs, and what prevents you from the permissibility of lying against the Jews and Christians and all transmitters of signs? And if this is permissible, then lying is also permissible against you in your transmission of the signs of every prophet whose prophethood you affirm, and the foundation of your religion becomes invalid. And they have no answer to any of that.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Khurramdaniyya, a sect that believed in a continuous succession of messengers (tawatur al-rusul). Baqillani employs an argument based on the universally transmitted hadith 'La nabiyya ba'di' (No prophet after me). He first establishes that this hadith is transmitted by all Muslims, including those who oppose the Khurramdaniyya, and that it clearly indicates perpetual negation of prophethood after Muhammad. He then presents a dilemma: If the Khurramdaniyya accept that the Muslims are truthful in transmitting this hadith, then they must accept that there is no prophet after Muhammad, which contradicts their belief. If they claim the Muslims are lying in this transmission, then why should they trust any transmission from Muslims or others? This would imply that their own transmissions of miracles and signs of previous prophets could also be false, thus destroying the very foundation of their religion. Baqillani concludes that they have no answer.

التأبيد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Khurramdaniyya could argue that the hadith is not universally transmitted, thus escaping the dilemma.
Correction: Baqillani assumes the hadith is universally accepted among Muslims to force a logical choice; the strength of the argument lies in the widespread acknowledgment of the hadith.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'No prophet after me' is used as a decisive proof against any claim of prophethood after Muhammad.

?
The Khurramdaniyya's error began with doubting a mass-transmitted truth. Is there any foundational belief of Islam that you have allowed yourself to doubt or question without legitimate scholarly basis? How might that doubt, if left unchecked, erode your entire faith?
