A Heretic Who Denied Quranic Miracles and Died Drunk
Baqillani recounts the heresy and shameful death of a denier of Quranic miracles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical example of a heretic who denied the miraculous nature of the Quran and the consensus of Islamic sects in declaring him an unbeliever.

Core Idea
Denying the Quran's miracle leads to heresy and a shameful end.

This passage from Imam Baqillani's Tamhid al-Awa'il recounts the scandalous life and death of a heretic who not only denied the Quran's miraculous composition but also all other miracles. The narrative serves as a powerful warning about the consequences of rejecting divine signs and the consensus of the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice the progression from his heresy to his immoral life to his death.
Pay attention to the poetic lines at the end.
2
Identify the key elements of his heresy
He denied the Quranic miracle and secretly adhered to Brahmin doctrine that rejects all prophets.
3
Reflect on the community's response
All Islamic sects, including early Mu'tazilites, declared him an unbeliever. Consider why this consensus is significant.
This highlights the importance of belief in miracles in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فضائحه قوله: في القرآن أنه لا معجز في نظمه وسائر المعجزات وإن وردت النصوص في ذلك وكان في الباطن يميل إلى مذهب البراهمة الذين ينكرون جميع الأنبياء وغير الأنبياء وغير ذلك من مصادر التشريع وكان سيرته الفسق والفجور وكان عاقبته أنه مات سكران وكان قد قال صفة حاله: ما زلت آخذ روح الزق في لطف واستبيح دماً من غير مذبوح حتى انثنيت ولي روحان في بدن والزق مطرح جسم بلا روح وكان آخر كلامه وما ختم به عمره أنه كان يده في قدح وهو على علية فأنشأ يقول: أشرب على طرب وقل عهود هو عليك يكون ما هو كائن فلما تكلم بهذا الكلام سقط من تلك العلية ومات بإذن الله تعالى في حدود سنة 231 وفرق الإسلام كلهم يكفرونه وأسلاف المعتزلة أيضاً.
Among his scandals is his saying: Regarding the Qur'an, it has no miracle in its composition and all other miracles, even though texts have come about that, and inwardly he inclined to the doctrine of the Brahmins who deny all prophets and non-prophets and other sources of legislation; and his conduct was immorality and debauchery, and his end was that he died drunk. He had described his state: I kept taking the soul of the wine-skin gently and I permit blood without a sacrificial animal until I turned back with two souls in one body, and the wine-skin is cast off, a body without a soul. His last words and that with which he sealed his life: He had his hand in a cup while he was on a roof, and he recited: I drink with joy and say what covenants? It is upon you; what will be, will be. When he spoke these words, he fell from that roof and died by the permission of God, exalted, in the year 231. All sects of Islam declare him an unbeliever, and also the predecessors of the Mu'tazila.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage describes a heretic who denied that the Qur'an is miraculous in its composition and denied all other miracles, secretly adhering to Brahmin doctrine that rejects all prophets. His life was immoral, and he died drunk after reciting boastful poetry, falling from a roof. The author notes that all Islamic sects, including early Mu'tazilites, declare him an unbeliever. This serves as a historical example of the consequences of heresy.

Key Terms

Nazzam's Doctrine of the Prophet's Invisible Spirit
Reports Nazzam's doctrine that only the Prophet's body was seen, not his spirit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilī thinker al-Naẓẓām's view that the Prophet Muḥammad is essentially an invisible spirit, and that his visible body is merely a container.

Core Idea
For Nazzam, the real Prophet is the unseen spirit, not the visible body.

This lesson explores a provocative doctrine from the Mu'tazilī scholar Ibrāhīm al-Naẓẓām. He argued that the Prophet Muḥammad was never truly seen by anyone, because his essence is an invisible spirit housed within a physical body. This distinction challenged traditional views of prophetic visibility and has implications for how we understand companionship and testimony.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without translation, focusing on the key terms 'الروح' and 'الشخص الظاهر'.
Notice the contrast between the seen container and the unseen reality.
2
Understand Nazzam's claim
From the translation, identify that Nazzam asserts that only the Prophet's 'container' (body) was seen, not his true self (spirit).
The phrase 'ظرفه الذي هو الشخص الظاهر' clarifies what is visible.
3
Consider the implications
Reflect on why this doctrine matters: it would mean no companion ever directly saw the Prophet, undermining the reliability of eyewitness testimony about him.
This contradicts mainstream Islamic belief.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you grasp the distinction between spirit and body in Nazzam's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم النظام أن النبي صلّى الله عليه لم يره أحد قط ولا شاهده، وإنما شوهد ظرفه الذي هو الشخص الظاهر. لأن النبي صلّى الله عليه إنما هو الروح وراء الجسم الظاهر .
And al-Naẓẓām claimed that no one ever saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor witnessed him, but rather only his container, which is the visible person, was seen. Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, is only the spirit behind the visible body.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage records a doctrine of the Mu'tazilī thinker Ibrāhīm al-Naẓẓām. He asserts that the true identity of the Prophet Muḥammad is his spirit (rūḥ), which is invisible, while his physical body is merely a container (ẓarf) or persona (shakhṣ ẓāhir). Consequently, no human ever directly observed the Prophet; they only saw his bodily form. This distinction undermines the traditional understanding of the companions' direct companionship with the Prophet and has implications for the reliability of testimony and prophetic miracles.

Key Terms

Correction: The passage clearly states that the visible body is the 'container' (ẓarf) of the spirit; Nazzam does not deny the body, only that it constitutes the true person.

Be specific about one relationship.
?

Jubba'i's Ruling on an Oath Conditioned by 'Insha' Allah'
Jubba'i's ruling on conditioned oath and when it is broken.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Jubbā'ī's controversial ruling on oaths conditioned by 'in shā'a Allāh' and why it contradicts Sunni consensus.

Core Idea
For Jubba'i, a conditioned oath is broken if Allah clearly wills the action.

This passage presents a unique and controversial opinion from the Mu'tazilī scholar Abū 'Alī al-Jubbā'ī. He tackles a specific legal case: an oath conditioned by 'in shā'a Allāh'. Normally, this phrase protects the oath from being broken, but al-Jubbā'ī argues that if Allah's will regarding the action is evident, the oath is still binding. The author of the Tamhīd records this view to refute it, highlighting the Sunni consensus against such reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English to grasp the literal claim.
2
Understand the scenario
The oath is 'I will give Zayd his right tomorrow, if Allah wills'. Normally this condition prevents oath-breaking.
3
Identify Jubba'i's argument
He says if Allah has willed the payment (as per justice), then failure to act breaks the oath.
4
Note the consequence
Expiation (kaffāra) becomes obligatory, which contradicts the community's consensus.
5
Reflect on the theological basis
Jubba'i's view stems from his belief that Allah's will is always effective and knowable through moral law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم الجبائي أن حالفاً، لو حلف بالله ليعطيَنَّ زيداً حقه غداً إن شاء الله ، ثم جاء الغد ولم يُعْطِه مع التمكّن منه كان حانثاً. لأن الله تعالى قد شاء أن يدفع إليه الحق وكره مطله، وأن الكفارة تلزمه خلافاً للأمة وتقحماً لمشاقتها .
And al-Jubbā'ī claimed that if a person swore by Allah, 'I will definitely give Zayd his right tomorrow, if Allah wills,' then the morrow came and he did not give it, despite being able to do so, he would be an oath-breaker. Because Allah, exalted, had willed that the right be paid to him and disliked its delay, and that expiation is obligatory for him, contrary to the community and an advance into its difficulties.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage records a legal-theological opinion of the Mu'tazilī scholar Abū 'Alī al-Jubbā'ī. He considers a situation where someone makes an oath with the conditional phrase 'in shā'a Allāh' (if Allah wills). Normally, such a phrase prevents the oath from being broken if the condition is not met, because the condition is attached to the will of Allah, which is unknown. However, al-Jubbā'ī argues that if Allah has actually willed the action (the payment of the debt) and has revealed that will through His wisdom (knowing that the debt is just and delay is disliked), then the oath is broken if the person fails to act, even with the conditional phrase. He adds that expiation (kaffāra) then becomes obligatory, which contradicts the consensus (umma) and imposes hardship. The author of the Tamhīd rejects this view, noting that it is a deviant departure from Sunni consensus.

Key Terms
الجـبائي
الحلف
إن شاء الله
الحانث
الكفارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jubba'i is denying the validity of 'in sha'a Allah' as a protective phrase.
Correction: He is not denying its validity; he is interpreting it based on his belief that Allah's will is always effective and knowable through the moral law.

Checkpoint
According to al-Jubbā'ī, when does the oath become broken despite the conditional 'in shā'a Allāh'?
A) When the person forgets
B) When Allah has willed the action and the person fails to perform it while able
C) When the person intends to break it
D) When the debtor does not believe in Allah

Key Takeaway
Al-Jubbā'ī's opinion that a conditioned oath is broken if Allah's will for the action is known directly contradicts the Sunni consensus on the protective function of 'in shā'a Allāh'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'insha Allah' in your daily conversations, do you truly acknowledge that the outcome depends entirely on Allah's will, or has it become a mere cultural phrase? What would change if you meant it every time?
?
Al-Jubba'i argued that failing to fulfill an oath conditioned by 'insha Allah' still makes one an oath-breaker if Allah clearly wills the action. Do you treat your oaths and promises with such seriousness, knowing that Allah's will is involved? How often do you break promises thinking a simple 'insha Allah' excuses you?

The Claim of Creating Like Allah Refuted
Refutation of human creation claim with three Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic refutation of the claim that humans create actions comparable to Allah's creation.

Core Idea
No one creates besides Allah; claiming otherwise is shirk.

This passage confronts a serious theological claim: that human beings are true creators of their own actions. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, presents the view of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya, then refutes it decisively with three Quranic verses. Understanding this refutation is key to preserving tawhid in action and causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim and its accusation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Baqillani presents the opponents' claim and immediately labels it as making partners with Allah.
The phrase 'يخلقون كخلق الله' is the central claim being refuted.
2
Examine the first Quranic verse
Verse 13:16 from Surah al-Ra'd challenges the idea that any partner of Allah could create something similar to His creation.
3
Examine the second verse
Verse 16:20 from Surah al-Nahl states that those invoked besides Allah create nothing and are themselves created.
4
Examine the third verse
Verse 35:3 from Surah Fatir asks rhetorically: 'Is there any creator other than Allah?' This is a definitive negation.
5
Understand the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that the Quran explicitly declares the opponents liars in their claim of a creator besides Allah.
This reinforces the absolute uniqueness of Allah's creative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعموا بأسرهم أنهم يخلقون كخلق الله عزّ وجلّ ويصنعون كصنعه من الحركات والسكون والإرادات والعلوم موافقة منهم لمن جعل معه شريكاً يخلق كخلقه قال الله تعالى : أم جعلوا الله شركاء خلقوا كخلقه فتشابه الخلق عليهم . وقال تعالى : والذين يدعون من دون الله لا يخلقون شيئاً وهم يخلقون وقال : هل من خالق غير الله ؟ فنص على تكذيبهم في ادعائهم خالقاً غيره .
And they all claimed that they create like the creation of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and make like His making, of movements, stillnesses, wills, and knowledges, in agreement with the one who has made with Him a partner who creates like His creation. Allah Most High said: 'Or have they associated partners with Allah who create like His creation so that the creation appears similar to them?' And He said: 'And those whom they invoke besides Allah create nothing, while they are themselves created.' And He said: 'Is there any creator other than Allah?' So He declared them liars in their claim of a creator other than Him.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a polemic against those (likely the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya) who assert that human beings are true creators (khāliqūn) of their own actions—movements, stillness, wills, and knowledge—in a manner parallel to Allah's own creation. The author accuses them of making themselves partners with Allah in creating. He then adduces three Quranic verses to refute this claim: (1) Sūrat al-Ra'd 13:16 challenges the idea that Allah's partners could create anything comparable to His creation; (2) Sūrat al-Naḥl 16:20 states that those called upon besides Allah cannot create, while they themselves are created; (3) Sūrat Fāṭir 35:3 asks rhetorically if there is any creator besides Allah. The conclusion is that the Quran explicitly denies the existence of any other creator, thus refuting the opponents' claim.

Key Terms
يخلقون
كخلق الله
الحركات والسكون
الإرادات
العلوم
خلقوا كخلقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans are true creators of their own actions, separate from Allah's creation.
Correction: Allah is the sole creator; any claim of a creator besides Him is shirk and refuted by the Quran.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the author use to argue that those invoked besides Allah create nothing?
A) سورة الرعد 13:16
B) سورة النحل 16:20
C) سورة فاطر 35:3
D) سورة الزمر 39:62

Key Takeaway
Only Allah creates; claiming human creation like His is shirk and refuted by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt pride in your own knowledge or abilities as if you originated them? This lesson declares that claiming any creation besides Allah is shirk. Examine a recent decision you made—did you attribute its creation to yourself or to Allah? How would you reorient your mindset to see Allah as the sole creator even of your own actions?
?
The opponents claimed to create movements, stillness, wills, and knowledge. In your daily life, is there any area—your career, relationships, even your prayers—where you subtly act as if you are a creator alongside Allah? What would it mean to truly believe that Allah alone creates everything, and how would that change your attitude towards your own efforts?
?
This lesson forces you to check every source of power or action you think you have. Could there be any part of your life where you rely on your own creation instead of Allah's? What is one specific habit you can change today to affirm that Allah is the only creator?

The Claim of Exhausted Divine Goodness
Reports a Mu'tazilī doctrine limiting divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilī doctrine that Allah has done the utmost good for His servants and the theological implications of limiting divine power.

Core Idea
Allah's power is not exhausted; He can always do more than He has done.

This lesson examines a controversial Mu'tazilī stance reported by Imam al-Baqillani. The Baghdadis and al-Naẓẓām claimed that Allah has already bestowed the maximum possible benefit (ṣalāḥ) upon His servants, leaving no room for additional good. This directly challenges the Sunni understanding of divine omnipotence and generosity. Let's explore the text and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice how the claim is framed: 'the Pre-Eternal has set right His servants to the utmost extent of the good He is capable of.'
The term 'al-Qadīm' refers to Allah as the Eternal.
2
Identify the key assertion
Pinpoint the core claim: that there is no good in Allah's treasuries or dominion beyond what He has already given. This implies He cannot do more.
3
Understand the implication
Reflect on the theological consequence: if true, Allah's power would be limited, contradicting the Sunni belief in infinite divine capability.
4
Consider the refutation
The author, Imam al-Baqillani, presents this as a heretical view. Think about why this is problematic from an Ashʿarī perspective.
This passage is a report of a deviant opinion, not an endorsement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم البغداديون منهم، والنظام من البصريين أيضاً، أن القديم سبحانه قد استصلح عباده بغاية ما يقدر عليه من الصلاح، وأنه ليس في خزائنه ولا في سلطانه ولا يُتوهّم منه صلاح يقدر عليه أكثر مما قد استصلحهم به في دينهم ودنياهم .
And the Baghdadis among them, and al-Naẓẓām of the Basrans as well, claimed that the Pre-Eternal, glorified, has set right His servants to the utmost extent of the good He is capable of, and that there is not in His treasuries nor in His dominion, nor can one imagine from Him, good which He is capable of more than what He has already set them right with, in their religion and their worldly life.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a theological stance attributed to the Baghdad Mu'tazila (followers of Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir) and to al-Naẓẓām among the Basrans. They assert that Allah (described here as 'al-Qadīm', the Pre-Eternal) has already bestowed upon His servants the maximum possible benefit (ṣalāḥ) in both religious and worldly affairs. They further claim that Allah's treasuries and dominion contain nothing more, nor can any additional good be conceived, that exceeds what has already been granted. This implies that Allah's power is limited (finite), and that He cannot do more than what He has done. This doctrine is a form of the Mu'tazilī principle of 'al-ṣalāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ' (the good and the better), but taken to an extreme where Allah's power is exhausted.

Key Terms
البغداديون
النظام
القديم
استصلح
بغاية ما يقدر
صلاح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the opponents are simply affirming Allah's generosity, but the actual claim limits His power.
Correction: The passage explicitly says Allah has no more good He is capable of, making it a statement about divine power, not just generosity.

Checkpoint
What do the Baghdadis and al-Naẓẓām claim about Allah's power to grant good?
A) He can always grant more
B) He has exhausted all possible good
C) He never grants any good
D) Good is not from Allah

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilī claim that Allah has exhausted all possible good is a direct challenge to the Sunni doctrine of divine omnipotence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that Allah has given you all the good He can, and that there is no more hope for improvement in your life? How does this passage challenge that feeling of hopelessness? This week, when a situation seems 'maxed out,' pause and ask: 'Is my heart limiting Allah's power?'
?
When you look at your sins and mistakes, do you unconsciously assume that Allah's mercy and power to forgive are limited? In what specific area of your life do you need to expand your trust in His infinite ability to forgive and restore? Write down one such area and commit to calling upon Him with the name 'al-Qadīr' (the All-Powerful) daily.
?
If you truly believed that Allah's treasuries are never exhausted and He can always give more, how would you change the way you pray? Would you pray with more boldness and expectation? Identify one prayer you have been hesitant to make for fear it is too much, and make it today.

Basrans Limit Divine Power to Religion Only
Reports a sectarian doctrine with a paradoxical conclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Basran Mu'tazila's specific claim that Allah's power is finite only in the realm of religion and the paradoxical statement that follows.

Core Idea
The Basrans limit Allah's power to making the best religion—but that creates a logical puzzle.

The Basran Mu'tazila took a more cautious position than their Baghdad counterparts: they confined the limitation of Allah's power to religious guidance alone. Yet, as we will see, this position leads to an internal contradiction that the author highlights.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal English translation. Note the key terms and the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the Basran claim
The Basrans assert that Allah has set right His servants to the utmost good in religion only. Highlight the phrase 'في باب دينهم خاصة'.
This is a restriction compared to other Mu'tazila who applied it to all affairs.
3
Understand the consequence
They conclude that Allah's power is finite (تناهي مقدوراته). Ask yourself: why does this follow from their claim?
4
Examine the paradoxical sentence
Read the final sentence carefully: 'He is capable of a good the likes of which He is not capable, nor of increase over it.' This seems contradictory. Reflect on what it might mean.
The commentary suggests this may be a criticism by the author showing inconsistency.
5
Connect to broader theology
Compare this view with the Sunni position that Allah's power is absolute and unlimited. Consider why the Basran position is problematic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم البصريون منهم خاصةً أنه تعالى قد استصلح عباده بغاية ما في قدرته من الصلاح في باب دينهم خاصةً، وأنه لا يقدر على صلاح لهم في باب الدين أصلح مما فعله بهم فأوجبوا جميعاً تناهي مقدوراته، وأنه يقدر على صلاح لا يقدر على مثله ولا على الزيادة عليه .
And the Basrans among them specifically claimed that He, exalted, has set right His servants to the utmost extent of the good in His power, in the matter of their religion specifically, and that He is not capable of good for them in the matter of religion more beneficial than what He has done for them. So they all affirmed the finitude of His power, and that He is capable of a good the likes of which He is not capable, nor of increase over it.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage records a more restricted version of the previous doctrine, attributed specifically to the Basran Mu'tazila (followers of Abū al-Hudhayl and others). Unlike the Baghdadis and al-Naẓẓām, who applied the limitation to both worldly and religious life, the Basrans confine it to the religious domain (bāb dīnihim). They assert that Allah has given the best possible religion to His servants and cannot produce a better one. Consequently, they all (presumably both schools) affirm the finitude of Allah's power (tanāhī maqdūrātihi). The final clause is paradoxical: 'He is capable of a good the likes of which He is not capable, nor of increase over it' – this may reflect a theological puzzle or be a criticism by the author indicating the inconsistency of the Basran position.

Key Terms
البصريون
استصلح
باب الدين
تناهي مقدوراته
أصلح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Basrans deny Allah's power absolutely.
Correction: The Basrans only deny Allah's ability to improve upon the religion He actually prescribed; they do not deny His power in other matters.

Checkpoint
In what domain do the Basrans limit Allah's power?
A) Worldly affairs
B) Both worldly and religious
C) Religion only
D) Nowhere

Key Takeaway
The Basran Mu'tazila's attempt to limit divine power to religious matters results in a paradoxical statement that undermines their position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Basrans claimed Allah cannot do better than the religion He gave, do you ever find yourself wishing for a different decree or a different guidance? What does that reveal about your stance toward Allah's power?
?
The Basrans' logic led to a contradiction. Are there areas in your life where you try to limit Allah's power to fit your understanding—perhaps in how you think He should have created the world or revealed guidance? Where might you be falling into a similar trap?
?
How does the belief that Allah has done the utmost good for you in religion affect your satisfaction with Islam as a complete way of life? Are there aspects you secretly wish were different, and what does that say about your trust in His power?

Mu'tazilite Doctrine on Eternal Punishment for Grave Sinners
Baqillani states the Mu'tazilite position on eternal punishment for grave sinners and their rejection of Quranic verses on good deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite belief that a Muslim who dies persisting in a major sin will be eternally punished and that good deeds are nullified, and how this contradicts Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites denied that good deeds can erase major sins.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents the Mu'tazilite view on grave sins. They held that even a believing Muslim who performs many good deeds will be eternally punished if he dies without repenting from a major sin. This radical position rejects the Quranic promise that good deeds wipe out evil deeds. Let us examine their claims and the verses they oppose.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite claim
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning up to the mention of the verses. Notice how they assert that a Muslim who commits a major sin and dies unrepentant will be eternally punished, and that Allah nullifies all his good deeds.
They even consider a small sin like drinking a sip of wine sufficient for eternal punishment.
2
Identify the Quranic verses rejected
The passage then lists several Quranic verses that the Mu'tazilites reject in their literal sense. Find each verse and understand how it supports the Sunni position that good deeds can erase sins.
These verses include Hūd 11:114, al-Naml 27:89, al-Anʿām 6:160, and Āl ʿImrān 3:195.
3
Reflect on the nullification of reward
Consider the Mu'tazilite logic: they claim that a single sin can nullify the reward of tawhid, prayers, and all acts of obedience. Ask yourself how this differs from the Sunni understanding of divine mercy and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا كلهم بتخليد كل من اقترف كبيرةً ومات مُصرّاً عليها، وإن كان مسلماً موحداً مصدّقاً الله تعالى ولرسوله عليه السلام ولجميع من عنده عالماً بأن ما ركبه حرام محظور؛ فإن الله يبطل بذلك ثواب توحيده وتصديقه وصلواته وسائر طاعاته ولا يثيبه على شيء أمره بِفِعْلِه فَفَعَلَهُ، بل يأخذه بالذنب الواحد الذي هو شرب جرعة من خمر أو منع خمسة دراهم من الزكاة الواجبة في ماله أو غصب عشرة دراهم، على حسب اختلافهم في الوعيد ردّاً لقوله : إن الحسنات يذهبن السيئات، وقوله تعالى : من جاء بالحسنة فله خير منها، وقوله تعالي : من جاء بالحسنة فله عشر أمثالها وقوله تعالى: أني لا أضيع عمل عامل منكم من ذكر أو أنثى، في نظائر لهذه الآيات. واتفقوا بأسرهم على أنه لا شفاعة للنبي صلّى الله عليه في أحد يستحق أقلّ العقاب في الآخرة، وأنه إن سأل الله تعالى لم يقبل شفاعته ولم يُجِب مسألته . ولو تتبعتُ ذكر ضلالتهم وقبح مذاهبهم وشنيع ما أدخلوا في الدين وخالفوا به توقيف السنن وقول كافة المسلمين وسائر السلف الصالحين، لطال بذلك الكتاب ولخرجنا بذكره عما له قصدنا، ولم نأت مع الإسهاب فيه إلا على القليل منه . وإنما ذكرت طرفاً من ذلك لسيدنا الأمير أطال الله بقاءه ليعرف مفارقتهم للدين وعدولهم عن السبيل، وأنهم أضر فرقة على هذه الأمة وأشدها جراءة على الله عزّ وجلّ فإلى الله المشتكى وإليه نرغب في كشف البلوى ثم رجع بنا القول إلى إثبات صفات الله تعالى لذاته .
And they all said that everyone who commits a major sin (kabīra) and dies persisting in it is eternally [in Hell], even if he is a Muslim, a monotheist, believing in Allah the Exalted and His Messenger, peace be upon him, and in all that is with Him, knowing that what he committed is forbidden and prohibited; for Allah nullifies by that the reward of his tawḥīd, his belief, his prayers, and all his acts of obedience, and He does not reward him for anything He commanded him to do and he did it; rather, He seizes him for the single sin, which is drinking a gulp of wine or withholding five dirhams of the obligatory zakāt from his wealth or usurping ten dirhams, according to their differences regarding the threat (waʿīd), in rejection of His statement: 'Indeed, good deeds remove evil deeds' (Hūd 11:114), and His statement the Exalted: 'Whoever comes with a good deed will have better than it' (al-Naml 27:89), and His statement the Exalted: 'Whoever comes with a good deed will have ten times the like of it' (al-Anʿām 6:160), and His statement the Exalted: 'Indeed, I do not waste the work of any worker among you, male or female' (Āl ʿImrān 3:195), and similar verses. And they all agreed that there is no intercession (shafāʿa) for the Prophet, may Allah bless him, for anyone who deserves the least punishment in the Hereafter, and that if he asks Allah the Exalted, He will not accept his intercession and will not answer his request. And if I were to trace the mention of their misguidance, the ugliness of their doctrines, and the repulsive things they introduced into the religion and by which they opposed the instruction of the sunan (tawqīf al-sunan), the saying of the general body of Muslims, and all the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-ṣāliḥīn), the book would become long by that, and by mentioning it we would depart from what we intended, and we would not, even with elaboration, do more than a little of it. I only mentioned a portion of that for our master the amīr – may Allah prolong his life – that he might know their departure from the religion and their deviation from the path, and that they are the most harmful sect to this community and the most audacious against Allah, Mighty and Majestic. So to Allah is the complaint, and to Him we turn for the removal of affliction. Then we return to establishing the attributes (ṣifāt) of Allah the Exalted pertaining to His Essence.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal description followed by a methodological transition. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, first presents the Mu'tazilite position on grave sins and intercession, then states that he will not elaborate on their errors but will return to his main topic: proving the attributes of Allah. 

The passage begins by stating the Mu'tazilite view: everyone who commits a major sin (kabīra) and dies persisting in it will be eternally punished, even if that person is a Muslim, a monotheist, and believes in Allah and His Messenger. The Mu'tazila hold that such a person's good deeds – including tawḥīd, belief, prayers, and all acts of obedience – are nullified by the single grave sin. They claim that Allah will punish that person for the sin, even a seemingly minor one like drinking a sip of wine or withholding a small amount of zakāt. This view is based on their doctrine of al-waʿīd (the threat), which they interpret literally, rejecting the Quranic verses that promise forgiveness and the erasing of evil deeds by good deeds (e.g., Hūd 11:114, al-Anʿām 6:160, Āl ʿImrān 3:195). 

Next, al-Baqillani reports that the Mu'tazila unanimously deny the intercession (shafāʿa) of the Prophet for anyone who deserves any punishment in the Hereafter. They assert that if the Prophet were to ask Allah to intercede for such a person, Allah would neither accept the intercession nor answer the request. This extreme position contradicts the Sunni consensus on intercession. 

Al-Baqillani then explains that he could elaborate at length on the errors and innovations of the Mu'tazila, but that would make the book too long and divert from his primary aim. He mentions only a portion of their beliefs so that the amīr (the ruler) may recognize their departure from orthodox Islam. He characterizes them as the most harmful and audacious sect against Allah. Finally, he ends with a supplication to Allah and a transition: he will now return to establishing the attributes of Allah, which is the main subject of the work. This transition marks the end of the digression on Mu'tazilite views and the resumption of the positive theological exposition.

Key Terms
تخليد
كبيرة
حسنات
سيئات
ثواب
وعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilites believe that a Muslim who commits a major sin becomes a disbeliever (kafir).
Correction: The Mu'tazilites actually consider such a person a fasiq (grave sinner) but still a Muslim, though they hold that he will be eternally punished. The text explicitly says he is a Muslim and monotheist.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilites as described by al-Baqillani, what happens to the reward of a Muslim who commits a major sin and dies without repentance?
A) He is forgiven and enters Paradise
B) His reward is nullified and he is eternally punished
C) He is punished temporarily then forgiven
D) His good deeds are increased

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites taught that a single major sin, if unrepented, invalidates all good deeds and leads to eternal punishment, contradicting Quranic promises of forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever quietly assume that your daily prayers and charity will automatically cover over a sin you are reluctant to give up? What would it mean for you if they did not—if that one hidden sin could erase everything?
?
If you truly believed that a single unrepented sin—like a moment of gossip or a small dishonesty—could nullify all your worship and lead to eternal punishment, would you treat that sin differently today? What would you do?
?
The Mu'tazilites rejected the Quranic promise that good deeds remove evil deeds. When you sin, are you tempted to rely on your own good deeds rather than on Allah's mercy to forgive you? What does this passage force you to admit about your reliance?

Mu'tazilite Denial of Intercession and Transition to Divine Attributes
Baqillani reports Mu'tazilite denial of intercession, then transitions to divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite denial of prophetic intercession and Baqillani's critique, as well as his transition to the topic of divine attributes.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites denied intercession for the Prophet even for the least sinner.

Al-Baqillani continues his description of Mu'tazilite errors by reporting their unanimous denial of the Prophet's intercession for anyone deserving punishment. He then explains that he will not elaborate on all their misguidance, but will return to the main purpose: establishing Allah's attributes. This passage serves as a critique and a transition.

Guided Path
1
Read the intercession denial
Read the section starting with 'واتفقوا بأسرهم' and note the absolute denial: no intercession for anyone who deserves the least punishment, and that even the Prophet's request would not be accepted.
This contradicts the well-known Sunni belief in intercession for sinners.
2
Understand Baqillani's purpose
Baqillani states he only mentions a portion of their errors so that the ruler may recognize their deviation. Reflect on why he includes this critique even though it sidetracks from his main topic.
He characterizes them as the most harmful and audacious sect.
3
Note the transition
The passage ends with a prayer and a transition: 'Then we return to establishing the attributes of Allah.' This marks the resumption of the main subject after the digression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilites denied all forms of intercession.
Correction: They denied intercession for anyone who deserves any punishment, but some allowed intercession for increasing reward for the pious. The text specifies denial for those who deserve punishment.

A) The Prophet's intercession is accepted
B) There is no intercession for such a person
C) Intercession is possible but only for minor sins
D) They did not discuss intercession

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites rejected prophetic intercession for sinners, and Baqillani uses their errors to highlight the need for correct doctrine before transitioning to divine attributes.

?

?

Condemning Deviation and Returning to the Proof of Attributes
Baqillani condemns a deviant sect and returns to proving Allah's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani transitions from condemning a deviant sect to re-establishing the necessity of proving Allah's attributes for His essence.

Core Idea
The gravest error is departing from divine truth; the true path is affirming Allah's attributes.

Imam Baqillani uses a sharp critique of a deviant group to set the stage for the core theological task: proving Allah's attributes. This passage marks a pivot from refutation to positive doctrine, reminding us that theological precision is both a shield against error and a foundation for faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the emotional tone of condemnation and the formal return to argument.
The phrase 'أطال الله بقاءه' is a supplication for the reader's longevity.
2
Identify the two parts
The passage has a clear break: first, the condemnation of a sect; second, the return to proving attributes. Mark where the shift happens.
The word 'ثم' signals the transition.
3
Analyze the condemnation
Baqillani describes the sect's departure from religion, deviation from the path, and being the most harmful and audacious. Reflect on why he uses such strong language.
This sets a warning for the reader about theological extremes.
4
Understand the return
After expressing complaint to Allah, Baqillani explicitly returns to 'إثبات صفات الله تعالى لذاته'. This is the central task of kalam.
'لذاته' means the attributes are essential, not accidental.
5
Connect to broader lesson
Realize that this passage serves as a bridge: the condemnation is a foil, and the return is the positive agenda for the coming sections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطال الله بقاءه ليعرف مفارقتهم للدين وعدولهم عن السبيل، وأنهم أضرُّ فرقة على هذه الأمّة وأشدّها جراءةً على الله عزّ وجلّ فإلى الله المشتكى وإليه نرغب في كشف البلوى ثم رجع بنا القول إلى إثبات صفات الله تعالى لذاته.
May Allah prolong his life so that he may recognize their departure from the religion and their deviation from the path, and that they are the most harmful sect to this nation and the most audacious against Allah, may He be glorified and exalted. To Allah is the complaint, and to Him we turn in seeking relief from the trial. Then we return to saying about proving the attributes of Allah, the Exalted, for His essence.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a transitional statement. The author first invokes a blessing on someone, then describes a deviant group (likely the Mu'tazila or anthropomorphists), stating they are the most harmful and audacious against Allah. He then expresses his complaint to Allah and his hope for relief. Finally, he announces a return to the main subject: proving the divine attributes for Allah's essence. This sets the stage for the following discussion on specific attributes.

What does the author do after condemning the deviant sect?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone whose beliefs or actions clearly depart from the truth, does your heart first turn to complaint to Allah and a desire to return to correct theology, or does it react with self-righteous anger? What does that reveal about your own attachment to divine attributes?
?
Have you ever considered that your own small compromises in faith might be a form of 'departure from the religion'? How will you actively reaffirm Allah's attributes in your life today to guard against such deviation?
?
The passage calls the sect 'most audacious against Allah'. Where in your own life have you shown audacity toward Allah—perhaps through negligence or disobedience? What specific step will you take to replace that audacity with humility and a firm return to affirming His attributes?

Meaning of God's Disavowal from Polytheists
Baqillani explains the meaning of God's disavowal of polytheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Qur'anic expression 'God is disavowed of the polytheists' refers to the abrogation of treaties, not to God's disavowal of their polytheism, and how Baqillani refutes alternative interpretations.

Core Idea
God's disavowal is from covenants, not from polytheism itself.

This lesson examines an objection raised against the orthodox understanding of a key Qur'anic verse. Imām al-Bāqillānī clarifies the correct interpretation and refutes a misinterpretation that would lead to theological absurdities. By engaging with this passage, you will learn how classical scholars defended divine transcendence through precise linguistic and rational analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Baqillani's answer
Carefully read the opening objection about the meaning of 'God is disavowed of the polytheists'. Then read Baqillani's response that the verse actually refers to covenants.
Notice how Baqillani immediately specifies what the verse does NOT mention.
2
Identify the two absurd consequences
Baqillani points out that the opponent's interpretation leads to two absurdities: that God would not disavow some polytheism, and that the Prophet's disavowal would mean disavowing the creation of actions. Identify these.
3
Follow the counter-analogy
Baqillani then uses the verse 'God is the protector of the believers' to show that if the opponent's logic were applied, it would imply God creates righteousness. Understand this analogical argument.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Consider what this passage teaches about how to interpret ambiguous Qur'anic statements in light of clear rational and scriptural principles.
The key principle: God’s attributes (like disavowal) must be understood in their context, not literalistically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا فما معنى قول الله تعالى: أن الله بريء من المشركين وتبرئه من شركهم؟ قيل لهم: إن الله تعالى لم يعرض في هذه الآية لذكر الشرك منه. وإنما قال: براءة من الله ورسوله إلى الذين عاهدتم من المشركين إلى قوله: أن الله بريء من المشركين ورسوله يعني: من العهود والمواثيق التي كانت بينهم وبين رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم. ثم قال: إلا الذين عاهدتم عند المسجد الحرام فيجب على تأويلهم الا يكون قد برىء من شرك الذين عاهدوا منهم وهذا جهل من قائله. ويقال لهم: فيجب على تأويلكم أن تكون براءة الرسول منهم براءة من خلق فعلهم وهذا جهل لا يقوله أحد فدل ذلك على أن التأويل ما ذكرناه. ثم يقال لهم: فيجب أن يدل قوله تعالى: الله ولي الذين آمنوا على أنه متوّل لخلق برّهم وإيمانهم. فإن مروا على هذا، تركوا دينهم وقالوا بالحق؛ وإن أبوا هذا التأويل أبطلوا استدلالهم وتعلقهم.
If they say: 'What is the meaning of God's statement, "That God is disavowed of the polytheists" and He disowns their polytheism?' It is said to them: God did not mention in this verse the mention of polytheism from them. Rather He said: 'A disavowal from God and His messenger to those with whom you made covenants from the polytheists' up to His statement: 'That God is disavowed of the polytheists and His messenger' meaning from the covenants and pledges that were between them and His messenger (peace be upon him). Then He said: 'Except those with whom you made a covenant at the Sacred Mosque' so according to their interpretation, it would be necessary that He is not disavowed of the polytheism of those with whom they made a covenant, and this is ignorance of the speaker. And it is said to them: According to your interpretation, the messenger's disavowal of them would be a disavowal of the creation of their action, and this is ignorance that no one says. So that indicates that the interpretation is what we mentioned. Then it is said to them: Then it would be necessary that His statement, 'God is the protector of those who believe' indicates that He is responsible for creating their righteousness and faith. If they pass by this, they abandon their religion and speak the truth; and if they reject this interpretation, they invalidate their argument and their clinging.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector asks about the meaning of God's disavowal (براءة) from polytheists. Baqillani explains that the context of the verse from Surah Tawbah is about treaties, not about shirk itself. He refutes the misinterpretation by showing that it leads to absurd consequences, such as God not disavowing some shirk or disavowing the creation of actions. He also uses the verse 'God is the protector of the believers' to show that if the opponent's logic were applied, it would imply God creates righteousness, which they may not accept.

Key Terms
براءة
المشركين
عهود
مواثيق
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that God's disavowal (براءة) in the verse means God is disavowing the polytheism of the polytheists themselves.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the verse is about disavowal from the covenants (treaties) with the polytheists, not from their polytheism. The context and subsequent verses make this clear.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what does God's disavowal (براءة) refer to in the verse?
A) Disavowal of their polytheism
B) Disavowal of the covenants
C) Disavowal of their persons
D) Disavowal of their actions

Key Takeaway
God's disavowal of the polytheists in the Qur'an refers to the abrogation of treaties, not to disavowal of their polytheism, as alternative interpretations lead to theological absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about God disavowing people, do you assume it means He rejects them entirely without hope? How does understanding the context of covenants change your view of God's mercy and justice? Will you commit to reading verses in their full context before forming beliefs about God's treatment of others?
?
Are you ever quick to adopt an interpretation of difficult verses that confirms your biases without considering the theological consequences? This lesson shows that bad interpretations lead to absurdities. What step will you take to ensure you seek sound understanding before judging others?
?
The opponent's interpretation would have made the Prophet disavow the creation of polytheism—an absurdity. Is there any belief you hold about God or His Prophet that, when pushed to its logical conclusion, becomes equally absurd? Are you willing to re-examine it in light of the Quranic context?

Why the Qadariyya Are Called Qadariyya
Baqillani explains the origin of the name 'Qadariyya' and cites the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the origin of the name 'Qadariyya' and why Baqillani argues they must be called that.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya are named so for their false claim of independent creation.

Baqillani explores the origin of the term 'Qadariyya' and defends its application as a term of blame. This passage answers the objection of those who reject the label, grounding it in both rational argument and prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of the author's argument.
Notice the concise style of Baqillani.
2
Understand the accusation
Identify the core accusation against the Qadariyya: they claim to create their own actions and have power over them apart from Allah.
This claim is described as 'false with no basis'.
3
Note the hadith citation
Baqillani supports his naming with a hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.'
The hadith reinforces that the name is a blameworthy label from revelation.
4
Reflect on the naming logic
Consider why the name 'Qadariyya' is used despite their denial of Qadr. The lesson shows it is because of their claim to be the creators of their own deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في وجوب تسميتهم قدرية
فإن قالوا: فلِمَ سميتمونا قدريَّة؟ قيل لهم: لادّعائكم لأنفسكم الكذب الذي لا أصل له من خلق أعمالكم وتقديرها والتفرد بملكها والقدرة عليها دون ربكم. وهذا اسم وُضع في الشريعة لذم من قال بالكذب. وجاء في الحديث: «القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة». رواه ابن حبان وأبو داود.
Chapter on the obligation of calling them Qadariyya. If they say: 'Why do you call us Qadariyya?' It is said to them: Because of your false claim, which has no basis, of creating your own actions, measuring them, possessing them exclusively, and having power over them apart from your Lord. And this name was established in the Sharia for condemning those who say the falsehood. And it came in the hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.' Reported by Ibn Hibban and Abu Dawud.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a definition and naming explanation. The author begins a new chapter on the necessity of calling the Qadariyya by that name. The Qadariyya object: why are you calling us Qadariyya? The answer is that they falsely claim to create their own acts, measure them, and have power over them independently of Allah. This claim is false (no basis). The name is a term of blame in the Sharia. The author then cites the well-known hadith that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Qadariyya are those who affirm Qadr, not those who deny it.
Correction: The name 'Qadariyya' is applied to those who claim to create their own actions and thus deny Allah's sole creative power. The hadith confirms this is a blameworthy label.

C) Because they deny the hadith

Key Takeaway
The name 'Qadariyya' is a term of blame for those who falsely claim to create their own actions independently of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something good, do you ever silently credit your own ability, willpower, or intelligence as the ultimate cause? This passage calls that very attitude a false claim. Honestly, how much of your success do you attribute to yourself versus to Allah? What one thing can you do today to shift that attribution entirely to Him?
?
The hadith labels the Qadariyya as 'Magians'—a severe comparison. If someone were to examine your daily thoughts, how often do you act as though you are the sole agent of your actions? In what areas of your life (work, relationships, worship) do you resist acknowledging that Allah is the true Creator and Controller? Commit to one specific moment this week where you will explicitly say 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' before acting.
?
Imagine standing before Allah and being asked: 'Did you create your own deeds?' According to this lesson, claiming that is a baseless falsehood. If Allah were to question your reliance on your own power, what would you say? How does this teaching expose a hidden pride in your heart? Write down one practical step you will take to humble yourself before Allah’s absolute power over your every action.

Refuting Qadariyya through the Magian Comparison and Shafi'i's Argument
Baqillani explains the hadith about Qadariyya and quotes Shafi'i's argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qadariyya are compared to Magians in positing two creators and how al-Shafi'i's argument exposes their inconsistency.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya, like the Magians, effectively believe in two creators by making humans independent agents.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani connects the hadith calling the Qadariyya the 'Magians of this nation' to a core theological error: attributing independent creative power to humans alongside Allah. He then quotes a powerful argument from Imam al-Shafi'i that forces the Qadariyya to confront the implications of divine knowledge and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to get the full meaning.
2
Understand the Magian comparison
Notice how Baqillani explains that the Qadariyya, by making humans independent agents, implicitly assert two creators—like the Magians' dualism of good and evil.
3
Analyze Shafi'i's argument
Identify the steps of al-Shafi'i's refutation: if the Qadariyya concede divine knowledge, they are defeated; if they concede that Allah creates the ability for disbelief, then He is responsible.
Pay attention to the phrase 'if they concede knowledge, they are defeated.'
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why Shafi'i's argument shows the Qadariyya position is inconsistent—it ties divine knowledge and creative power together to expose the flaw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمعنى أنهم يجعلون القسم مستبدين بالفعل والله تعالى فاعل وهم فاعلون فيستندون أفعال العباد إلى قدر العباد فكأنهم يثبتون خالقين في الحقيقية كما أثبت المجوس خالقين خالق الخير وخالق الشر. وقد ألجمهم الشافعي حيث قال: «القدرية إذا سلموا العلم خصموا، وإذا سلموا أن الله تعالى علم أن زيداً يموت وليس بقادر على الكفر إلا بما خلق له من القدرة، فأي صلاح من خلق ما هو السبب المؤدي إلى الكفر». وكذلك خلقه في نفسه لأنه تعالى لو شاء لم يخلقه، فأي صلاح له في خلقه.
Meaning that they make the people independent in action, while Allah the Exalted is the agent and they are agents, so they attribute the actions of servants to the Qadr of the servants, as if they establish two creators in reality, just as the Magians established two creators: the creator of good and the creator of evil. And al-Shafi'i silenced them where he said: 'The Qadariyya, if they concede knowledge, they are defeated; and if they concede that Allah the Exalted knew that Zayd would die and he is not capable of disbelief except by what He created for him of ability, then what benefit is there in creating what is the cause leading to disbelief?' And likewise His creating it in itself, because if He willed, He would not have created it, so what benefit is there for Him in creating it.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and refutation. It begins by explaining the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation': the Qadariyya hold that people are independent agents in their actions alongside Allah, thus effectively positing two creators—just as the Magians believe in two principles (good and evil). Then al-Shafi'i's argument is quoted: if the Qadariyya admit that Allah knows everything, they are defeated because if He knows a person will disbelieve and yet creates in them the ability to disbelieve, then He is creating the cause of disbelief. If He could have not created that ability, then He is responsible for the disbelief, which undermines their claim of independent human power. This shows the inconsistency of their position.

Key Terms
مجوس
خالقين
الشافعي
العلم
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Qadariyya are called Magians because they worship fire.
Correction: The Prophet ﷺ called them Magians because they resemble the Magians in their dualism, not because of fire worship.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for comparing the Qadariyya to the Magians?
A) They both deny divine predestination.
B) They both posit two creators.
C) They both reject the Prophet's teachings.
D) They both worship fire.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya are refuted by showing that their belief in independent human agency implies a dualism similar to the Magians, and al-Shafi'i's argument exposes that if Allah knows and creates the ability for disbelief, He is the cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Do you ever act as if you are the sole creator of your actions, forgetting that Allah creates your ability and knowledge? What would change if you truly acknowledged that every action is by His permission?
?
2. If you truly believed that Allah’s knowledge encompasses every choice you will make, yet He still created the ability for you to choose, how would that affect your sense of responsibility and your reliance on Him?
?
3. The Qadariyya feared that acknowledging divine control would make God responsible for evil, but al-Shafi’i showed that denying it leads to a worse error. Are you willing to accept that some things are beyond your understanding, or do you insist on a simplistic explanation that may imply falsehood about Allah?

Hadith Evidence and Refutation of the Mu'tazila on Qadr
Baqillani presents hadiths and refutes the Mu'tazila claim that Qadariyya are those who deny Qadr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses hadith evidence to identify the Qadariyya as those who deny Qadr and refute the Mu'tazila interpretation.

Core Idea
The hadiths explicitly condemn deniers of Qadr, not affirmers.

This lesson presents a chain of hadith evidence that Baqillani uses to establish that the Qadariyya are deniers of divine decree, contrary to the Mu'tazila claim that the label applies to those who affirm Qadr. The passage includes multiple prophetic traditions and a discussion of their authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Read the complete passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the three hadiths cited and the author's commentary.
The passage is dense; read carefully.
2
Identify the first hadith and its point
The first hadith from Ibn Umar condemns those who say 'no Qadr'. Understand what action is prescribed against them.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila counter-claim
Baqillani reports the Mu'tazila argument that the hadith refers to those who affirm Qadr. See how he refutes it with the second hadith.
4
Analyze the second and third hadiths
These hadiths explicitly say 'Magians of this nation are those who say no Qadr'. Note how they settle the dispute.
5
Reflect on the authentication argument
Baqillani argues that Abu Hanifa's use of these hadiths proves their authenticity. Consider the significance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى محمد بن الحسن والحارثي والأنصاري عن أبي حنيفة قال: حدثني نافع عن عبد الله بن عمر رضي الله عنهما عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام: «يجيء قوم يقولون لا قدر، فإذا لقيتموهم فلا تسلموا عليهم، وإن مرضوا فلا تعودهم، وإن ماتوا فلا تشهدوا جنازتهم، فإنهم شيعة هذه الأمة حق على الله أن يلحقهم بهم». فالمعتزلة القدرية لأنهم جعلوا الله والعبد سواء ينفي قدرته عز وجل على ما يقدر عليه عبده، وبالعكس كما المجوس قائلون بمبدأين مستقلين هما الظلمة والنور أو يزدان وأهرمن. وقول المعتزلة: «أنتم القدرية المرادون بهذا الحديث، فإن الشيء ينسب إلى من يثبته لا إلى من ينفيه». فهو مردود لما رواه أبو داود عن حذيفة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لكل أمة مجوس، ومجوس هذه الأمة الذين يقولون لا قدر». فهو نص في أنهم هم المرادون. وأخرج البيهقي والإمام أحمد عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مجوس هذه الأمة الذين يقولون لا قدر، فإن مرضوا فلا تعودوهم، وإن ماتوا فلا تشهدوهم، وهم شيعة الدجال، فحق على الله أن يحشرهم معه». فهو من الأحاديث المشهورة التي تقوم بها الحجة في العقيدة، ولذلك أورده الإمام أبو حنيفة في بعض رسائله الاعتقادية، فاحتجاج أبي حنيفة به في مسألة اعتقادية دليل على تصحيحه له، والإمام أبو حنيفة من المحدثين الحفاظ الذين يصح منهم التصحيح والتضعيف. ورواه ابن حبان في صحيحه وصححه وإن كان عند كثيرين ضعيفاً.
And Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Harithi and al-Ansari reported from Abu Hanifa: Nafi' narrated to me from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, from him, peace be upon him: 'A people will come saying there is no Qadr. When you meet them, do not greet them, and if they fall ill, do not visit them, and if they die, do not attend their funeral. For they are the sect of the Dajjal, it is a right upon Allah to join them to him.' So the Mu'tazila are the Qadariyya because they made Allah and the servant equal in negating His power over what His servant is capable of, and vice versa, just as the Magians say there are two independent principles: darkness and light, or Yazdan and Ahriman. And the statement of the Mu'tazila: 'You are the Qadariyya intended by this hadith, for a thing is attributed to the one who affirms it, not to the one who denies it.' So it is refuted by what Abu Dawud reported from Hudhayfa from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Every nation has Magians, and the Magians of this nation are those who say there is no Qadr.' This is explicit that they are the intended ones. And al-Bayhaqi and Imam Ahmad reported from Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The Magians of this nation are those who say there is no Qadr. If they fall ill, do not visit them, and if they die, do not attend their funeral, and they are the sect of the Dajjal; it is a right upon Allah to gather them with him.' So it is among the well-known hadiths by which proof is established in creed. Therefore, Imam Abu Hanifa mentioned it in some of his creedal epistles. Abu Hanifa's using it as proof in a creedal matter is evidence of his authenticating it, and Imam Abu Hanifa is among the hadith masters who are capable of authentication and weakening. And Ibn Hibban reported it in his Sahih and authenticated it, even though many consider it weak.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is hadith evidence and a refutation of the Mu'tazila interpretation. It begins by reporting a hadith from Ibn Umar that condemns those who deny Qadr. The author then explains that the Mu'tazila are the Qadariyya because they equate Allah and the servant by denying Allah's power over what the servant can do, similar to Magian dualism. The Mu'tazila claim that the hadith refers to those who affirm Qadr, but the author refutes this by citing another hadith from Abu Dawud that explicitly says 'those who say there is no Qadr' are the Magians. Then a third hadith is cited with similar wording. The author argues that these hadiths are proof in creedal matters, and that Abu Hanifa's quoting of them shows they are authentic, since he was a hadith expert.

مجوس

نفي القدر
المعتزلة
أبو حنيفة

Misconception: That the hadith about Qadariyya being Magians refers to those who affirm Qadr.
Correction: The hadith explicitly says 'those who say no Qadr' are the Magians, so the Qadariyya are the deniers.

Key Takeaway
The hadith evidence clearly identifies the Qadariyya as those who deny Qadr, and the Mu'tazila attempt to invert the meaning is refuted by explicit prophetic texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of the moments you feel most in control—your career, your relationships, your daily decisions—do you truly believe that Allah's power encompasses every detail? Or is there a hidden belief that some outcomes depend solely on you? How would your prayer life change if you really lived the truth that 'there is no Qadr' is a statement of disbelief?
?
The hadith commands us to shun those who deny Qadr. Have you ever sat under the influence of someone (a speaker, a friend, a book) who subtly downplayed Allah's sovereignty? Did you feel any unease, or did you rationalize it away? This lesson calls you to examine your company: who shapes your understanding of Allah's decree?
?
The Mu'tazila twisted the Prophet's words to escape condemnation. In what area of your life are you most tempted to reinterpret clear revelation to fit your desires—whether it's about money, relationships, or your own sense of righteousness? What would it cost you to submit fully, without mental 'workarounds', to what the Prophet taught?

The True Qadariyya Are Those Who Deny Divine Predestination
Baqillani refutes the claim that Ash'aris are Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'Qadariyya' applies to those who deny divine predestination, not to those who affirm it.

Core Idea
The true Qadariyya are those who deny God's control over actions, not those who affirm it.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani addresses a polemical accusation: some groups claim that the Ash'aris are Qadariyya because they affirm God's creation of all actions. Baqillani turns the tables by arguing that the real Qadariyya are those who deny God's role in creating actions and instead attribute creation to themselves. Let's see how he builds this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the structure: claim, objection, response.
2
Identify the opponents
Who is Baqillani addressing? The passage uses 'you' (plural) referring to those who deny divine creation of actions. Identify that these are likely the Mu'tazila.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The opponents object that since Ash'aris affirm God's creation and measuring, they should be called Qadariyya. Baqillani responds by distinguishing between truthful and false attribution.
Key point: truthfulness in attributing actions to God does not incur blame.
4
Understand the core principle
The blameworthy name applies to those who make false claims, i.e., those who deny God's creation and attribute it to themselves. The Ash'aris are truthful, so they are not Qadariyya.
Reflect on how labels can be misapplied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلق الأفعال خاصةً ودان بغير الحق. فلما كان ما قدمناه من الأدلة على خلق الأفعال قد أبطل دعواكم، وجب أن تكونوا أحق الناس بهذا الاسم. وقولهم بعد ذلك إنهم ينفون القدر عن ربهم وإننا نحن نثبته، فيجب أن نكون أولى بهذه التسمية تمويه منهم. لأنهم ينفون تقدير الأعمال وخلقها عن ربهم ويثبتون ذلك لأنفسهم، وهم مبطلون في هذه الدعوى، فلزمهم اسم الذم لادعائهم غير الحق. فإن قالوا: فالباري سبحانه قد أثبت الخلق والتقدير لنفسه، وأثبتموه أنتم له، فيجب أن تكونوا بذلك قدرية. قيل لهم: لا يجب ما قلتم، لأن الله تعالى صادق محق في إثبات الخلق والتقدير لنفسه، وكذلك نحن صادقون محقون في إضافة ذلك إلى الله تعالى، فلم يلزمنا اسم الذم، وأنتم مبطلون في دعواكم لهذه الأمور.
Especially the creation of actions, and he believed in other than the truth. Since what we have presented of the proofs for the creation of actions has invalidated your claim, it is necessary that you be the most deserving people of this name. And their statement after that that they negate [divine] predestination from their Lord while we affirm it, so we must be more entitled to this designation — this is a deception from them. Because they negate the measuring and creation of actions from their Lord and affirm them for themselves, and they are false in this claim, so the blameworthy name is incumbent upon them for their claim of untruth. If they say: The Creator, glorified be He, has affirmed creation and measuring for Himself, and you affirm it for Him, so you must thereby be Qadariyya. It is said to them: What you say is not necessary, because God Almighty is truthful and right in affirming creation and measuring for Himself, and likewise we are truthful and right in attributing that to God Almighty, so the blameworthy name does not apply to us, while you are false in your claim of these matters.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. The author first states that the proofs for the creation of actions (i.e., that God creates all human actions) have disproven the opposing view, so the opponents are more deserving of the blameworthy name 'Qadariyya'. Then the opponents' objection is presented: they claim that since the author's party (the Ash'aris) affirm God's creation and measuring, they should be called Qadariyya. The answer is that God's affirming Himself is true, and the Ash'aris' affirming it for God is also true, so no blame attaches. The opponents, by contrast, are false in their claims.

Key Terms
قدري (Qadari)
القدر (al-qadr)
خلق الأفعال (khalq al-af'al)
التقدير (al-taqdir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the term Qadariyya applies to those who affirm divine predestination.
Correction: The passage shows that the Qadariyya are those who deny God's creation of actions and attribute it to themselves, i.e., the Mu'tazila.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, who are the true Qadariyya?
A) Those who affirm God's creation of all actions.
B) Those who deny God's creation of actions and attribute it to themselves.
C) Those who frequently mention the word 'qadr'.
D) Both the Ash'aris and the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
The term 'Qadariyya' is a blameworthy label for those who deny God's creation of actions, not for those who affirm it truthfully.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own actions, do you truly feel that God is the Creator of each one, or do you sometimes feel that you are independently in control? What would change in your daily life if you genuinely believed that every movement and thought is created by Him?
?
The opponents in this lesson were called 'false' because they claimed creation for themselves while denying it to God. Are there areas of your life where you implicitly claim control without acknowledging God's role? Spend a moment silently naming one such area and commit to consciously attributing it to God tomorrow.
?
This passage distinguishes between truthful and false attribution of creation to God. How often do you check whether your beliefs about God are based on truth or on deceptive arguments like those of the opponents? What step will you take today to verify your understanding of God's actions in the world?

The Term Qadari – Polemics and Linguistic Roots
Baqillani clarifies the sectarian term Qadari and its linguistic root qadr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'Qadari' is specifically applied to those who claim to create their own actions, and how the root 'qadr' carries multiple meanings in Arabic.

Core Idea
A Qadari is not just anyone discussing qadr, but one who falsely claims independent creation.

Imam Baqillani tackles both the sectarian label 'Qadari' and its linguistic foundation. He first shows why this name sticks to certain claimants, then unpacks the rich meanings of the Arabic root 'q-d-r'. This passage combines polemics with philology, grounding theological labels in language.

Guided Path
1
Understand the polemical context
Read the opening lines where Baqillani addresses those who claim to estimate and create their own actions. Note that the name 'Qadari' is forced upon them by their own claim.
The blame is directed at a specific group, not all who discuss qadr.
2
Grasp the linguistic meanings of qadr
Go through the various meanings: decree (qada'), setting a measure, and the verbs qadara / qaddara. Pay attention to the Quranic and poetic examples.
The heavy and light forms are both used in classical Arabic.
3
Connect language to label
See how the term Qadari is derived from the root qadr, but the label is reserved for those with a false opinion about it.
Baqillani links the lexical analysis back to the definition of the sect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذم . وأنتم تكثرون ذكر تقديركم لأفعالكم وتفردكم بملكها، وخلقها وتكذبون وتفترون في هذه الدعوى، فوجب لزوم الاسم لكم . على أنه لو جميع الفرق وعامة الناس وخاصتهم عن القدرية، لم يرشدوا إلا إليكم دون كل فرقة من فرق الأمة. وجملة هذا القول أن قدرياً سئل نسبة إلى القول بالباطل في القدر. والقدر يكون بمعنى القضاء، ويكون بمعنى جعل الشيء على قدر وقد يقال قَدَرَ وقَدَّرَ، مخفف ومثقل. والعرب تقول: قدرت الشيء، وقدرته. قال النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم في الهلال: «فإن غُمَّ عليكم فاقدروا له ثلاثين»، أي: قدّروا. وقد قال الله تعالى: وما قدروا الله حق قدره، وتثقيلها جائز. وكذلك قوله: فسالت أودية بقدرها، ولو خففت لكان ذلك جائزاً شائعاً. والعرب تقول: قدّر الله، وقدَّر الله. وقال الشاعر: كل شيء حتى أخيك متاع وبقدر تفرق واجتماع. وقال آخر: وما صب رجلي في حديد مجاشع مع القدر الأحاجة لا أريدها يعني بالقدر القدرة. وكل من في القدر قولاً باطلاً لزمه اسم قدري، لأنه وضع لذمّ المبطل.
Blame. And you frequently mention your estimation of your actions and your unique possession of them and creation of them, and you lie and fabricate in this claim, so the name becomes necessary for you. For if all the sects and the common people and their elites were asked about the Qadariyya, they would not point to anyone except you, apart from every sect of the community. The summary of this statement is that a Qadari was asked, attributed to false speech about al-qadr. And al-qadr can mean al-qada' (decree), and it can mean setting a thing according to a measure, and it is said Qadara and Qaddara, light and heavy. The Arabs say: Qadartu al-shay'a and Qaddartuhu. The Prophet (peace and blessings upon him and his family) said about the crescent: 'If it is obscured over you, then estimate it as thirty' meaning apportion. And Allah Almighty said: 'And they measured not Allah with His true measure,' and its emphasis is permissible. Likewise His saying: 'So the valleys flowed according to their measure,' and if it were lightened that would be widespreadly permissible. And the Arabs say: Qaddara Allah and Qadara Allah. And a poet said: 'Everything, even your brother, is a possession, and in measure is separation and union.' And another said: 'And what brought my foot into the iron of Mujashi' with al-qadr, need? I do not want it,' meaning by al-qadr ability. And everyone who holds a false opinion about al-qadr is necessarily named Qadari, because it is established for the blame of the falsehood-holder.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a combined explanation of the polemical term 'Qadari' and the linguistic root 'qadr'. Baqillani begins by addressing a group (likely the Qadariyya) who claim to independently estimate, own, and create their own actions. He asserts that such a claim necessarily earns them the name 'Qadari'. He supports this by noting that if one were to ask all people—both common and elite—about the Qadariyya, they would point to this group alone. The summary is that a Qadari is defined as one who is asked and found to hold a false view about al-qadr. Then Baqillani provides a detailed lexical analysis of the word 'qadr'. It can mean al-qada' (divine decree) or setting a thing to a measure. The verb appears in both light (qadara) and heavy (qaddara) forms. Arabic usage includes both, as in the Prophet's hadith about crescent estimation (faqduru lahu thalatheen, meaning 'apportion') and in the Quranic verse 'What did they measure Allah with His true measure' where the heavy form is also permissible. Another Quranic example is 'the valleys flowed according to their measure' where the light form would be acceptable. Arabs also say both 'qaddara Allah' and 'qadara Allah'. Poetic evidence is given: a line about everything—even a brother—being a possession with separation and union according to measure; another about a poet's foot not being placed in iron with 'al-qadr' meaning 'al-qudra' (power). Baqillani concludes that anyone who holds a false statement about al-qadr is called Qadari, because the name was coined to blame the falsehood-holder.

قضاء
تقدير
قدرة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term Qadari applies to anyone who believes in predestination (qadr).
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the name is for those who falsely claim to create their own actions, not for all believers in qadr.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The term 'Qadari' is a polemical label for those who claim independent creation of their actions, rooted in the linguistic flexibility of the word 'qadr'.

Refuting Dualist and Zoroastrian Views on Guidance
Baqillani refutes dualist and Zoroastrian views on the origin of guidance and misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why dualist and Zoroastrian views on guidance and misguidance are incompatible with Islamic monotheism.

Core Idea
Attributing good and evil to separate sources violates the unity of Allah.

Throughout history, various groups have attempted to explain the existence of good and evil by positing two independent principles. The Thunawiyya (dualists) and the Majus (Zoroastrians) held such views. Baqillani rejects these by pointing to the foundational doctrine of tawhid, which has already been established. This lesson examines those claims and their contradiction with Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Read the passage and note that two groups are mentioned: the Thunawiyya (dualists) and the Majus (Zoroastrians). Each has a distinct claim about the source of guidance and misguidance.
These groups are ancient religious sects with dualistic cosmologies.
2
Understand each claim
The dualists say guidance comes from light and misguidance from darkness. The Zoroastrians say guidance is from the deity and misguidance from Satan. Write down each claim clearly.
Notice that both assign good and evil to separate, autonomous forces.
3
See the refutation by tawhid
Baqillani does not argue at length here; he simply refers to the earlier chapter on the unity of the Creator. This implies that the very foundation of tawhid—that Allah is the sole creator and source of all things—renders these dualistic views false.
Think about how attributing any power to another being contradicts Allah's exclusive lordship.
4
Connect to broader theology
Reflect on why this refutation is important: it preserves Allah's absolute sovereignty and prevents any notion of rival creators. This is a fundamental tenet of Islamic belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
