Conditional Cursing and the Knowledge Distinction
Baqillani refutes objection about conditional cursing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why conditional cursing of sinners by humans does not imply that God can also curse conditionally, due to the difference in knowledge.

Core Idea
God's absolute knowledge makes conditional judgments inappropriate for Him.

Baqillani addresses an objection: if we conditionally curse sinners, why can't God? He responds with an analogy of false witnesses and highlights the key difference—our limited knowledge versus God's omniscience. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the full translation to grasp the flow.
The passage is a refutation of an objection.
2
Identify the objection and response
Find where the objectors claim that human conditional cursing implies God's conditional cursing. Then see Baqillani's counter-analogy.
The objection is in the middle of the passage.
3
Understand the analogy with false witnesses
Notice the parallel: we conditionally curse false witnesses, but that does not force God to do so. This weakens the original objection.
4
Grasp the distinguishing reason
Baqillani explains the key difference: our ignorance vs. God's omniscience. Conditional judgments are for those unaware of outcomes.
This is the core of the argument.
5
Reflect on divine attributes
Consider why this matters: God's knowledge is absolute, so His judgments are unconditional. This safeguards divine perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل لهم : وكذلك مدحنا للمؤمنين وتوليهم وحسن الثناء عليهم ليس بثواب، لأننا نفعل ذلك أجمع بالمنافقين متى أظهروا لنا الإيمان، وليس ذلك بثواب ولا دلالة على حصول الثواب في الآخرة . وإن هم قالوا : لو جاز أن نعادي الفاسق ونذمه ونلعنه بشريطة أن يكون ممن يعاقب في الآخرة، لجاز أن يعاديه الله ويلعنه على هذه الشريطة . يقال لهم : ولو جاز أن نلعن نحن شهود الزنى ونبر منهم بشريطة أن كانوا كاذبين لجاز أن يلعنهم الله ويعاديهم على هذه الشريطة . فإن لم يجب هذا، لم يجب ما قلتم . والسبب المفرق بين وعداوتنا بشريطة يجوز أن تكون ويجوز أن لا تكون وامتناع لعن الباري لهم بشريطة، لأننا نحن لا نعلم عواقب أمورهم، والباري سبحانه عالم بذلك، فلم يجز عليه لعنهم والعداوة لهم بشريطة، وإن جاز وصح ذلك فينا .
It was said to them: Likewise, our praising of the believers, showing loyalty to them, and speaking well of them is not a reward, because we do all of that to the hypocrites when they show us faith, and that is not a reward nor an indication of obtaining reward in the Hereafter. And if they say: If it were permissible for us to show enmity to the sinner, blame him, and curse him on the condition that he be among those punished in the Hereafter, then it would be permissible for God to show enmity to him and curse him on this condition. It is said to them: And if it were permissible for us to curse false witnesses and disavow them on the condition that they were lying, then it would be permissible for God to curse them and show enmity to them on this condition. If this is not necessary, then what you said is not necessary. And the differentiating reason between our conditional enmity that may or may not be, and the impossibility of the Creator's cursing them on a condition, is that we do not know the outcomes of their affairs, while the Creator, exalted, knows that, so it is not permissible for Him to curse them or show enmity to them on a condition, although that is permissible and correct in our case.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection regarding conditional cursing and enmity. The objectors argue that if we can curse a sinner conditionally on their deserving punishment in the afterlife, then God could also curse them conditionally. Baqillani responds by drawing an analogy with false witnesses: we curse them conditionally on their being liars, but that does not imply that God curses them conditionally, because God knows their true state absolutely. The key distinction is our limited knowledge versus God's omniscience. Thus, conditional judgments are valid for us but not for God, as He knows actual outcomes without condition.

Correction: Baqillani shows the difference is based on knowledge: humans are ignorant, so they use conditions; God knows all, so He cannot curse conditionally.

B) Because God knows their actual outcomes absolutely.
C) Because sinners are not deserving of cursing.

Key Takeaway
Conditional judgments are valid for humans due to limited knowledge, but not for God because He knows outcomes absolutely.

The Logical Parity of Eternal Reward and Punishment
Baqillani refutes the objection for eternal punishment by logical parity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the same reasoning used to claim eternal punishment for the sinful believer also proves eternal reward, thus undermining the conclusion of eternal punishment.

Core Idea
Same logic that demands eternal punishment also demands eternal reward.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani responds to those who argue that the sinful believer deserves eternal punishment because he deserves eternal blame. He reveals a powerful logical parity: the same reasoning shows the sinner deserves eternal reward for his faith, so punishment cannot be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the source where the objectors present their case: the sinful believer deserves perpetual blame, so he deserves perpetual punishment.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ما لم يتب' (as long as he does not repent).
2
Identify Baqillani's counterargument
Notice how Baqillani applies the exact same reasoning to reward: just as blame is perpetual, so is praise for faith; thus the sinner deserves perpetual reward, so he cannot be punished eternally.
3
Reflect on the logical parity
Ask yourself: If both punishment and reward are claimed to be eternal based on the same type of reasoning, how does Baqillani's objection undermine the original claim?
This is a classic example of using the opponent's own logic against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
وإن قالوا : الدليل على خلود الفاسق الملّي في جهنم أنه قد ثبت أنه مستحق للعقاب وثبت أن ما يستحقه دائم ، كما أنه مستحق للذم دائماً ما لم يتب ؛ فوجب أنه غير مثاب . يقال لهم : وما أنكرتم أن يكون الفاسق غير معاقب بالنار بهذه العلة بعينها ؟ لأنه قد ثبت أنه مستحق لثواب دائم على إيمانه وطاعته، كما أنه مستحق لمدح دائم، فوجب أنه غير معاقب بالنار .
فإن قالوا: لو كان مستحقاً للثواب ، لم يُلْعَن ولم يُهَن في الدنيا ولزالت عنه الحدود.
قيل لهم : هذه الحدود ليست بعقاب، وإنما هي امتحان .
ثم يقال لهم : ولو لم يستحق الفاسق بطاعته الثواب، لم يستحق المناكحة والموارثة والدفن في مقابر المسلمين .
فإن قالوا : هذه الأمور ليست بثواب .
قيل لهم : والحدود ليست بعقاب لأنها جارية على التائب الولي . وكذلك ذمنا وبغضنا ليس بعقاب، لأنه جارٍ على شهود الزنى إذا اختلفت شهادتهم ونقص عددهم، وإن كانوا صادقين أبراراً عند الله عزّ وجلّ . ولا فصل في شيء من ذلك .
Issue. And if they say: The proof for the eternity of the sinful believer in Hell is that it is established that he deserves punishment, and it is established that what he deserves is perpetual, just as he deserves perpetual blame as long as he does not repent; therefore he is not rewarded. It is said to them: Why do you deny that the sinner is not punished with fire by this same reason? Because it is established that he deserves perpetual reward for his faith and obedience, just as he deserves perpetual praise; therefore he is not punished with fire. Then if they say: If he deserved reward, he would not be cursed nor humiliated in this world, and punishments would be removed from him. It is said to them: These punishments are not punishment; rather, they are a trial. Then it is said to them: And if the sinner did not deserve reward for his obedience, he would not deserve marriage, inheritance, and burial in Muslim cemeteries. If they say: These things are not reward. It is said to them: And the punishments are not punishment because they are applied to the repentant saint. Likewise, our blame and hatred are not punishment, because they are applied to false witnesses when their testimonies differ and their number falls short, even if they are truthful and righteous in the sight of God Almighty. And there is no distinction in any of that.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument about the eternal punishment of the sinful believer. The objectors argue that since the sinner deserves eternal blame, he deserves eternal punishment. Baqillani counters by applying the same logic: the sinner also deserves eternal reward for his faith, so he cannot be punished eternally. When the objectors object that if he deserved reward, worldly punishments and curses would not apply, Baqillani explains that those are not punishments but trials. He further argues by analogy: if the sinner did not deserve reward, he would not inherit or be buried as a Muslim. The objectors say those are not reward, and Baqillani retorts that worldly punishments are not punishment either, as they apply even to the repentant saint and to truthful witnesses whose testimony is rejected. He concludes there is no distinction in these examples.

الخلود
الفاسق الملّي
الاستحقاق
الثواب
العقاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the sinful believer deserves eternal blame, he must also deserve eternal punishment.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the same reasoning also proves eternal reward, so the conclusion of eternal punishment does not follow.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's main argument against the eternity of punishment for the sinful believer?
A) The sinner repents before death.
B) The sinner deserves both eternal reward and punishment, so punishment is cancelled.
C) The same reasoning that proves eternal punishment also proves eternal reward, so punishment does not follow.
D) God's mercy overrides punishment.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses logical parity to argue that the sinful believer's eternal reward for faith negates the conclusion of eternal punishment.

Worldly Punishments as Trials, Not Eternal Retribution
Baqillani refutes objections by reinterpreting worldly punishments as trials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's distinction between worldly punishments (hudud) as trials and eternal punishment, and his analogy with other worldly matters like inheritance and witness testimony.

Core Idea
Hudud are trials, not punishments; they apply even to saints and truthful witnesses.

After establishing the parity argument, Baqillani addresses the objection that worldly punishments like cursing and hudud (legal penalties) show the sinner deserves eternal punishment. He explains that these are trials, not punishments, and uses further examples to show that worldly treatment does not indicate eternal fate.

Guided Path
1
Read the second objection and response
Read from 'فإن قالوا' to 'امتحان' to see the objectors' point about curses and hudud, and Baqillani's immediate reply calling them trials.
Note that Baqillani redefines 'hudud' as trials (امتحان), not punishment.
2
Follow the extended analogy
Read the rest where Baqillani argues that if hudud were punishment, then inheritance and burial would be reward, but objectors deny that. He then gives the example of false witnesses who are blamed despite being truthful.
3
Connect to the larger debate
Reflect on how this second argument supports the first: worldly treatment (good or bad) does not determine eternal fate. Only the Hereafter matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
وإن قالوا : الدليل على خلود الفاسق الملّي في جهنم أنه قد ثبت أنه مستحق للعقاب وثبت أن ما يستحقه دائم ، كما أنه مستحق للذم دائماً ما لم يتب ؛ فوجب أنه غير مثاب . يقال لهم : وما أنكرتم أن يكون الفاسق غير معاقب بالنار بهذه العلة بعينها ؟ لأنه قد ثبت أنه مستحق لثواب دائم على إيمانه وطاعته، كما أنه مستحق لمدح دائم، فوجب أنه غير معاقب بالنار .
فإن قالوا: لو كان مستحقاً للثواب ، لم يُلْعَن ولم يُهَن في الدنيا ولزالت عنه الحدود.
قيل لهم : هذه الحدود ليست بعقاب، وإنما هي امتحان .
ثم يقال لهم : ولو لم يستحق الفاسق بطاعته الثواب، لم يستحق المناكحة والموارثة والدفن في مقابر المسلمين .
فإن قالوا : هذه الأمور ليست بثواب .
قيل لهم : والحدود ليست بعقاب لأنها جارية على التائب الولي . وكذلك ذمنا وبغضنا ليس بعقاب، لأنه جارٍ على شهود الزنى إذا اختلفت شهادتهم ونقص عددهم، وإن كانوا صادقين أبراراً عند الله عزّ وجلّ . ولا فصل في شيء من ذلك .
Issue. And if they say: The proof for the eternity of the sinful believer in Hell is that it is established that he deserves punishment, and it is established that what he deserves is perpetual, just as he deserves perpetual blame as long as he does not repent; therefore he is not rewarded. It is said to them: Why do you deny that the sinner is not punished with fire by this same reason? Because it is established that he deserves perpetual reward for his faith and obedience, just as he deserves perpetual praise; therefore he is not punished with fire. Then if they say: If he deserved reward, he would not be cursed nor humiliated in this world, and punishments would be removed from him. It is said to them: These punishments are not punishment; rather, they are a trial. Then it is said to them: And if the sinner did not deserve reward for his obedience, he would not deserve marriage, inheritance, and burial in Muslim cemeteries. If they say: These things are not reward. It is said to them: And the punishments are not punishment because they are applied to the repentant saint. Likewise, our blame and hatred are not punishment, because they are applied to false witnesses when their testimonies differ and their number falls short, even if they are truthful and righteous in the sight of God Almighty. And there is no distinction in any of that.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument about the eternal punishment of the sinful believer. The objectors argue that since the sinner deserves eternal blame, he deserves eternal punishment. Baqillani counters by applying the same logic: the sinner also deserves eternal reward for his faith, so he cannot be punished eternally. When the objectors object that if he deserved reward, worldly punishments and curses would not apply, Baqillani explains that those are not punishments but trials. He further argues by analogy: if the sinner did not deserve reward, he would not inherit or be buried as a Muslim. The objectors say those are not reward, and Baqillani retorts that worldly punishments are not punishment either, as they apply even to the repentant saint and to truthful witnesses whose testimony is rejected. He concludes there is no distinction in these examples.

Key Terms
الحدود
الامتحان
المناكحة
الموارثة
شهود الزنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that receiving worldly punishments like hudud indicates that the person is eternally damned.
Correction: Baqillani shows that these are trials, not retribution, and they apply even to saints and truthful witnesses.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why are worldly punishments (hudud) not considered true punishment?
A) Because they are only applied to disbelievers.
B) Because they are applied even to the repentant saint and to truthful witnesses.
C) Because they are always followed by repentance.
D) Because they are lighter than eternal punishment.

Key Takeaway
Worldly punishments are not punishments in the Hereafter; they are trials and apply even to the righteous, so they cannot be used to argue for eternal punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship, do you instinctively interpret it as punishment for your sins? How does Baqillani's distinction between trial and punishment change how you might respond to your next difficulty? Will you ask Allah for the strength to see it as a test rather than a sign of His displeasure?
?
Think of a person you look down on because of their public failures or punishments. Does your attitude reflect a judgment that God has rejected them? After reading this lesson, will you repent of such judgments and treat them as fellow Muslims who may be undergoing a trial?
?
If worldly blessings like marriage and inheritance are not rewards, what does that mean for your tendency to envy those who have them? Can you genuinely thank Allah for your own blessings without feeling superior, and can you detach your sense of spiritual worth from your outward circumstances starting today?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner

Mu'tazilite Division on Intercession and Three Categories
Classifies Mu'tazila into two factions and three intercession categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite division on intercession and the three categories of believers for whom intercession is valid according to one faction.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila split into deniers and restrictors of intercession.

This passage from Imam al-Baqillani's Tamhid al-Awa'il presents the Mu'tazilite position on intercession. It shows that they were not monolithic: one group rejected it entirely, while another accepted it but limited it to three specific types of believers. This classification helps in understanding the sectarian debates on intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
The passage uses technical terms like 'صغائر' and 'كبائر'.
2
Identify the two factions
Find the two groups mentioned: one denies intercession altogether, the other affirms it for three categories.
The first faction is described as rejecting reports and Quran.
3
List the three categories
According to the second faction, intercession is for: those with minor sins avoiding major sins, those who repented from major sins, and those completely sinless.
Note that these are all believers.
4
Understand the limitation
The passage explicitly states that intercession is invalid for one who dies persisting in a major sin without repentance.
This is a key point of contention with other Sunni groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
وقد افترقت المعتزلة فريقين . فأنكر فريق منهم الشفاعة جملة وحمل نفسه على جحد الأخبار ورد القرآن. وقال الفريق الآخر إن للأنبياء والملائكة شفاعة، إلا أنها تشفع لثلاثة فرق من الناس المؤمنين .
ففريق من أهل الشفاعة هم أصحاب الصغائر الذين واقعوها مع مجانبة الكبائر.
والفريق الآخر أصحاب الكبائر الذين تابوا منها وندموا عليها . والفريق الآخر هم المؤمنون الذين لا ذنب لهم أصلاً. فتكون شفاعة الأنبياء والملائكة فيهم شفاعة في الزيادة لهم من النعيم على قدر منا يستحقون بأعمالهم. فأما الشفاعة في صاحب كبيرة ، إذا مات مصراً عليها، فإنها باطلة .
And the Mu'tazila have divided into two groups. One group denied intercession entirely and burdened themselves with denial of the reports and rejection of the Quran. And the other group said that the prophets and angels have intercession, but they intercede for three groups of believers. One group of those eligible for intercession are the people of minor sins who commit them while avoiding major sins. The other group are the people of major sins who repented from them and regretted them. And the other group are the believers who have no sin at all. So the intercession of the prophets and angels for them is intercession for an increase for them in bliss according to what they deserve by their deeds. As for intercession for a committer of a major sin, if he dies persisting in it, then it is invalid.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the Mu'tazilite positions on intercession. The author notes that the Mu'tazila split into two groups: one outright rejects all intercession, denying the relevant hadith and Quranic verses; the other accepts intercession but limits it to three categories of believers: those guilty only of minor sins (avoiding major sins), those who have repented from major sins, and those who are entirely sinless. For these groups, intercession serves to increase their reward in Paradise, not to forgive sins. The passage explicitly excludes intercession for anyone who dies persisting in a major sin without repentance.

Key Terms
شفاعة
معتزلة
صغائر
كبائر
توبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think all Mu'tazila denied intercession.
Correction: The passage shows one faction affirmed intercession for three limited categories.

Checkpoint
According to the second Mu'tazilite faction, for whom is intercession valid?
A) Only for those with minor sins.
B) For three groups: minor sinners, repentant major sinners, and the sinless.
C) Only for those who have no sins.
D) For all believers including persistent major sinners.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila are not uniform in rejecting intercession; one faction allows it for three specific groups of believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on the hope of intercession to feel safe about persisting in a major sin without repentance? If the Mu'tazilites insist that intercession is only for those who repent or avoid major sins, what does that say about your own attitude toward sin? Will you change today?
?
Are you among those who commit minor sins while complacent about them, assuming they will be forgiven? How does the condition of 'avoiding major sins' in this passage challenge your view of minor sins? What step will you take to guard against major sins?
?
The Mu'tazilites say intercession only increases reward for those already deserving. Do you live as if your deeds alone earn you Paradise, or do you hope for God's mercy beyond what you deserve? Which belief truly motivates you to obey God more?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner

The Mu'tazila's Inconsistency on Repentance Acceptance
Baqillani critiques Mu'tazila's interpretation of 'faghfir' and its inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the Mu'tazila's view that God is obligated to accept repentance and why their principles prevent them from adopting the Sunni interpretation.

Core Idea
Acceptance of repentance is God's favor, not an obligation.

Baqillani examines a key difference between Sunni and Mu'tazila theology: whether God must accept repentance. He argues that the Mu'tazila, by making acceptance obligatory, contradict their own principles when they try to interpret a Quranic verse. This passage highlights a fundamental doctrinal divide.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to understand Baqillani's argument.
2
Identify the two positions
Notice the Sunni view (acceptance is a favor) and the Mu'tazila view (acceptance is obligatory). Understand why Baqillani says the Sunni interpretation is inconsistent with Mu'tazila principles.
The Mu'tazila would deem God unjust if He rejected repentance.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does Baqillani conclude that the Mu'tazila cannot adopt the same interpretation? Connect the dots between their principles and the logical conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من تابوا أي تفضل عليهم بقبول توبتهم فاغفر لهم . لأن قبول التوبة تفضل الله له أن يفعله وله أن لا يفعله وهذا التأويل غير مطرد على أصول المعتزلة، لأنها توجب قبول التوبة على الله وتظلمه وتجوره في ردها وترك قبولها والعقاب على ما هي توبة منه . فلا يسوغ لهم مع ذلك مثل تأويلنا .
From those who repent, meaning: bestow favor upon them by accepting their repentance and forgive them. Because acceptance of repentance is a favor of God; He may do it and He may not do it. And this interpretation is not consistent with the principles of the Mu'tazila, because they make it obligatory for God to accept repentance and deem Him unjust and tyrannical if He rejects it and leaves it unaccepted and punishes for that from which repentance is made. So such an interpretation as ours is not permissible for them.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's interpretation of the verse 'faghfir lahum' (and forgive them). Baqillani argues that the correct understanding is that acceptance of repentance is a favor from God, not an obligation. The Mu'tazila, however, make it obligatory for God to accept repentance, and if He were to reject it, they would consider Him unjust. This contradicts their own principles. Therefore, the author concludes, the Mu'tazila cannot adopt the same interpretation as the Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
توبة
تفضل
أصول المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accepting repentance is a duty upon God.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Sunna, acceptance is a favor (tafaddul) from God, not an obligation.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the nature of God's acceptance of repentance?
A) An obligation upon God
B) A favor from God
C) A reward for good deeds
D) A punishment for sins

Key Takeaway
Acceptance of repentance is a favor from God, not an obligation, and the Mu'tazila's opposing view is inconsistent with their own principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that God owes you forgiveness after you repent? How does this lesson challenge that entitlement? What would it mean for you to receive His forgiveness as an undeserved favor rather than a right? Commit to one practical way you will shift from expectation to gratitude in your next act of repentance.
?
The Mu'tazila would accuse God of injustice if He did not accept repentance. Are there any hidden expectations you hold about how God should treat you that, if unmet, would make you resentful or doubt His goodness? Take a moment to consciously surrender that expectation to God, acknowledging that He owes you nothing and everything is a favor.
?
If acceptance of repentance is a pure favor, then every time God forgives you, He is giving you unmerited kindness. Recall a specific sin you repented from that He forgave. Let the reality of His favor sink in. How will you respond to that grace today in a tangible act of obedience or thanks?
